# Generation + Cross-Domain Coherence Audit

_Produced by a 12-analyst + synthesis multi-agent pass over the generation pipeline and the institution/service/good/supply-chain/resource/subsumption/magic mappings, config through simulation. Companion to SIMULATION_LOGIC_AUDIT.md (the simulation-side pass)._

## Mapping-matrix verdict

NOT clean — 5.5/10. Coverage is nearly exhaustive on paper (269/270 institutions resolve to some service set; all 33 resources map to chains/institutions/goods; all 52 chain resource labels resolve to real keys), and the core causal path config->resources->institutions->chains->exports/imports/income genuinely works with honest gates and receipts. But cleanliness and coherence fail at virtually every join: every mapping runs on unvalidated free-string matching, and each has at least one high-severity leak — seven chains (the whole entrepot/magic-item/planar/smuggling layer) can never activate; subsumption deletes its own greaters, required institutions, and the upstream producers its chains depend on; 'magically_sustained' reads as 'stable' to the entire sim; ~115 bespoke service mappings are shadowed by a half-rotten override table; 7 goods are dead from case drift; power<->economy feedback runs on four phantom fields (faction.category, governingName, neighborRelationship, prosperityLevel); and the needKey literals 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' sever trade and arcane chains from the causal loop. Architecture: 8/10. Data-join hygiene: 3/10. What a DM actually experiences: 5.5/10 — and recoverable to 8+ with mostly S/M-effort vocabulary repairs plus one validator test.

## Overall assessment

The architecture deserves the thesis; the data-join layer betrays it. Twelve analysts independently converged on the same verdict: the spine — resolveConfig normalization, topologically-ordered steps with per-step PRNG forks, conserved ledgers (food/defense/governance/magic/healing) with single read-points, chain-first derivation with extraction/processing gates (no iron exports without a mine, the external-mill banalite note), trace receipts at nearly every decision, and magic-as-supplement semantics (exportable=false, tradition-ranked recovery, honestly-priced teleport imports) — is genuinely well designed and exactly right for the DM audience. The config-to-simulation trace is REAL for the strongest path: config -> resources -> institution biasing -> chains -> exports/imports/income, with receipts a DM can read aloud.

But the whole value proposition is coherence, and coherence lives in the joins — and the joins are free-string substring/prefix/case-sensitive matches across at least five uncoordinated vocabularies (catalog names, service keys, chain processors, needKeys, toggle keys) with zero build-time validation. That layer has rotted to the point where the failures are the things a DM hits first: a city that rolls 'Multiple courthouses' ends with no courts (subsumption self-deletion — Brewery, Tailor's guild, Cobbler's guild, and Mint can NEVER exist); merchant guilds erase the salt chain; the entire entrepot/magic-item/planar/smuggling economy can never activate (empty processor lists); the 'magically_sustained' status — the exact receipt the owner asked about — canonicalizes to 'stable' so the sim cannot see magic holding a chain up; teleportation circles offer airship services and village elders offer druid consultations; faction-pulled institutions arrive after the economy is derived and are economically inert; the faction->institution feedback loop and noble/craftsman NPCs are dead because factions never carry a category; and 'convert SEVERITY to cloth' ships in live prose. Worse for the thesis, a stratum of the receipts themselves lies: Pipeline Rail summaries read context keys that never exist, every settlement gets a false '+6 Defensive walls in place', and what-if edits relabel emergent stress as user-chosen.

The good news is proportionality: this is data alignment and field-path repair, not redesign. Of the 20 amendments below, 9 are S-effort and 11 are M; none require new ledgers (per the owner's ruling, findings urging craft/welfare/transport/labor capacity fixes were explicitly deprioritized as noise — the classifier amendment is scoped to healing/civic/arcane only). The single highest-leverage item is the missing CI join-validator: virtually every finding in all twelve reports would have been caught by one test asserting that every rule endpoint, processor string, override target, needKey literal, and requiredInstitution resolves against its source-of-truth table. Land that first, then fix what it lights up.

## Cross-cutting themes

### Free-string name joins with no validation guard (the root disease)
_config-pipeline, institutions-generation, services-coherence, goods-economy, supply-chains, subsumption, economy-power-institutions, magic-supplement, resources-terrain, cross-mapping-matrix, gen-to-sim-trace, validation-narrative_

Five vocabularies (catalog institution names, service keys, chain processors/ids, needKeys, toggle keys) are joined by exact/substring/12-char-prefix/case-sensitive matching with zero build-time verification, and every analyst independently hit the consequences: catalog 'baseChance' vs readers of 'def.p'/'h.p'/'h.on' kills the entire cascade pass, faction signature-institution selection, and getHistoryModifiers; case drift kills 7 goods ("Hunter's Lodge" vs "Hunter's lodge"); apostrophes kill rules ('mages district', 'Wizard Tower' vs "Wizard's tower"); needKey literals 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' match nothing, so trade-chain health never moves trade_connectivity and the smuggling escalation clock can never fire; 'magically_sustained'/'unexploited' are unknown to the canonical status fold; stale magicLevel bands ('pervasive'/'common'/'moderate') linger in two consumers; categoryToggles has three keying schemes and goodsToggles two value shapes, inverting user intent on the bulk path. One CI join test would have caught essentially all of it.

### Subsumption consolidates by destroying — including itself
_subsumption, institutions-generation, supply-chains, gen-to-sim-trace, cross-mapping-matrix_

Substring matching with no self-exclusion means five rules delete their own greater (Multiple courthouses, Brewery, Cobbler's guild, Tailor's guild, Mint (official) — empirically verified as never able to exist); no protection for required/forced/custom means a cathedral deletes a city's REQUIRED parish-church network and user-authored canon is spliceable; producer-eaten-by-consumer rules sever the very chains the engine then reports as broken (merchant guilds erase Salt works — the salt chain's only processor; smelter eats its own charcoal burner and mine; butchers eat shepherds and dairy farmers); and nothing transfers the absorbed institution's services, export gates, or chain roles, so upgrading to Tanner (established) kills leather exports and the academy upgrade kills the spellcasting chain. Three parallel dedup systems use different matchers and protection policies, and the cascade pass that should ADD chain-adjacent institutions is 100% dead code (reads data.p from a baseChance catalog), with the airship maritime override trapped inside its dead guard.

### Authored archetypes that can never exist (dead strata)
_supply-chains, services-coherence, goods-economy, resources-terrain, cross-mapping-matrix, validation-narrative_

Whole categories of authored content are unreachable: seven chains declare empty processingInstitutions, so the entire entrepot-luxury (spices, silk, transit finance), magic-item, planar, and smuggling economy never activates in any settlement; RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS references nine nonexistent need keys ('agricultural.*', 'services.hospital'), half-inerting the desert/mountain biome content; 'Major port', 'University', 'Navy (if coastal)', and 'Specialist craftsmen quarters' are gated on by five-plus consumers (Port Duties income, export gates, dependencies, subsumption, spatial) but exist in no catalog; ~115 bespoke institution-service entries are shadowed by override redirects; the goods-toggle UI renders SERVICE_TIER_DATA while the engine rolls GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER; a Stage-3 export enrichment block (slave trade, military services, toggle pushes) is computed then wiped by the chain override; a legacy third chain model (RESOURCE_CHAINS) feeds the dossier's resource analysis from generic terrain words instead of rolled resources; and the religion/law/healing chains are 'processed' by almshouses and bathhouses while the catalog's actual churches, courthouses, and hospitals back nothing.

### Magic: right semantics, signal erased at every boundary
_magic-supplement, supply-chains, goods-economy, institutions-generation, config-pipeline_

The supplement design is correct and well-priced — exportable=false on sustained chains, druid>divine>arcane recovery ranking, teleport imports 'real but expensive', three-tier magic income ladder — but the signal dies at the seams. The same food offset is implemented four times (foodGenerator, economicGenerator's viability copy, chainMagicSubstitution, defenseGenerator) with divergent gates and matchers, so the food ledger, viability tab, and chain display can disagree about one settlement. The divine tradition bypasses every magicExists gate (dead-magic worlds still get 'Temple granaries blessed'), and isolated towns get forced teleportation circles in no-magic and priorityMagic=1 worlds, contradicting the 66+ gate. Downstream, 'magically_sustained' canonicalizes to 'stable' (the purpose-built 'substituted' status is unreachable), the second upstream pass overwrites the status it just granted, magicRecovery magnitude is display-only, and foodSecurity.magicSupplement is cosmetic while the applied offset has no receipt. Magic also only rescues failing chains — never boosts healthy ones — and the two flagship arcane chains (magical_goods, planar) can never activate. Nine-plus undocumented thresholds straddle the band edges.

### Pipeline order and config echo break the config-to-sim trace
_config-pipeline, economy-power-institutions, gen-to-sim-trace_

Step order contradicts data flow at three points: factionCorrelationPass pushes institutions AFTER economy/services/spatial/subsumption, so faction-pulled institutions are dossier-visible but provide no services, join no chains, get no placement, bypass subsumption, and the dossier's narrative half and economy half describe different institution sets; resolveStress runs before institutions exist, so every institution stress modifier (walls suppress siege, granaries suppress famine, healers suppress plague) is dead and the trace papers over it; and the assembly-time legitimacy patch updates the score/label but not the faction powers and relationships computed from the stale band. Worse, derived state (emergent stressTypes, military floor, _magicTradeOnly, overwritten priorityMagic) is baked into settlement.config and echoed back as forced input on every what-if edit — emergent stress becomes 'selected by user config', and same-seed regens erase sim-acquired state.

### Power-economy connective tissue severed by phantom fields
_economy-power-institutions, institutions-generation, validation-narrative_

The closed-loop power<->economy design is authored on both ends but four field names never exist in between: generated factions carry no .category, so deriveFactionBoosts always returns [] (the entire 'dominant thieves' guild pulls criminal institutions' feature is dead) and noble/master-craftsman NPCs can never spawn (generatePopulation also never passes powerStructure); powerStructure.governingName is never set, so the governing faction never inherits public legitimacy in profiles or traces; config.neighborRelationship never exists, so hostile-neighbour military/economy multipliers are permanently 1.0 (and generatePowerStructure's tradeRoute is hardwired null, killing the external-threat stability branches); neighbour prosperity is read via nonexistent 'prosperityLevel', so economicStrength is always 0.5. Add vocabulary holes — 'Thriving' checked but never produced, 'Lightly Defended' produced but missing from both DEFENSE_CONTRIB maps (non-monotonic legitimacy), nobles orphaned from both correlation loops, five stress-archetype flags computed and consumed nowhere — and the Power tab's relationship to the economy is mostly cosmetic.

### Depletion and resource state: three stores and one-way doors
_resources-terrain, supply-chains, config-pipeline_

Resource depletion lives in three uncoordinated stores (config.nearbyResourcesDepleted from generation, key-form nearbyResourcesState from world-pulse, label-form nearbyResourcesState from the DEPLETE_RESOURCE event), and each consumer reads a different one — deriveSystemState misses generation depletion, world-pulse misses event depletion, and food security and stress ignore depletion entirely while exports honor it strictly, so the dossier can say 'fishing grounds exhausted' and 'surplus from fishing' simultaneously. RECOVERED_RESOURCE moves abstract dials but has no mutation, making event depletion a one-way door; same-seed regeneration erases sim-acquired depletion. Manual resource mode is independently broken: any abundant/depleted mark silently drops every plain selection, and the terrain-specific resources the UI offered are filtered out by a missing terrain argument. Positional resources (crossroads, mountain pass) can 'deplete', and the city-tier bypass of the pressure gate produces runaway auto-depletion — the same class of runaway the corruption system got a soak-test guard for.

### Receipts that lie (the thesis-level risk)
_validation-narrative, config-pipeline, services-coherence, gen-to-sim-trace, economy-power-institutions_

For a product sold on honest receipts, a stratum of the receipts is fiction: Pipeline Rail step summaries read context keys that never exist (subsumption always shows 'Nothing collapsed'; 'No active stressors' in a plague town); subsumption traces name absorbers that deleted themselves; explicit-config route rewrites and military floors apply silently while the random-path trace claims floors that did not happen; causalState credits '+6 Defensive walls in place' to EVERY settlement via a JSON.stringify property-name match; aiLayer reads phantom fields (conflicts at the wrong location, plotHooks/incomeSources never resolving, the stability label string compared as a number so every settlement reads as contested) and prints '300% food surplus' for absolute units; the arrival-scene tables are cross-wired (route-keyed templates indexed by a field that never exists), 5 of 15 stress types have no arrival vignette and never promote to conditions (wartime, insurgency, mass_migration); the fuzzy service fallback hands thorp household elders druidic consultation; and a find-replace accident left 'SEVERITY' where 'it' belongs in ~9 live DM-facing strings.

## Prioritized amendments

1. **[high/M] Add a CI cross-vocabulary join validator (the meta-fix)**  
   `cross-mapping-matrix — new test (e.g. tests/mappingJoins.test.js) validating src/data/supplyChainData.js, src/data/servicesData.js, src/data/tradeGoodsData.js, src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js, src/generators/steps/stepMetadata.js against src/data/institutionalCatalog.js and SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS`  
   Virtually every finding in all twelve reports is a free-string join that fails silently. One test asserting that every SUBSUMPTION_RULES endpoint, chain processingInstitution, RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS id, LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES target, requiredInstitution name, needKey literal, and STEP_METADATA key resolves against its source-of-truth table would have caught nearly all of them and prevents regression while the data fixes land. Land this FIRST and fix what it lights up.

2. **[high/M] Fix subsumption: self-match exclusion, exact-name matching, required/forced/custom protection, delete producer-eating rules**  
   `subsumption — src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:42-117 (rules 25,28,37-43,49,61-68; matcher at 84-92)`  
   Empirically verified: Multiple courthouses, Brewery, Cobbler's guild, Tailor's guild, and Mint (official) delete themselves and can never exist; a cathedral deletes required parish churches; merchant guilds erase the salt chain's only processor; smelters eat their own fuel suppliers. This is the single most destructive pass in the pipeline and directly contradicts the supply-chain layer.

3. **[high/S] Re-key needKey literals 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' to real keys**  
   `supply-chains — src/domain/causalState.js:360; src/domain/hookEscalation.js:430; src/domain/supplyChainState.js:107-155; src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:240-263`  
   Trade-chain health never feeds trade_connectivity, the smuggling_rise escalation clock can never fire, and entrepot/arcane chains get generic beneficiaries/victims and generic downstream traces — the chains->causal.scores loop is severed for the entire trade domain by a one-word vocabulary mismatch.

4. **[high/S] Map 'magically_sustained' -> 'substituted' (and 'unexploited' -> 'strained'); set substituteActive; exempt from the second upstream pass**  
   `magic-supplement — src/domain/supplyChainState.js:57-79,294-297; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:320-334`  
   The exact receipt the owner asked about — magic holding a supply chain up — currently reads as a perfectly 'stable' chain to capacityModel, causalState, the dossier, and the AI overlay, and the upstream-propagation pass can overwrite the status it just granted. Three one-line changes restore the entire magic-as-supplement signal at the gen-to-sim boundary.

5. **[high/S] Give the seven empty-processor chains real processors**  
   `supply-chains — src/data/supplyChainData.js:534,651,667,684,1052,1074,1213 (vs gate at src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117)`  
   The entire entrepot-luxury, magic-item, planar, and smuggling economy is dead data: spices_dyes, silk_luxury_textiles, transit_finance, luxury_goods, magical_goods, planar, and smuggling can never activate because computeActiveChains requires >=1 matched processor. A port metropolis gets no silk, spice, banking, magic-item, or smuggling chain — and 'magic as a trade booster' exists only in income labels.

6. **[high/S] Fix the nine dead RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS need keys and index the terrain chains**  
   `resources-terrain — src/data/supplyChainData.js:1529-1568`  
   date_palms, desert_salt, camel_herds, alpine_pasture, hot_springs_mineral, foraging_areas, and ancient_grove point at need keys that don't exist ('agricultural.*', 'services.hospital'), and every dedicated desert/mountain chain is absent from the index — the entire newer biome content half-works: chains show 'operational' instead of 'running' and their outputs never reach localProduction.

7. **[high/M] Assign faction.category at creation and pass the full settlement into generateNPCs**  
   `economy-power-institutions — src/generators/powerGenerator.js:943,990,1049 (faction creation); src/generators/steps/generatePopulation.js:33; src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:65-66,129-170 (also fix def.p -> baseChance and the toggle-key check while there)`  
   Factions never carry a category, so the entire faction->institution feedback pass (Item 16) is dead code, demand profiling degrades to name-matching, and Lord/Baron/Knight/Master Blacksmith NPCs can NEVER generate (the gate also never receives powerStructure at all). One field assignment plus one parameter revives three authored systems.

8. **[high/S] Use resolved tier, not raw settType, in the three institutionProbability gates**  
   `config-pipeline — src/generators/institutionProbability.js:79,210-211,252-253,264 (resolveConfig already writes effectiveConfig.tier)`  
   settType:'random' is the DEFAULT, and for it the tier-magic penalty misses its table (wizard towers in thorps at ~5x intended rate), neighbour tierDiff computes from indexOf(-1) (patron suppression fires for any neighbour), and goods-toggle institution penalties are a complete no-op. Most generations run with these gates broken.

9. **[high/M] Move factionCorrelationPass (and stripArcaneInstitutions) before generateEconomy, or re-derive services/chains and re-subsume after additions**  
   `config-pipeline — src/generators/steps/index.js:16-21; src/generators/steps/factionCorrelationPass.js:24-98`  
   Faction-pulled institutions currently exist in the dossier with no services, no chain participation, no spatial placement, and no subsumption check, and the arcane safety-strip runs after the economy was derived from institutions it then deletes — the dossier's narrative half and economy half describe two different settlements.

10. **[high/M] Persist raw user config separately from effectiveConfig**  
   `config-pipeline — src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:84; src/store/settlementSlice.js:737-743; src/generators/steps/resolveStress.js:27-35`  
   Derived state (emergent stressTypes, military floor, _magicTradeOnly, overwritten priorityMagic, normalized threat) is echoed back as input on every what-if edit: emergent stress becomes forced and its trace falsely claims 'selected by user config', floors persist past their causes, and magicExists=false bakes priorityMagic=0 forever. This silently breaks the product's core 'config -> sim traces coherently' promise on the second edit.

11. **[high/M] Audit LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES: let exact-name win, fix/delete 55 dead targets, add ~6 government overrides, require a minimum fuzzy score**  
   `services-coherence — src/data/servicesData.js:8-240; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:806-855 (also unify the exact/fuzzy toggle-resolution paths at 813-882)`  
   ~115 bespoke service entries are shadowed (Teleportation circle gets Airship services, carpenters offer horseshoeing, bakers offer sawmilling), 55 targets point at keys that don't exist, and the fuzzy fallback hands thorp household elders druid services and town councils town-crier services. These are receipts a DM reads verbatim — the most visible mapping failure in the product.

12. **[high/S] Fix healing/civic/arcane classifiers to key on category/tags instead of name regexes**  
   `gen-to-sim-trace — src/domain/healingLedger.js:23; src/domain/capacityModel.js:322; src/domain/magicLedger.js:26 (also retire the stale 'pervasive' read at capacityModel.js:221-224)`  
   healingLedger doesn't recognize 'hospital' (a city's Major hospital reads healerCount=0 and gets 'No dedicated healing institutions' receipts); CIVIC_PATTERN misses 'City administration'/'Royal seat' while counting gambling halls; the canonical ARCANE pattern misses "Mages' guild"/"Mages' district"/'Academy of magic'. Scoped per the owner ruling: REL_PATTERN/CRAFT_PATTERN (welfare/craft) fixes are deliberately deprioritized as noise.

13. **[high/M] One shared magic-tradition detector and one offset table; gate divine on magicExists**  
   `magic-supplement — src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:49,70-75; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:39-67; src/generators/foodGenerator.js:96-167; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:417-447 (model: src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:97-124)`  
   Four parallel implementations (foodGenerator, economicGenerator viability copy, chainMagicSubstitution, defenseGenerator) use divergent matchers and gates, so food ledger, viability, chains, and defense disagree about the same settlement — and the divine branch leaks full magic substitution into magicExists=false worlds, breaking the flagship dead-magic guarantee. defenseGenerator's gating is the model to extract.

14. **[high/M] Unify depletion state: key-form event writes, RECOVERED_RESOURCE mutation, manual-mode membership and terrain fixes, one shared accessor**  
   `resources-terrain — src/domain/events/mutate.js:314-325 (+missing RECOVERED_RESOURCE case at 51-124); src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:39-113; src/domain/state/deriveSystemState.js:243-263; src/generators/foodGenerator.js:34-76`  
   DEPLETE_RESOURCE writes label-keyed state nothing reads, recovery has no mutation (one-way door), same-seed regens erase sim depletion, manual mode silently drops every plain selection once any resource is marked and filters out the terrain resources the UI offered, and food/stress ignore depletion entirely — the cross-domain consequence a DM most expects.

15. **[medium/S] Revive the cascade pass: read baseChance, spread the catalog def into additions, hoist the airship override out of the dead guard**  
   `subsumption — src/generators/cascadeGenerator.js:110-118; src/generators/steps/cascadePass.js:31-88`  
   The owner's named 'cascade logic' (smelter pulls charcoal burner) is 100% dead because it reads data.p from a baseChance catalog — and the airship maritime override plus post-cascade re-subsumption are trapped inside its never-true guard. Same one-field schema fix also repairs faction-boost rarity sorting.

16. **[medium/S] Case-insensitive requiredInstitution matching in getGoodsModifiers**  
   `goods-economy — src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1158-1164; src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:477-687`  
   Seven goods (Game meat, Charcoal, Peat fuel, Fresh fish, Fresh milk and dairy, Quality boots and shoes, Finished garments) are permanently dead because "Hunter's Lodge" never equals "Hunter's lodge". One-line lowercase fix; pair with the validator test asserting every requiredInstitution resolves.

17. **[medium/S] Delete or relocate the Stage-3 export enrichment the chain override wipes**  
   `goods-economy — src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2017-2113 (built) vs 2219-2246 (wiped)`  
   Slave-trade, military-services, siege-annotation, and goods-toggle export logic is computed (consuming RNG) then discarded by re.length=0 — dead code that looks load-bearing and already misled one refactor. Port the military/slave logic after the chain override or into deriveExportsFromChains; delete the rest.

18. **[medium/M] Two-phase stress: re-weight/confirm stress after institutions exist**  
   `config-pipeline — src/generators/steps/resolveStress.js:21; src/generators/stressGenerator.js:59-165 (add a stressConfirmPass before generateEconomy)`  
   resolveStress runs against an empty institution list, so every institution stress modifier (walls x0.6 siege, granary x0.5 famine, healer x0.6 plague, bank x1.4 debt) is inert at generation — the code-implied promise 'walled towns get besieged less' is pure tier+slider odds, and the trace papers over it.

19. **[medium/S] Restore 'it' at every SEVERITY corruption site and lint for ALL-CAPS tokens in user-facing strings**  
   `validation-narrative — src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1919; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:343,345,388,408,1989,2019,2199; src/data/spatialData.js:49`  
   'weavers and fullers convert SEVERITY to cloth' and ~8 sibling strings ship verbatim in the dossier — machine damage in the exact honesty layer the product sells. Trivial fix, outsized credibility cost while it remains.

20. **[medium/M] Fix narrative-layer phantom reads: conflicts location, stability-as-string, plotHooks/incomeSources paths, arrival-table wiring**  
   `validation-narrative — src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:73; src/generators/aiLayer.js:55-60,80,99,119,137,279; src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:1074-1092; supabase/functions/generate-narrative/index.ts:1105-1117`  
   Faction conflicts are generated but every narrative/AI consumer reads powerStructure.conflicts where they never live; aiLayer compares the stability label string to numbers so every settlement reads as contested; plot hooks and income sources never reach the AI grounding; and the arrival tables are cross-wired so most settlements open with the bare fallback. All one-line field-path fixes that reconnect the engine's richest outputs to the prose a DM reads first.

## Orphans and mismatches (the snapped joins)

1. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): 'Major port' — gates Port Duties income (economicGenerator.js:1646), TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS, subsumption rule 29, spatial entries, and port service patterns, but no catalog or generator ever creates it; port cities top out at 'Docks/port facilities' and never earn their flagship customs income.

2. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): 'University', 'Navy (if coastal)', 'Specialist craftsmen quarters', 'Grove Shrine', 'Mining settlement', 'Monster Part Dealers', 'Spellcasting Services', 'Magic Item' — full service blocks, export gates, subsumption rules, and validator prereqs exist for institutions absent from every tier catalog.

3. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): 'mason'/'stonemason' gate keywords and instBoosts (computeActiveChains.js:361-434, resourceData.js:111,232) match no catalog institution — 'Building materials' is permanently unexportable and the stone/clay institution boosts bias nothing.

4. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): 13 phantom chain processors ('Barracks (town)', 'City wall district', 'Town fortifications', 'Wizard Tower', 'Horse market', 'Armourers', "Dyers' workshop", 'Leatherworkers', etc.) — the fortification chain effectively requires a Citadel because 'Town walls'/'City walls and gates' match nothing.

5. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): 10 of 69 TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS keys name institutions that don't exist; canonical chain statuses 'substituted'/'blocked'/'captured' are priced by capacityModel/causalState/deriveRegionalState but have ZERO producers; UI checks status 'broken' that nothing emits.

6. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): read-but-never-written fields — powerStructure.governingName, config.neighborRelationship, econ.prosperityLevel, settlement.supplyChainState.failures, powerStructure.conflicts, economicState.tradeCommodity, def.p / h.on / h.p, instFlags._govFacName, `_export_`/`_import_` toggle namespaces, config.mustImport.

7. ORPHAN (consumer, no producer): NEED_HEURISTICS and trace-switch keys 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' (real keys: trade_entrepot, arcane_magical; no energy category exists); 'cathedral'/'prelate' Government names for the theocracy boost; 'Thriving' prosperity; UPGRADE_GOODS_BY_TIER city/metropolis branches (route-vs-tier confusion).

8. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): seven chains with empty processingInstitutions (spices_dyes, silk_luxury_textiles, transit_finance, luxury_goods, magical_goods, planar, smuggling) — authored, fed by RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS, never activatable; the entire entrepot/magic-item/planar/smuggling economy is dead data.

9. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): statuses 'magically_sustained' and 'unexploited' canonicalize to 'stable' — magic-degraded chains read as healthy in food scores and the magic story is erased from every canonical consumer.

10. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): foodSecurity.magicSupplement is persisted but read by no deriver, while the actually-applied magicOffset is never returned (no receipt); magicRecovery magnitude feeds only an EconomicsTab badge — 25% and 70% recovery are mechanically identical.

11. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): five stress-flag outputs (secularBrutalism, magicMilitarized, mageTheocracy, stateCrimeIntensity, heresyIntensity) computed and consumed nowhere; chain.services tags produced on every chain but consumed only as free-text search — and in a vocabulary ('crafts','trade','military','textiles','security','construction','fuel') outside the canonical 11 service buckets.

12. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): dead config/data strata — _INCOME_TO_CHAINS, _isolationInfraType, _isolationFoodStress, ITEM_CATEGORIES, SPECIAL_RESOURCES featureEffects (always fed []), five Phase-D config fields (customInstitutions/customResources/customTradeRoutes/powerDynamicsConfig/defenseScenarioConfig), SERVICE_TIER_DATA + getHistoryModifiers + _computeIncomeStreams, _getUpgradeOpps, ~450 lines of dead servicesGenerator helpers holding the lost magic-import narrative copy, the never-called _resolveUpgrades auto-fix layer, and aiLayer's built-then-discarded 85-line prompt.

13. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): 'Communal root cellar' and "Woodcutter's camp" generate but resolve to zero services (the woodcutter is actively resource-boosted yet a dead end); the 'Abundant' resource state has no downstream effect anywhere; RECOVERED_RESOURCE moves dimension dials but mutates no resource state.

14. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): faction-pulled institutions (factionCorrelationPass, step 12) and their demand imports arrive after economy/services/spatial/subsumption — dossier-visible but economically inert, tagless, and able to violate subsumption; the Stage-3 heuristic export enrichment (slave trade, military services, toggles, stress labels) is computed then wiped by the chain override.

15. ORPHAN (producer, no consumer): ~115 bespoke INSTITUTION_SERVICES entries shadowed by override redirects (including the Teleportation circle's own entry — THE magic-trade institution) and ~120 service keys unreachable through any path; 79 SERVICE_CATEGORY_MAP entries name services no institution offers.

16. MISMATCH (schema): catalog 'baseChance'/'defaultEnabled' vs readers of 'def.p'/'h.p'/'h.on' — kills the entire cascade pass, flattens faction signature-institution rarity to 0.5, and makes getHistoryModifiers always return [].

17. MISMATCH (case/spelling): "Hunter's Lodge"/"Charcoal Burner"/"Peat Cutter"/"Fisher's Landing"/"Dairy Farmer"/"Cobbler's Guild"/"Tailor's Guild" vs sentence-case catalog names — seven goods permanently dead; 'mages district' vs "Mages' district", 'Wizard Tower' vs "Wizard's tower", 'pit fights' vs 'Fighting pits' — dead subsumption rules and a wizard tower that can't run its own alchemy chain; 'clay_pits' vs 'river_clay'; 'desert_salt' missing from every salt check; misspelled 'requiresInstitution' twin field.

18. MISMATCH (key vocabulary): toggle store writes `${tier}::${category}::${name}` objects and `${tier}_good_${name}`; consumers check bare names === false/'exclude' and read `_export_`/`_import_` keys nothing writes — user force/exclude intent is invisible or INVERTED (bulk-exclude objects are truthy and enable goods); categoryToggles has three keying schemes and the engine's lookup can never match what the UI writes.

19. MISMATCH (category vocabulary): NPC categories 'crafts'/'magic'/'noble' vs archetype keys 'craft'/'arcane' (guildmasters and mages get 'other' templates); faction category 'economy' vs NPC checks for 'crafts'; priorityCategory systematically mis-assigned (34 Crafts entries tagged 'government', metropolis Criminal tier tagged 'entertainment' — historyGenerator reports thieves'-guild metropolises as crime-free); HISTORY_EVENTS 'religious' never equals priorityCategory 'religion'.

20. MISMATCH (status/label vocabulary): 'Lightly Defended' produced by defenseGenerator but missing from both DEFENSE_CONTRIB maps (scores better than 'Vulnerable'); safetyContrib misses 'Controlled/Quarantined/Critical' compound labels (worst slave-revolt state contributes MORE legitimacy than the mildest); powerStructure.stability is a label string consumed as a 0-100 number by aiLayer; stale magicLevel bands 'pervasive'/'common'/'moderate' in resourceTaxonomy and capacityModel.deriveHealing; magicProfile defaults missing magicLevel to 'low' while magicLedger defaults to 'medium'.

21. MISMATCH (stress vocabulary): conditionPromotion regexes miss 'wartime'/'insurgency'/'mass_migration' (their archetypes exist); STRESS_DESCS/STRESS_NOTES cover 10 of 15 stress types; STRESS_FLAVOR omits the five newer stressors; housing-pressure regex misses 'migration'.

22. MISMATCH (cross-wiring): ARRIVAL_SCENES is ambience-keyed but indexed by route, ARRIVAL_ADDONS is route-keyed but indexed by the never-set tradeCommodity — both halves of the dossier's opening prose are dead and most settlements open with the bare fallback.

23. MISMATCH (units/semantics): food surplus is absolute units printed as a percentage ('300% food surplus' in AI prompt and daily-life prose while the PDF says units); 'days of reserves' is a production ratio scaled to 30, not a stock; the economy-output income multiplier cancels itself in normalization; substituteActive means MUNDANE substitution but is reported as 'magical substitute in use' while genuine magic substitution never sets it.

24. MISMATCH (boundary tables): popToTier (<=80 thorp) vs POPULATION_RANGES (61+ hamlet) vs UI labels — in the 61-80 band the user's institution toggles are keyed to a tier the generator never resolves; noMagic treats omitted priorityMagic as 0 while priorityMagicEffective defaults it to 50 (resolveConfig.js:48-49 vs 68), and servicesGenerator's `(priorityMagic || 50) === 0` no-magic gate is unsatisfiable dead code.

25. MISMATCH (duplicate identities): two chains share id 'shipbuilding' (last-wins in every map); near-duplicate 'fish'/'fishing' chains double-credit +8/+8 food security and let landlocked salt towns 'run' a fishing chain; two contradictory upstream-dependency graphs (CHAIN_DEPS vs catalog upstreamChains) fight across three propagation passes.

## What is missing

1. A build-time/CI join validator — the single missing guard. There is no test that rule endpoints, chain processors, override targets, requiredInstitution names, needKey literals, RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS ids, or STEP_METADATA keys resolve against their source tables; every high-severity finding in this review is a silent join failure that one such test would have caught.

2. Magic as a BOOSTER, not just a rescuer: the substitution pass only fires on impaired/depleted chains — a high-magic druid settlement gets zero chain-level benefit while healthy, magicRecovery magnitude feeds no mechanical consumer, and the two chains that would make magic a trade engine (magical_goods, planar) can never activate. The owner's 'supplement AND booster' framing is currently half-implemented.

3. A producer for the 'captured' chain status: the corruption/faction-capture layer never marks a chain captured despite three consumers pricing it — faction capture of supply chains is authored vocabulary with no mechanism.

4. Chains->power feedback: dominant chains never seat or strengthen factions, so 'who controls the grain?' is answered by a string-picked inferController, not the faction system; generated services likewise feed nothing (display-only). Cheap wiring of existing structures, not new ledgers.

5. A RECOVERED_RESOURCE mutation and any depletion->food/stress consequence: depletion is currently a one-way door that exports respect but food security and stress probability ignore entirely.

6. The institutions the data layer already wired for: University, Major port, Navy (coastal), Specialist craftsmen quarters, a theocratic Government entry (Cathedral chapter/Prelate's seat), Stonemason, and a noble demand/correlation mapping — each has services, gates, subsumption rules, or dependency entries waiting and nothing to attach to.

7. Arrival vignettes, founding notes, and condition promotion for 5 of 15 stress types (wartime, insurgency, mass_migration, religious_conversion, slave_revolt) — a slave-revolt settlement gets a crisis dossier with a serene arrival paragraph and an empty activeConditions array.

8. A canonical instId join key decoupling display names from joins: nearly every bug in this review descends from joining on punctuated, pluralized, parenthesized display strings with four different matchers (exact, substring, slice(0,12), slice(0,16)).

9. Named threshold constants for the magic gate zoo (nine-plus undocumented values straddling the documented band edges, 65 vs 66) and a single shared magic-tradition detector — currently four divergent implementations.

10. Per-culture institution aliasing: every culture choice (mesoamerican, steppe, east_asian) still requires a 'Parish church' and 'Priest (resident)' — cheap display-time aliasing would close the most visible audience-fit gap. (Deliberately excluded per owner ruling: craft/welfare/transport/labor capacity ledgers and the REL_PATTERN/CRAFT_PATTERN regex repairs that serve them.)

---

## Full findings by subsystem

### config-pipeline

The config pipeline has a genuinely good spine: one normalization step (resolveConfig) producing effectiveConfig, topologically-ordered steps with declared deps, per-step PRNG forks, and trace receipts at most decision points. But coherence frays at four seams: (1) several downstream gates consult raw config.settType where the resolved tier is needed, silently disabling magic-tier penalties, goods-toggle suppression, and neighbour tier logic for the DEFAULT 'random' mode; (2) step ORDER contradicts data flow — stress is rolled before institutions exist (institution modifiers dead), and faction-pulled institutions + demand imports are added after economy/services/spatial were already computed; (3) derived state is baked into settlement.config and echoed back as input on every what-if edit (emergent stress becomes forced, military floor and _magicTradeOnly persist past their causes); (4) a cluster of receipts lie — Pipeline Rail step summaries read context keys that never exist, and the route/military-floor overrides on explicit (non-random) config paths are applied silently with no trace.

- **[high] settType used where resolved tier is needed — three gates silently wrong for 'random'/'custom'** (doesnt_make_sense) — `src/generators/institutionProbability.js:79,210-211,252-253,264; src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:125-140`  
  effectiveConfig keeps settType='random'|'custom' while also carrying the resolved tier, but getBaseChance consults settType FIRST. (a) institutionProbability.js:79 tierMagicPenalty['random'] misses the table and falls back to 0.75 (town), so a random-rolled thorp gets ~5x the intended arcane-institution likelihood — wizard towers in thorps; (b) lines 210-211 and 252-253 compute tierDiff from TIER_ORDER.indexOf('random') = -1, so the patron-government suppression (×0.4) fires for ANY neighbour ≥ village regardless of real tier, and 'custom' is hardcoded to 'village' ignoring population; (c) line 264 keys getPriorityModifiers by settType, so GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER['random'] = {} and goods-toggle institution penalties are a complete no-op in the default random mode. Since settType:'random' is DEFAULT_CONFIG's default, most generations run with these gates broken.  
  _Fix:_ Use (config.tier || mapped settType) in all three lookups; resolveConfig already writes effectiveConfig.tier, so flip the fallback order to config.tier first. Add a unit test that a settType:'random' seed resolving to thorp rejects high-magic institutions and honors a goods exclusion.
- **[high] factionCorrelationPass mutates institutions and imports AFTER economy/services/spatial were derived** (doesnt_make_sense) — `src/generators/steps/factionCorrelationPass.js:24-98; src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:28-31; src/generators/steps/index.js:16-21`  
  Step order is generateEconomy (9) → generatePower (10) → factionCorrelationPass (12), but factionCorrelationPass pushes faction-pulled institutions into ctx.institutions and appends demand imports directly onto economicState.primaryImports. Consequences: a faction-pulled institution exists in the dossier but provides NO services (availableServices built at step 9), no supply-chain participation (activeChains fixed), no spatial placement, and no subsumption check (a faction could pull 'Wizard's tower' alongside an existing 'Mages' guild' that subsumes it). The arcane safety-strip also runs here — after economy — so services/chains computed from later-stripped institutions survive. Meanwhile generateNarratives/generatePopulation (13-14) see the post-mutation list, so the dossier's NPC/narrative half and its economy half describe two different institution sets.  
  _Fix:_ Either move the faction-institution feedback loop before generateEconomy (factions can be derived from institutions pre-economy), or re-run service/chain derivation for additions, and re-apply subsumption after the push. At minimum run stripArcaneInstitutions before generateEconomy.
- **[high] Derived state echoes back into config on every what-if edit (settlement.config = effectiveConfig)** (incoherence) — `src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:84; src/store/settlementSlice.js:737-743; src/generators/steps/resolveStress.js:27-35; src/generators/stressGenerator.js:205-217`  
  assembleSettlement persists effectiveConfig — including DERIVED fields: stressTypes/stressType written by resolveStress, normalized monsterThreat, resolved tradeRouteAccess, priorityMagic overwritten with priorityMagicEffective, priorityMilitary possibly floored to 25, _magicTradeOnly, _neighbourEconBias, _population, resolved nearbyResources — as settlement.config. applyChange rebuilds the next run's raw config from it. Effects: (a) emergent stress becomes Mode-0 FORCED stress (stressGenerator.js:205-211) on every subsequent edit, and resolveStress then labels it 'applied / selected by user config' in traces — the receipt is now false; (b) a militaryFloor applied under 'plagued' persists after the user lowers threat, losing their original slider value; (c) magicExists=false bakes priorityMagic=0 forever; (d) stale _magicTradeOnly survives route edits (hasTeleportationInfra trusts it, priorityHelpers.js:175). Derived-state-as-input quietly breaks 'config → sim traces coherently'.  
  _Fix:_ Persist raw user config and effectiveConfig separately (settlement.config vs settlement.effectiveConfig), and have applyChange regenerate from the raw one; or strip derived keys (stressTypes, _magicTradeOnly, floored priorities, normalized threat) before re-feeding.
- **[high] Stress resolves before institutions exist — all institution-presence stress modifiers are dead** (doesnt_make_sense) — `src/generators/steps/resolveStress.js:21; src/generators/stressGenerator.js:59-165`  
  resolveStress (step 3) calls generateStress({ name:'', tier, institutions: [] }, effectiveConfig) — institutions are assembled at step 5. buildStressContext computes hasWalls/hasMilitary/hasGranary/hasMarket/hasChurch/hasHealer/hasGuild/hasBank from that empty list, so every institution modifier is inert at generation: walls never suppress siege (×0.6), granaries never suppress famine (×0.5), banks never raise debt odds (×1.4), healers never suppress plague (×0.6). Only threat/route/priorities/resources actually modulate stress. A DM reading the code-implied promise ('walled towns get besieged less') gets pure tier+slider odds instead. The resolveStress trace even attributes emergent stress to 'tier/threat/economy heuristics', papering over the missing half of the model.  
  _Fix:_ Split stress into two phases: roll candidate stress early for config threading, then re-weight/confirm after assembleInstitutions (a 'stressConfirmPass' before generateEconomy), or move resolveStress after the institution phase and thread only intended stress types early.
- **[medium] Silent overrides with no receipt: explicit isolated→road rewrite and military floor** (incoherence) — `src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:101,123,184-200,202-217`  
  Three receipt gaps in resolveConfig: (a) the isolated→road rewrite (line 101) applies to an EXPLICIT user choice of 'isolated' too, but the trade-route trace is only emitted when routePool exists (random path, line 184) — a user who picked Isolated for a no-magic city gets 'road' in the dossier with zero explanation; (b) the priorityMilitary floor (line 123) applies whenever threat is plagued, but is only mentioned in a trace when monsterThreat was 'random_threat' (line 202) — explicit plagued + military 10 silently becomes 25; (c) that random-threat trace claims 'priorityMilitary floored to 25' unconditionally for any plagued roll (line 214), even when the user's slider was ≥25 and no floor applied — the receipt asserts an effect that didn't happen.  
  _Fix:_ Emit a dedicated trace whenever tradeRoute or priorityMilitary differs from the user's input (decision-made = trace, regardless of random vs explicit path), and gate the 'floored' downstreamEffect on militaryFloor actually being non-null.
- **[medium] Pipeline Rail step summaries read context keys that don't exist — receipts blank or false** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/stepMetadata.js:27-122; src/generators/steps/index.js:21`  
  stepMetadata summary functions use a vocabulary the pipeline never writes: ctx.resources?.local (step provides nearbyResources), ctx.stressors?.active (step provides stress/stressTypes) — so the rail prints 'No active stressors' even for a plague town; ctx._subsumed (never set) — subsumption always shows 'Nothing collapsed' no matter how many institutions were absorbed; ctx.economy?.prosperityBand (actual: economicState); ctx.power?.factions (actual: powerStructure.factions); ctx.tensions (never set); ctx.config?.tier (raw config lacks tier on first generation). Additionally corruptionPass is registered but missing from STEP_METADATA (falls back to raw machine name), and isolationPass's description ('detach institutions that lost their dependencies') describes a mechanic the step doesn't perform (it forces teleport infra and strips trade institutions in subsistence mode). For a product whose thesis is honest receipts, the per-step receipt strip is mostly fiction.  
  _Fix:_ Point each summary at the real provides keys (nearbyResources, stressTypes, economicState, powerStructure, institutions delta), add a corruptionPass entry, rewrite the isolationPass description, and add the promised DEV-loud test asserting STEP_METADATA keys === registered steps and that summaries return non-null on a seeded fixture.
- **[medium] noMagic treats an omitted priorityMagic as 0 while priorityMagicEffective defaults it to 50** (incoherence) — `src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:48-49,68,87,101`  
  resolveConfig.js:48-49 defaults a missing priorityMagic to 50 (priorityMagicEffective, magicLevel 'medium'), but line 68 computes noMagic = magicExists===false || (config.priorityMagic || 0)===0, which treats undefined as 0. A config that simply omits the slider (headless/API/test callers; the UI always supplies it) is simultaneously 'medium magic' downstream and 'noMagic' for route logic: isolated is filtered from town+ route pools and an explicit isolated choice is rewritten to road — for a world that nominally has magic. The same `|| 0` vs `?? 50` split recurs in ConfigurationPanel.jsx:306, so the UI's constraint preview and the engine agree only because the UI never omits the field.  
  _Fix:_ Define noMagic from the already-computed effective value: noMagic = config.magicExists === false || priorityMagicEffective === 0.
- **[medium] popToTier disagrees with POPULATION_RANGES and the UI's resolveDisplayTier (61–80 band)** (inconsistency) — `src/data/constants.js:7-32; src/store/selectors.js:27-37; src/components/ConfigurationPanel.jsx:342-347`  
  Three tier boundaries coexist: POPULATION_RANGES says thorp 8-60 / hamlet 61-400 (constants.js:7-12); popToTier says ≤80 is thorp (constants.js:26-32) — used by resolveConfig for settType:'custom'; the UI's resolveDisplayTier walks POPULATION_RANGES (selectors.js:27-35) so a custom population of 70 displays the HAMLET catalog and writes institution toggles keyed 'hamlet::…', while the generator resolves tier 'thorp' and looks up 'thorp::…' — the user's forces/excludes silently don't apply in the 61-80 band. The ConfigurationPanel dropdown adds a fourth vocabulary ('Thorp (20-80)', 'Hamlet (81-400)', ConfigurationPanel.jsx:342-347). A DM tuning a custom hamlet of 75 souls gets a thorp with none of their toggles honored.  
  _Fix:_ Make popToTier read POPULATION_RANGES (single source of truth), and regenerate the UI labels from the same table.
- **[medium] categoryToggles: three keying vocabularies; the engine's lookup can never match what the UI writes** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:175-179; src/store/toggleSlice.js:44-49; src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:122-123; src/components/InstitutionalGrid.jsx:259,467`  
  assembleInstitutions' isCategoryEnabled checks `${config.settType}::${cat}` — i.e. 'random::Economy' or 'custom::Economy' (assembleInstitutions.js:175-179). The store helper keys by display tier `${tier}::${category}` where random mode uses 'all' (toggleSlice.js:49, resolveDisplayTier) — so even if the UI wrote a disable, the generator looks up a key that can't exist for the default settType. factionCorrelation adds a third format, `${tier}_${catalogCat}` (factionCorrelation.js:122-123). In practice the whole channel is vestigial: InstitutionalGrid hardcodes isEnabled={true} and the category-toggle handler is the unused `_onCategoryToggle` (InstitutionalGrid.jsx:259,467), yet categoryToggles is still persisted, threaded through _categoryToggles into every generation, and consulted in two generator passes — dead plumbing wearing three different key formats.  
  _Fix:_ Either delete the category-toggle channel end-to-end, or restore it with one canonical key (resolved tier + 'all' fallback, matching institutionToggles' dual lookup).
- **[medium] Faction-boost additions bypass user toggles and collapse all rarity to 0.5** (inconsistency) — `src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:122-170`  
  applyFactionInstitutionBoosts checks institutionToggles[name] with a bare institution name and compares it to the string 'exclude' or boolean false (factionCorrelation.js:132-133) — but toggles are keyed `${tier}::${category}::${name}` and valued {allow,require,forceExclude} objects, so a user's force-exclude can be resurrected by a dominant faction. It also reads def.p (lines 147,154) while the catalog defines baseChance (296 occurrences, zero `p:`), so every candidate defaults to 0.5: the 'sort by baseChance descending' is a no-op and a rare institution is as likely a faction gift as a common one. Additions are also metadata stubs missing tags/baseChance (lines 160-168), invisible to tag-keyed consumers. Same def.p disease that killed the cascade pass.  
  _Fix:_ Look up toggles with the same dual-format keys assembleInstitutions uses (honoring forceExclude), read def.baseChance, and spread the full catalog def into the addition.
- **[medium] Pinned terrain doesn't constrain the random trade route — desert ports roll legally** (realism_gap) — `src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:72-95,120; src/components/ConfigurationPanel.jsx:392-402`  
  TERRAIN_ROUTE_POOLS (deliberately excluding port/river for desert, port for hills/mountain) is consulted only when terrain was ROLLED (resolveConfig.js:83-95, gated on resolvedTerrain, which requires tradeRouteAccess==='random_trade' AND terrainOverride auto). A user who pins terrainOverride='desert' and leaves the route on Random draws from the generic pool ['road','road','road','river','crossroads','port',…] — and can get a desert port or mountain port settlement, with getTerrainType honoring the override so the dossier proudly reads 'Desert / Arid + Port'. The coherence rule the data encodes applies only in fully-random mode, exactly backwards from when the user has expressed terrain intent.  
  _Fix:_ When terrainOverride is pinned and route is random_trade, draw from TERRAIN_ROUTE_POOLS[terrainOverride] instead of the generic pool.
- **[medium] Narrative steps fed terrain-catalog resources instead of the settlement's actual resources** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:30-38; src/generators/resourceGenerator.js:202-226`  
  generateNarratives passes TERRAIN_DATA[terrainT].allowedResources.slice(0,7) — the terrain's THEORETICAL pool — as nearbyResources to both generateResourceAnalysis and generateEconomicViability, and always passes specialResources: [] (generateNarratives.js:30-38). The rest of the pipeline (economy, institutions, structural validation, food) consumes the real ctx.nearbyResources that resolveResources rolled and wrote into effectiveConfig. Result: the dossier's resource-analysis/viability prose can discuss chains for resources the settlement doesn't have, ignores depletion and custom resources entirely, and the specialResources channel (ancient_ruins, magical_node feature effects) is permanently empty. Two halves of one dossier answer 'what does the land yield?' from different data.  
  _Fix:_ Pass ctx.nearbyResources (minus depleted, or annotated) and derive specialResources from the rolled rare resources; keep the terrain pool only as the 'unexploited potential' contrast.
- **[medium] Five Phase-D config fields are dead: defined, persisted, never read** (dead_config) — `src/store/configSlice.js:30-35`  
  DEFAULT_CONFIG declares customInstitutions, customResources, customTradeRoutes, powerDynamicsConfig ('pre-set faction relationships / government prefs') and defenseScenarioConfig ('pre-configured defense posture') (configSlice.js:30-35). No generator, step, or component reads any of them — custom content moved to the compendium registry (customDeps) and power/defense prefs were never wired. They persist in every saved config and imply capabilities (pre-set faction relationships, defense scenarios) that silently do nothing — exactly the kind of phantom knob a DM will set and trust.  
  _Fix:_ Delete the five fields (with a save-migration that drops them), or if power/defense presets are still roadmap, mark them and fail loudly when set.
- **[medium] goodsToggles carries two value shapes; bulk-exclude is invisible to both consumers** (inconsistency) — `src/store/toggleSlice.js:56-58,114-143; src/generators/institutionProbability.js:8-18; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1385-1403`  
  toggleGood writes booleans, but bulkSetGoods writes {allow,force,forceExclude} objects (toggleSlice.js:56-58,129-143). Consumers expect booleans: getPriorityModifiers only reacts to `=== false` (institutionProbability.js:12), so a bulk 'exclude' object never penalizes producing institutions; getUpgradeChain treats any defined value as the toggle state (`goodsToggles[toggleKey] !== undefined ? goodsToggles[toggleKey] : item.on`, economicGenerator.js:1402), where a truthy exclude-object ENABLES the good — bulk-excluding goods can turn them all on in trade streams. One map, two vocabularies, and the consumer semantics invert the user's intent on the bulk path.  
  _Fix:_ Normalize goodsToggles to one shape (boolean, or read .allow/.forceExclude at both consumers) and make bulkSetGoods write it.
- **[low] Out-of-tier force path skips the metropolis catalog and the legacy parser leaks cross-tier toggles** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:300-363`  
  fullCatalogAllTiers is built from ['thorp','hamlet','village','town','city'] only (assembleInstitutions.js:326), so a metropolis-exclusive institution can never be force-required into a smaller settlement — the toggle is silently ignored. Separately, the legacy `_`-format force block (lines 300-321) splits on '_' and discards parts[0] entirely: a toggle written for one tier ('village_Religious_X') force-injects X into ANY tier whose catalog contains it, and the parse mangles names/categories containing underscores; '::'-format keys skip this block (split('_') length 1). Two force paths, different tier semantics.  
  _Fix:_ Include metropolis in fullCatalogAllTiers and make the legacy block honor (or at least compare) the tier prefix before forcing.
- **[low] Five of seven rollable terrains have zero terrain-specific resources — reserved slots are no-ops** (realism_gap) — `src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:43-63; src/data/resourceData.js:327-411; src/generators/terrainHelpers.js:13-25`  
  resolveConfig can roll plains/hills/forest/riverside/coastal/mountain/desert (resolveConfig.js:15-18), and resolveResources reserves 2 selection slots for terrain-specific resources when terrain is set (resolveResources.js:48,62). But RESOURCE_DATA only declares terrain for desert and mountain entries (resourceData.js:327-411) — for the other five terrains the slots find nothing and terrain identity expresses only through TERRAIN_DATA institution modifiers and route pools (coastal/riverside get a partial water-unlock via getCompatibleResources). A 'forest' settlement is mechanically just its trade route plus a name; hills doubly so (no route mapping yields hills either, terrainHelpers.js:13-25).  
  _Fix:_ Add terrain tags for forest (hunting/timber), hills (grazing/quarry), riverside/coastal (existing water set), plains (grain) so the reserved slots do what the code shape promises.

Strengths: Single normalization point: resolveConfig produces effectiveConfig (resolved tier, route, normalized threat, priorityMagicEffective) and every downstream generator reads it — threat normalization (low/medium/high → heartland/frontier/plagued) and priorityMagic=effective hold consistently at nearly all call sites (src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:125-140).; Determinism is taken seriously end-to-end: per-step PRNG forks keyed by step name (pipeline.js:102-106), a monotonic trace clock instead of Date.now (generateSettlementPipeline.js:49-53), seed attached before normalize so settlement ids are stable (assembleSettlement.js:143-145), and custom-content injection iterates in sorted name order consuming zero rng when absent (resolveResources.js:123-127, assembleInstitutions.js:373-376).; The step registry's deps/provides + topological sort makes write-before-read explicit, and the effectiveConfig threading discipline (resources → stress → population written back before consumers) mostly holds (pipeline.js:47-71).; Receipt substrate is rich where it's wired: tier/terrain/route/threat/culture rolls, per-resource presence/depletion, per-institution selection with base-chance × resource-multiplier breakdown, subsumption attribution, and declined-stressor traces all emit structured causes (resolveConfig.js:146-234, resolveResources.js:152-185, assembleInstitutions.js:232-293, resolveStress.js:44-82).; The no-magic + isolation incompatibility is a well-articulated design rule enforced at three layers — UI blockers (ConfigurationPanel.jsx:305-374), resolveConfig route rewrite, and isolationGenerator's mandatory teleport infrastructure with named arcane maintainer — magic-as-trade-substitute is a coherent, DM-legible concept.; The retirement of the partial-rerun engine in favor of full same-seed regeneration (pipeline.js:76-92, settlementSlice.js:714-731) was the right call for coherence: edits preserve identity while recomputing everything, eliminating a whole class of stale-derived-state bugs.

### institutions-generation

The institution selection machinery itself (tier gates, exclusive groups, priority multipliers, terrain/resource boosts, custom injection, trace receipts) is solid and the magic-as-supplement story is genuinely well executed. The failures are almost all VOCABULARY SEAMS between the catalog and its consumers: institution records carry no services/goods linkage of their own, so five downstream layers re-derive meaning from names/categories with drifted dictionaries. Three high-impact breaks: (1) generated factions never carry a category, killing the faction-to-institution feedback pass AND the noble/crafts NPC roster (which also never receives powerStructure at all); (2) the capacity regexes miss the catalog's actual names — no parish church counts as religious welfare, no blacksmith as craft, no 'City administration' as civic — while thieves' guilds count as craft and gambling halls as administration, corrupting the DM-facing receipts; (3) the service-resolution override table shadows 115 hand-written per-institution service entries (Teleportation circle gets Airship services), and the fuzzy fallback maps village headmen to musician services. Add the subsumption self-deletion bug (Multiple courthouses removes itself), producer-eaten-by-processor rules that contradict the supply-chain layer, the dead goods-toggle penalty, the systematically wrong priorityCategory field, and a forced Teleportation circle in no-magic worlds. Each fix is small; collectively they would make the cohesion engine's receipts match what it actually generated.

- **[high] Faction-to-institution feedback loop is dead: factions never carry a category** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:65-66; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:943,990,1049`  
  deriveFactionBoosts keys on faction.category (factionCorrelation.js:65) and skips 'government' (line 66). But powerGenerator.js pushes factions as {faction, power, desc, isGoverning} with NO category field (e.g. lines 943, 990-994, 1049-1053; zero 'category:' occurrences in the file). Every faction therefore defaults to 'government' and is skipped, so deriveFactionBoosts always returns [] and applyFactionInstitutionBoosts never runs. The entire 'Item 16: power-economy correlation' step (steps/factionCorrelationPass.js:50-78) — a dominant thieves' guild pulling in criminal institutions, a temple pulling religious ones — is dead code, despite trace plumbing claiming it works. Same missing field degrades demandProfile.js:175, factionDynamics.js:150/438, neighbourFactions.js:23 and generatePopulation.js:43-49 to their name-matching fallbacks.  
  _Fix:_ Assign a category at faction creation in powerGenerator (or run domain/factionArchetypes.factionArchetype() over factions in generatePower and persist the result), then delete the dead 'government' default in deriveFactionBoosts.
- **[high] Noble and master-craftsman NPCs can never generate: gate reads data that is never passed** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/npcGenerator.js:1236-1246,1409-1415,1484-1489; src/generators/steps/generatePopulation.js:33`  
  npcGenerator.js:1246 builds powerFactionCats from settlement.powerStructure.factions[].category, then gates NOBLE_ROLES on has('noble') (line 1409) and CRAFTS_ROLES on has('crafts')||has('economy') (line 1415, comment claims 'Craft Guilds have category=economy'). Doubly broken: (a) generated factions never carry category (see other finding), and (b) steps/generatePopulation.js:33 calls generateNPCs({ tier, institutions }, ...) — powerStructure isn't even on the object, so powerFactionCats is always empty. Result: Lord/Lady of the Manor, Baron, Knight, Master Blacksmith, Guild Warden etc. never appear, even in settlements with 'Noble Families' factions and 30+ craft institutions. npcConfig._dominantFaction/_prosperity (lines 1486-1488) are likewise always null in the pipeline.  
  _Fix:_ Pass the full settlement (with powerStructure and economicState) from generatePopulation, and derive faction categories via factionArchetype() instead of the never-set .category field.
- **[high] Subsumption removes the GREATER institution itself when its name contains the lesser fragment** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:81-92 (rules 28,37,39,40,41,25)`  
  applySubsumption matches lessers by substring with no self-exclusion (subsumptionPass.js:84-90). Five rules have a greater whose own name contains the lesser fragment, so generating the greater deletes it: 'Multiple courthouses' removes itself via lesser 'courthouse'; 'Brewery' via 'brewer'; "cobbler's guild" via 'cobbler'; "tailor's guild" via 'tailor'; 'Mint (official)' via 'mint'. A city that rolls Multiple courthouses ends up with NO courthouse at all — and the trace dutifully reports it was 'absorbed into Multiple courthouses', an institution that no longer exists. Also overbroad: greater 'cathedral' lesser 'parish church' substring-matches 'Parish churches (2-5/10-30/50-100+)', so one cathedral deletes the entire parish network the tier catalog deliberately scales up.  
  _Fix:_ Skip indices whose institution IS the matched greater, and use exact-name (or word-boundary) matching for lessers instead of raw substring.
- **[medium] Subsumption deletes upstream producers because a downstream processor exists** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:42-68; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:113-116`  
  Several rules conflate 'upgraded version of X' with 'consumer of X's output': 'smelter' subsumes 'mine (open cast)' and 'charcoal burner' (subsumptionPass.js:42,61); 'butchers (3-8)' subsumes 'dairy farmer' and 'shepherd' (line 64, also substring-catches 'Shepherd collective'); 'merchant guilds (3-8)' subsumes 'salt works' and 'vintner' (66,68); 'craft guilds (5-15)' subsumes 'dairy farmer' (65); 'fish market' subsumes 'fishmonger' (44). A smelter NEEDS mines and charcoal; butchers need herders. Since computeActiveChains.js:113-116 activates supply chains by matching processingInstitutions against the surviving institution list, deleting producers can silently deactivate or weaken the very chains (charcoal/fuel, dairy, salt) the processor implies — the opposite of supply-chain coherence a DM expects.  
  _Fix:_ Restrict subsumption to genuine scale upgrades of the same function; producers feeding a processor should co-exist (they ARE the chain).
- **[high] 115 bespoke institution-service entries are dead — shadowed by override redirects, some semantically wrong** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/servicesData.js:8-240; src/data/institutionServices.js; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:804-860`  
  getServicesForInstitution checks LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES before exact key match (servicesGenerator.js:806,812,855). 115 of ~270 catalog institutions have a hand-written INSTITUTION_SERVICES entry under their exact name that can never be reached because an override redirects them to a generic key. Worst semantic losses: 'Teleportation circle' → 'Airship' services (its bespoke 'Long-distance teleportation / Planar transit / Emergency extraction' entry at institutionServices.js:1501 is dead — and this is THE magic-trade institution); 'Healer (divine, 1st level)' → generic Church/Temple (loses Cure-wounds pricing); 'Scroll scribe' → 'Wizard Tower' arcane services; 'Carpenter (part-time)'/'Carpenters (5-15)' → 'Blacksmith'; 'Bakers (5-15)' → 'Mill'; 'Kidnapping ring' → 'Assassins Guild'; 'Palisade or earthworks' → 'Garrison' (a dirt berm offering 'military escort').  
  _Fix:_ Audit the override table: delete redirects where a bespoke exact-name entry exists (let exact match win), keep overrides only for true aliases.
- **[medium] Fuzzy service fallback produces absurd mappings for unmapped government institutions** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:831-855; src/data/servicesData.js (missing entries)`  
  Institutions with neither an override nor an exact INSTITUTION_SERVICES key fall through to token-overlap fuzzy matching (servicesGenerator.js:831-855). Verified resolutions: 'Household elder' (thorp government) → 'Elder Grove Council' — the village head dispenses DRUID services; 'Village elder' and 'Village headman' → 'Village musician'; 'Town council' → 'Town crier'; 'City administration' → 'City granaries'; 'Caravanserai' (hamlet desert inn) → "Caravan masters' exchange" (metropolis-scale exchange services). The override table covers some government variants ('village reeve', "lord's steward" → Courthouse) but not these, so coverage is arbitrary. For a DM the receipt reads as nonsense: why does the headman of a 12-person thorp offer grove blessings?  
  _Fix:_ Add the ~6 missing government/lodging names to LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES (→ Courthouse / Inn-Tavern) and require a minimum fuzzy score before accepting a match.
- **[high] Religious-welfare capacity regex omits 'church' — every parish church is invisible** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:503-511`  
  REL_PATTERN (capacityModel.js:503) is /(temple|cathedral|monastery|chapel|abbey|shrine|sanctum|priory|congregation)/i — no 'church', 'priest', 'hospital', 'almshouse', 'friary'. The catalog's religious backbone is church-named: 'Parish church' (REQUIRED at village), 'Access to parish church', 'Parish churches (2-5/10-30/50-100+)', 'Priest (resident)', 'Small/Major hospital', 'Almshouse', 'Foundling home', 'Hospital network' — 16 of the Religious-category names match nothing. A village with required church+priest+graveyard gets the 'No religious institution' −5 receipt, while a thorp with a mere 'Wayside shrine' gets +9. This is the primary supply term for religious_welfare (no ledger fallback guards it), so the DM-facing 'why is welfare strained' explanation is wrong for most settlements.  
  _Fix:_ Add church|priest|friary|hospital|almshouse|foundling to REL_PATTERN, or key on category==='Religious' / tags includes 'religious' instead of names.
- **[high] Administrative capacity regex misses most real governments and counts gambling halls as civic** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:322-330`  
  CIVIC_PATTERN /(court|hall|council|government|chancery|registry|moot|forum)/i (capacityModel.js:322) misses 18 Government-category institutions including 'City administration', 'Royal seat', 'Democratic assembly', 'Merchant oligarchy', 'Noble governor', 'Guild governance', "Lord's appointee", and every small-tier government (reeve/elder/headman/steward/consensus). A city governed by 'Royal seat'+'City administration' gets 'No civic institutions detected' −8. Meanwhile 'hall' false-positives: 'Gambling halls', 'Hireling hall', "Adventurers' charter hall", 'Free company hall', "Carriers' hiring hall" all add administrative supply. Note governanceLedger legitimacy partially compensates, but the institution term and its receipt are wrong in both directions.  
  _Fix:_ Match on category==='Government' (plus courthouse/prison infra) rather than name fragments; drop bare 'hall'.
- **[medium] Craft capacity counts thieves'/assassins'/mages' guilds but not the Blacksmith** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:376-384,542-548`  
  CRAFT_PATTERN (capacityModel.js:542) includes 'guild', so "Thieves' guild chapter", "Assassins' guild", "Mages' guild", 'Merchant guilds (50-100+)', "Multiple adventurers' guilds" and 'Guild consortium' all add CRAFT supply — a criminal metropolis reads as a crafting powerhouse. Meanwhile the pattern's 'smithy'/'forge' tokens miss the actual catalog names 'Blacksmith', 'Blacksmiths (3-10)', 'Resident smith (part-time)', plus 'Potter', 'Brewer', 'Thatcher', 'Dyer', 'Fuller'. Similar cross-domain noise: FOOD_PATTERN's 'mill' counts 'Sawmill'/'Sawmill (commercial)' as food production while missing 'Fishing community', "Fisher's landing", 'Communal root cellar', 'Shepherd collective' and village 'Brewer' (pattern has 'brewery' only).  
  _Fix:_ Qualify 'guild' with craft context (or exclude Criminal/Magic/Economy categories), add smith|black smith|potter|brewer tokens, and remove sawmills from the food regex.
- **[medium] Canonical arcane matcher misses the flagship magic institutions it exists to find** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/magicLedger.js:26; src/domain/capacityModel.js:278,599`  
  ARCANE_INSTITUTION_PATTERN (magicLedger.js:26, advertised as 'one source of truth') is /(tower|sanctum|college|conclave|circle|guild.*mage|enclave|atheneum|library.*arcane)/i. 'guild.*mage' is word-order-reversed vs the actual name "Mages' guild", so the city's flagship arcane institution doesn't match; nor do 'Academy of magic', "Mages' district", "Enchanter's shop", 'Alchemist shop/quarter', 'Scroll scribe', or 'Hedge wizard' (16 Magic-category names total). False positives: 'Bardic college' (Entertainment) and anything containing 'tower' counts as arcane; conversely DEFENSE_PATTERN's 'tower' counts "Wizard's tower" as a fortification. Effect: capacityModel.deriveMagical (line 599) under-credits real arcane infrastructure that computeEffectiveMagicPresence (priorityHelpers.js:104-134) correctly recognizes — the two magic lenses disagree about the same settlement.  
  _Fix:_ Extend the pattern with mage|wizard|arcane|academy|enchant|alchemist (or reuse priorityHelpers' INST_WEIGHTS keyword sets), and exclude 'bardic college'.
- **[medium] priorityCategory field is systematically mis-assigned across the catalog** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionalCatalog.js (lines above); src/generators/historyGenerator.js:663; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1436`  
  Distribution audit: 34 Crafts entries carry priorityCategory 'government' (Charcoal burner, Maltster, Tannery, Potter, Brewer, Cobbler, Tailor, Beekeeper...), Midwife/Village scribe/Wildfowler carry 'magic' (institutionalCatalog.js:698-712), Fish market/Toll bridge/Pawnbroker 'government' (497,504,401), and the entire metropolis tier is shifted: Government→'infrastructure' (2144,2152), Religious→'infrastructure' (2181-2205), Magic→'exotic' (2215-2239), Criminal→'entertainment' (2250-2274). Consumers: historyGenerator.js:663 (hasCriminal = some priorityCategory==='criminal') reports a metropolis with a powerful Thieves' guild as having no criminal institutions; getUpgradeOpportunities (economicGenerator.js:1436) lets a Maltster satisfy the 'government' NPC-role gate. The catalog category fallback hides some damage, but the field as data is noise.  
  _Fix:_ Regenerate priorityCategory from the parent catalog category (lowercased, Defense→military, Religious→religion) and hand-fix the few genuine exceptions.
- **[medium] NPC category vocabulary ('crafts'/'magic'/'noble') doesn't match archetype keys ('craft'/'arcane')** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/npcProfile.js:32-47,269-291; src/data/historyData.js:6-855`  
  NPC roles inherit category from HISTORY_EVENTS keys (historyData.js: government, religious, noble, crafts, military, economy, criminal, magic, other) plus injected 'noble'/'crafts' roles. But npcProfile's CATEGORY_TO_ARCHETYPE (npcProfile.js:32-42) only knows 'craft' (singular) and 'arcane' — no 'crafts', 'magic', or 'noble'. So every crafts NPC maps to archetype 'other' instead of 'craft', every magic NPC to 'other' instead of 'arcane', and nobles to 'other' — their tailored leverage/vulnerability/removal templates and CATEGORY_INSTITUTION_HINTS links (npcProfile.js:269-277, also keyed 'craft'/'arcane') are unreachable from generated data. A guildmaster NPC gets generic 'other' leverage and no institution link despite a Craft guilds institution sitting in the list.  
  _Fix:_ Add crafts→craft, magic→arcane, noble→(new noble template or government) to CATEGORY_TO_ARCHETYPE and mirror keys in CATEGORY_INSTITUTION_HINTS.
- **[medium] Goods-toggle → institution-probability penalty is dead (object vs boolean, wrong key family)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/institutionProbability.js:8-19; src/store/toggleSlice.js:129-144; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:952,1156`  
  The store writes goodsToggles as `${tier}_good_${name}` → {allow, force, forceExclude} objects (toggleSlice.js:136-141; TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:38). But institutionProbability.getPriorityModifiers (institutionProbability.js:12) and structuralValidator.js:158 check `goodsToggles[key] === false` — an object is never === false, so the designed 0.35 institution-probability penalty for user-disabled goods never fires. Separately, economicGenerator.getGoodsModifiers/getHistoryModifiers look up `${tier}_export_${name}` keys (economicGenerator.js:952,1156) that nothing writes — only the `/_good_(.+)$/` regex paths (1979,2036) see real toggles. Net: the DM's 'this settlement does NOT trade in X' toggle no longer suppresses the institutions that would produce X.
