  _Fix:_ Normalize toggle reads through one helper that understands {allow,force,forceExclude} and the _good_ key family; delete the _export_ lookups.
- **[medium] Terrain and resource institution-boost tables reference 16+ institutions that don't exist** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/geographyData.js (institutionModifiers); src/data/resourceData.js (instBoosts); src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:107-121`

- **[low] Dead subsumption rules from vocabulary drift: apostrophes and nonexistent names** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:21,23,29,30,50,60`

- **[medium] No-magic worlds still receive a forced Teleportation circle for isolated towns** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:17-92,129-145; src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:430-438; src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:172-181`

The later safety net stripArcaneInstitutions (lines 129-145) explicitly skips source==='forced' and forcedByIsolation entries, so in a magicExists=false world the arcane lifeline survives the strip — a world whose premise is 'magic does not function' resolves its isolation through magic anyway. - **[low] Subsistence mode strips the smith and alehouse from isolated hamlets; food-stress flag is written but never read** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:95-126`

Isolation should increase reliance on local crafts, not delete them; cutting through-traffic institutions (wayside inn, caravanserai) is right, cutting the smith is backwards. Additionally line 124 sets institutions._isolationFoodStress = true — a property on the array — and a project-wide search finds zero readers, so the intended 'isolated subsistence settlements sometimes start food-stressed' consequence never lands (and would not survive serialization anyway).

- **[low] Faction-boost pass reads def.p but the catalog field is baseChance; toggle check uses a format nothing writes** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:129-170`

(factionCorrelation.js:147,154,166) — but catalog entries define baseChance, not p, so every candidate flattens to 0.5: a 0.05-rarity exotic is as likely a 'signature institution' as a 0.8 staple, and the sort is a no-op. The pushed record {name, category, tier, source, factionSource, p, desc} also omits tags/baseChance/priorityCategory, so boost-added institutions are taglessly invisible to tag-keyed consumers (corruption, tagsToDownstream). Currently moot because the pass never executes (factions lack category), but it will misbehave the moment that is fixed.

- **[low] Culture never gates or flavors institutions — every culture gets a European-Christian skeleton** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:30-33,116-118; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:736-765`

- **[low] Theocratic government can never be selected — the priority branch keys on names that don't exist** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/institutionProbability.js:53-55; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js (Government sections)`

The generation layer and the power layer disagree about whether theocracy exists as an institutional form.

- **[low] Hamlet 'Salt works' lacks the coastal gate its village twin (and its own description) requires** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:88-94,171-177,241-247,607-614`  
  The hamlet entry (institutionalCatalog.js:241-247) has no tradeRouteRequired/terrainRequired despite its desc: 'Only viable near salt flats or coastal access', so a landlocked plains hamlet can roll evaporation pans. The village entry (607-614) is correctly gated to port/river + coastal/riverside. Individually small, but these per-tier copies drifting apart is how the earlier vocabulary bugs were born.  
  _Fix:_ Copy the village gates onto the hamlet entry; normalize the thorp Palisade into a Defense category.
- **[low] True service orphans and dead druid vocabulary** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:136-143; src/generators/institutionProbability.js:84-86; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:69`  
  After overrides+exact+fuzzy, exactly two generated institutions resolve to NO services: 'Communal root cellar' and "Woodcutter's camp" — the latter is actively boosted near managed_forest/mountain_timber resources (assembleInstitutions.js:115,120) yet produces nothing downstream, so a forest thorp's defining economic institution is a dead end in the goods/services layer. Related dead vocabulary: 'grove shrine' and 'sacred grove' are referenced by the druid boost (institutionProbability.js:84-86), the druid tradition detector (computeActiveChains.js:69), and an INSTITUTION_SERVICES key 'Grove Shrine' — but no such institution exists in any tier catalog; druid tradition only ever fires via 'Druid Circle'/'Elder Grove Council'/"Warden's Lodge".  
  _Fix:_ Give Woodcutter's camp a timber service entry (it feeds the timber chain) and either add a Grove shrine institution or prune the three dangling references.
- **[low] getUpgradeOpportunities duplicated as dead private copy; tiny duplicate tag** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1450-1486; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:2230`  
  economicGenerator.js:1450-1486 contains _getUpgradeOpps, a byte-for-byte duplicate of the exported getUpgradeOpportunities (1409-1445) with no callers — drift bait for the NPC-role gating logic both encode. Also trivial data nit: metropolis 'Great library' has tags ['education','education'] (institutionalCatalog.js:2230). Neither affects behavior today; both are the kind of duplication that caused the live p/baseChance and 'craft'/'crafts' mismatches elsewhere.  
  _Fix:_ Delete _getUpgradeOpps; dedupe the tag.

Strengths: chainMagicSubstitution.js is exactly the 'magic as supply-chain supplement' the owner wants: tradition-gated (druid/divine/arcane/alchemy), tier-gated, with calibrated recovery rates, flavor receipts ('Druids call fish and bless the waters'), and the crucial exportable=false rule — magic sustains locals but can't be exported. All its chain ids verified present in supplyChainData.js.; The isolation design is coherent end-to-end at the happy path: institutionProbability 4x-boosts teleport/planar infra for high-magic isolated towns (priorityMagic>=70), isolationPass force-injects circle+maintainer with trace receipts, cascadePass adds airship-era docks to non-port airship settlements, and the structural validator downgrades the isolation violation to a plot-seed suggestion ('if the magic fails, the settlement dies').; capacityModel shows real conserved-ledger discipline: defense institutions are counted ONLY as a fallback when defenseLedger is absent (explicit de-dup comments at lines 274-277), food trade-route supply is fallback-only versus foodLedger's importCoverageRate, and the chains term is documented as intentionally orthogonal to the frozen ledger — the double-counting traps were thought through.; domain/factionArchetypes.js is a model fix for exactly the vocabulary-drift disease found elsewhere: one canonical detector, category-wins-then-name-inference, ordered regex rules with documented overlap reasoning, unioned from the four legacy matchers it replaced.; Trace receipts are pervasive and honest in the generation pipeline: required/forced/probabilistic selections, subsumptions ('absorbed into X'), isolation injections, and would-be faction pulls all emit structured causes — the 'why does this institution exist' promise is structurally real.; Custom-content integration in assembleInstitutions is careful: tier gates re-checked defensively, deterministic name-sorted rng so zero custom content means zero rng drift, custom subsumes mirroring UPGRADE_CHAINS with required-institution protection.; Cross-reference hygiene is clean in several places one would expect rot: every UPGRADE_CHAINS name exists in the catalog, every GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER institutionKeyword matches an institution in its tier, and 237 of 270 institutions have exact-name service entries.; computeEffectiveMagicPresence (priorityHelpers.js) is a well-designed single source of truth: slider as ambient ceiling, institutions weighted by sophistication tier not headcount, resource amplifiers, and a slider+30 anomalous-hub cap — exactly the deterministic-yet-flavorful dial the product thesis calls for.

### services-coherence

The services layer has a sound architecture — one institution→services table (INSTITUTION_SERVICES, 806 services), an explicit service→category map with keyword fallback, an 11-bucket vocabulary that is consistently consumed by the dossier, custom-content, and the healing ledger — but the data plumbing between its three name layers (catalog names → LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES → service keys → SERVICE_CATEGORY_MAP) has rotted badly. 55 of ~190 overrides point at canonical keys that no longer exist (silently degrading to fuzzy match), valid overrides shadow ~120 dedicated service sets (carpenters offer horseshoeing, bakers offer sawmilling, teleportation circles offer aerial reconnaissance), and the fuzzy matcher hands thorp household elders druidic consultation. The explicit category map claims full coverage but covers under a quarter of live services, with 79 orphan entries, and contains outright inversions — the Garrison's 'Defence services' is classified criminal and therefore suppressed in lawful settlements and shown under Criminal Services in crime-ridden ones. A parallel dead cluster (SERVICE_TIER_DATA/_UPGRADE_CHAINS/getHistoryModifiers/_export_ toggles) means the goods toggle UI shows a stale table the engine never rolls, and eight goods are permanently dead from case-mismatched requiredInstitution gates. Subsumption has three self-erasing rules (courthouse/brewery/mint vanish) plus producer-absorbed-by-consumer rules that sever supply-chain realism. A find-replace accident left 'SEVERITY' where the word 'it' belongs in live DM-facing strings. None of this breaks the sim loop — the buckets that feed capacity/causal signals (healing) work, though they conflate religious/welfare with medical care — but the generation-side mappings the owner asked about do not currently trace cleanly from catalog to dossier.

- **[high] Garrison's 'Defence services' classified criminal and gated by crime score** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1197,1955; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionServices.js:147`  
  SERVICE_CATEGORY_MAP maps 'Defence services' -> 'criminal' (servicesGenerator.js:1197), but its only provider is the Garrison ('Patrol, wall-walking, gate duty', institutionServices.js:147). Downstream, criminal-category services only survive a roll proportional to criminalEffective (servicesGenerator.js:1955): rng > min(1, crime/100*1.5) suppresses them. Net effect is exactly backwards: in a lawful settlement (crime 20) the garrison's flagship service is suppressed ~70% of the time; in a crime-ridden one it reliably appears — listed under the dossier's 'Criminal Services' header (servicesDisplay.js:27). A DM sees wall patrols as a criminal offering, or sees a garrison institution offering nothing.  
  _Fix:_ Map 'Defence services' to 'employment' (matching 'Armed patrol'/'Watch rotation') and audit the 9 criminal map entries for other legitimate-provider services ('Discreet meeting venues', 'Legitimate facade' are fine; this one is not).
- **[high] LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES is half-migrated: 55 broken targets, and valid ones shadow better data** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/servicesData.js:8-240; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:806-855`  
  55 of ~190 overrides point at canonical keys that do not exist in INSTITUTION_SERVICES ('black market'->'Black Market', 'town watch'->'Town Watch', etc.). Code at servicesGenerator.js:855 silently falls back to fuzzy matching — usually recovering the institution's own dedicated key, but not always: 'magical banking (high magic)' lands on 'Airship docking (high magic)' (a bank offering cargo loading), 'stock exchange (early)' lands on "Caravan masters' exchange". Worse, the overrides that DO resolve actively shadow richer dedicated entries: 'carpenter (part-time)'/'carpenters (5-15)' -> Blacksmith (servicesData.js:19-20) so carpenters offer Horseshoeing/Weapon creation while their real 'Basic repairs'/'Building construction' sets are unreachable; 'bakers (5-15)' -> Mill (bakers offer Sawing timber, 'Batch baking' dead); 'teleportation circle' -> Airship ('Aerial reconnaissance') while a dedicated 'Teleportation circle' key sits dead. ~120 INSTITUTION_SERVICES keys are unreachable this way.  
  _Fix:_ Delete overrides whose institution has a dedicated INSTITUTION_SERVICES key (let case-insensitive exact match win); fix or delete the 55 broken targets; add a startup assertion that every override target exists.
- **[high] Fuzzy matcher gives common governments absurd services: Household elder becomes a druid circle** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:831-855; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionalCatalog.js (thorp Government)`  
  'Household elder' — the most likely thorp government (baseChance 0.9, institutionalCatalog) — has no override and no exact key, so the token-overlap matcher (servicesGenerator.js:831-855) lands on 'Elder Grove Council' via the shared word 'elder': a mundane thorp elder offers 'Nature arbitration' and 'Druidic consultation' (institutionServices.js:458-462). 'Village elder' and 'Village headman' land on 'Village musician' ('Music and entertainment'). 'Town council' -> 'Town crier'; 'City administration' -> 'City granaries'. Also 'water source'/'dwellings' override to Inn/Tavern (servicesData.js:201-216), so 'Water source' can offer Gambling and Hiring hall; 'common grazing land'/'subsistence farming' -> Mill, so farmland can offer 'Fulling cloth' and 'Sawing timber'. These are receipts a DM reads verbatim.  
  _Fix:_ Add overrides for Household elder/Village elder/Village headman/Town council/City administration (-> Courthouse), and require the fuzzy match to clear a minimum normalized score before attributing services.
- **[high] Find-replace corruption: the word 'it' replaced with 'SEVERITY' in live DM-facing text** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1989,2019,2199,343-408; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1919; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/spatialData.js:49`

- **[high] Subsumption self-removal: courthouse, brewery, and mint erase themselves** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:28,39,43,84-93`  
  applySubsumption removes any institution whose name INCLUDES a lesser term (subsumptionPass.js:88-93). Three rules have lesser terms that are substrings of their own greater: 'multiple courthouses' subsumes 'courthouse' — 'Multiple courthouses'.includes('courthouse') is true, so the greater removes ITSELF, leaving the city with no courts; 'brewery' subsumes 'brewer' — Brewery removes itself; 'mint (official)' subsumes 'mint' — Mint (official) removes itself. The trace then tells the DM the institution 'was absorbed into' itself. Downstream, legal/food services and 'Coin production' vanish from settlements that explicitly generated the larger institution.  
  _Fix:_ Skip removal when the matched institution is the greater itself (compare indices/names), or switch lesser matching to exact-name comparison.
- **[high] Goods toggle UI renders a stale duplicate table; the engine rolls a different one** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/components/TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:6-38; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:426,491; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:860,947`

- **[high] Eight goods can never fire: requiredInstitution names case-mismatch the catalog** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:452+ (requiredInstitution fields); C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1158-1164`  
  getGoodsModifiers gates a good on a case-SENSITIVE name match (economicGenerator.js: w.name === reqInst || w.name.includes(reqInst)). Seven requiredInstitution strings differ from the catalog only by capitalization, so the gate never passes: hamlet 'Game meat' needs "Hunter's Lodge" (catalog: "Hunter's lodge"), 'Charcoal' ('Charcoal Burner' vs 'Charcoal burner'), 'Peat fuel', 'Fresh fish' ('Fisher's Landing' vs landing), village 'Fresh milk and dairy' ('Dairy Farmer'), town 'Quality boots and shoes' ("Cobbler's Guild"), 'Finished garments' ("Tailor's Guild"). - **[medium] Healing bucket conflates medical, religious, and welfare — and inflates the healing capacity signal** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1332-1349,1090-1113,1254; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/healingLedger.js:39; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:215`

- **[medium] No-magic gate in services is unsatisfiable: (priorityMagic || 50) === 0** (math_error) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1938; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:48,68`  
  servicesGenerator.js:1938 computes _noMagicSvcs = magicExists === false || (d.priorityMagic || 50) === 0. The second clause can never be true: if priorityMagic is 0 the || yields 50. The canonical test in resolveConfig.js:68 uses (config.priorityMagic || 0) === 0, so a world with magicExists=true but priorityMagic=0 is 'noMagic' to the pipeline yet still generates magic-category services. (resolveConfig has its own wobble: unset priorityMagic makes noMagic=true while priorityMagicEffective defaults to 50.) The store defaults priorityMagic to 50 so this is latent for UI users, but bites API/custom configs — the exact durability case the product cares about.  
  _Fix:_ Use (d.priorityMagic ?? 50) === 0 in servicesGenerator and (config.priorityMagic ?? 50) === 0 in resolveConfig so both gates agree.
- **[medium] Exact-match branch ignores force/exclude toggle objects for 64 institutions** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:813-830 vs 864-882`  
  The toggle store saves {allow, force, forceExclude} objects (toggleSlice). The fuzzy branch unwraps them (servicesGenerator.js:869-871), but the exact-match branch (:821) does 'const S = o[M] ... : T.on; if (!S) return;' — an exclusion object {allow:false, forceExclude:true} is truthy, so excluded services still roll, and force is never honored. The exact branch also skips the requiredTradeRoute check the fuzzy branch applies (:875). This affects the 64 catalog institutions that resolve via exact key (Brewery, Mint, Toll bridge, Druid Circle, Dairy farmer, Salt works, Midwife...). The ServicesTogglePanel cycles Allow→Forced→Excluded for these with no effect.  
  _Fix:_ Extract one shared toggle-resolution helper (object unwrap + force + requiredTradeRoute) and use it in both branches.
- **[medium] `_export_` toggle namespace is read but never written** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:952,1156,1979,2036; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/components/TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:38`

- **[low] ~450 lines of dead helpers in servicesGenerator (including the better narrative text)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:27-97,190-422,906-945`  
  Eight module-private helpers are defined and never called (each greps exactly once, its definition): _getTierConstraints, _Sv, _generateSafetyNarrative2, _jv, _Av (economic narratives), _generateTradeScore, _Rv (food-deficit narratives incl. the magic-supply-chain copy), _getCategoryDisplay plus CATEGORY_COLORS. _UPGRADE_CHAINS likewise (counted in the dead-tables finding). - **[low] Double randomness compounds service availability below configured p; first-provider-wins attribution** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:823,874,1947-1962`  
  A service must pass rng < p*tierChance inside getServicesForInstitution (servicesGenerator.js:823/874) and then, when p<1 and the domain priority multiplier v<1, a second rng > v suppression in generateAvailableServices (:1956). A p=0.7 service in a town (tier 0.65) with v=0.8 actually appears with ~36% probability, not the 70% the data author wrote. Separately, the per-name dedupe set (:1950) means whichever institution iterates first claims a shared service name ('Religious services', 'Tax collection' have 3-4 providers) — attribution depends on institution array order, so a cathedral's mass can be credited to a wayside shrine.  
  _Fix:_ Fold the priority multiplier into a single roll (p * tierChance * v), and prefer the highest-p provider when deduping names.
- **[low] Lawless-services injection ignores governance entirely** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1980-2009`  
  The fallback that injects 'No law, bring coin'/'Protection (informal)' keys off b = militaryEffective / max(8, criminalEffective) (servicesGenerator.js:1980-1985). A peaceful, well-governed town with crime 5 and military 5 gets b=0.625 < 1.2 → informal crime services injected, and at b<0.6 it is declared lawless — even though governanceLedger/government institutions (council, courthouse, reeve) exist and would adjudicate disputes. The gate reads only the military-vs-crime ratio; civic authority never enters. A DM gets 'There is no official recourse here' in a settlement whose dossier shows a functioning town council two tabs over — a cross-domain contradiction.  
  _Fix:_ Gate the lawless variant on weak governance too (e.g. require no court/council institution or low governance score), keeping the milder fence/muscle variant for weak-military-only cases.

Strengths: The 11-bucket service vocabulary is genuinely consistent producer-to-consumer: generateAvailableServices' buckets exactly match customCategories.SERVICE_TYPES, servicesDisplay's labels/EXPECTED_SERVICES_BY_TIER, healingLedger's read, and the PDF view — custom services funnel through serviceTypeKeyFromCategory with an explicit 'equipment' fallback rather than silently dropping (generateEconomy.js:167).; Every surfaced service is attributed to a provider — generated ones carry institution: A.name, and synthetic criminal services carry honest pseudo-providers ('(covert)', '(state apparatus)', '(criminal governance)', '(arcane underground)') so the WHY receipt survives even for informal offerings.; INSTITUTION_DEFAULT_CATEGORY is fully synchronized with the institution catalog (zero stale keys found in a programmatic cross-check) — the last-resort categorizer is the best-maintained layer of the classifier.; Stress-flag and safetyProfile crime-type injections (stateCrime, crimeIsGovt, arcaneBlackMarket, religiousFraud, merchantCriminalBlur) map cleanly onto matching criminal services with dedupe, tying the services surface to the corruption/stress systems — exactly the gameable-consequence coupling the product wants.; No-magic worlds are guarded at two layers (magic/exotic institution category filter plus magic-category service skip), and the custom-content path (_customProducedServices) honors toggles, avoids name collisions, and tier-scales — durable to custom content as designed.; Subsumption emits per-removal traces naming the absorbing institution, so even when a rule is wrong the DM can see what happened and why — the receipt mechanism itself is sound.

### goods-economy

The goods-economy subsystem has a strong, coherent core — the chain-first pipeline (resources → chains → exports/imports/local production) with extraction/processing gates, upstream cascades, depletion, stress annotation, and magic-as-booster is well designed and mostly maps cleanly. The damage is concentrated in the half-finished migration to that core: a Stage-3 enrichment layer (slave trade, military exports, toggle overrides, stress labels) is computed and then wiped by the chain override; toggle key namespaces (_export_/_import_) are never produced by the store; the flagship 'Port Duties' income and several dependency entries are keyed to institutions ('Major port', 'Navy (if coastal)') that no generator creates; and viability analysis is fed the terrain resource pool in three different vocabularies instead of the settlement's actual resources. Around the edges: an income multiplier that cancels itself, tier-vs-route confusion that kills the luxury import tables, backwards processor gates on necessity imports, case-sensitive institution-name mismatches, a handful of phantom resource/chain keys for the desert/mountain expansion, and one user-visible corrupted string ('convert SEVERITY to cloth'). Most fixes are small re-keyings/deletions rather than redesign; the chain spine itself is sound.

- **[high] Port Duties income and naval dependencies gated on institutions that are never generated** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1646; src/data/economicData.js:491,891`  
  Income source 'Port Duties' requires an institution named 'major port' (hasInst('major port') && tradeRoute==='port'), but no generator or catalog ever creates 'Major port' — institutionalCatalog.js only has 'Docks/port facilities', 'Warehouse district', "Harbour master's office". So a port city never gets its flagship customs income; it can only get 'River Tolls' (river route). Same orphan names elsewhere: TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS['Major port'] (economicData.js:891) and ['Navy (if coastal)'] (economicData.js:491) never fire (exact-name lookup at economicGenerator.js:2132); spatialData.js:45,151 entries dead; structuralValidator.js:110 subsumption rule "'Major port' subsumes Docks" dead; priorityHelpers.js:50 hasNavy always false; INSTITUTIONAL_SERVICE_MAP patterns 'major port'/'navy' (computeActiveChains.js:691) only ever match via 'docks/port'.  
  _Fix:_ Either add 'Major port' / 'Navy (if coastal)' as town/city-tier port institutions in institutionalCatalog, or re-key all five consumers to the names that actually generate ('Docks/port facilities', 'Shipyard', "Harbour master's office") and gate Port Duties on route==='port' + docks.
- **[high] Stage-3 export/import enrichment (slave trade, military services, toggles, stress labels) is computed then discarded by the chain override** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2017-2113 vs 2219-2246`  
  generateEconomicState builds heuristic arrays re/q, then enriches them: siege/occupied export annotations (2017-2027), goods-toggle force/exclude on exports + localProduction (2035-2058), military-services export (2075-2085), and an RNG-gated slave-trade export plus 'Enslaved labour' import (2086-2113). Then lines 2219-2226 do re.length=0 / q.length=0 and refill from chainExports/chainImports, and 2243-2246 wipe localProduction. Every enrichment is dead. Stress labels and export toggles are independently re-implemented inside deriveExportsFromChains (computeActiveChains.js:519-541) so those survive by duplication, but the military/slave logic has no chain counterpart except criminal_economy.slave_trade, which requires a 'Workhouse'. The dead slave block still consumes an RNG draw (line 2095). Classic order-dependency rot from the chain-first refactor.  
  _Fix:_ Delete the dead heuristic enrichment blocks (and their RNG draw), and port the military-services and slave-trade export/import logic to run AFTER the chain override (or into deriveExportsFromChains/deriveImportsFromChains).
- **[high] Per-good export/import toggle namespaces (`_export_`, `_import_`) are never written by the store** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/store/toggleSlice.js:8,136 vs src/generators/economicGenerator.js:952,1156,1397`  
  toggleSlice.js documents and creates only `${tier}_good_${name}` keys (toggleSlice.js:8,136; TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:38 confirms). But getGoodsModifiers reads `${tier}_export_${name}` (economicGenerator.js:1156), getHistoryModifiers the same (952), and getUpgradeChain reads `${tier}_import_${name}` (1397). Those toggle keys can never exist, so per-good export overrides and all import toggles are dead vocabulary; DM control over goods flows exclusively through the `_good_` regex paths — two of which (economicGenerator.js:2035-2058) are themselves dead per the chain-override finding. Net: the only live toggle path is deriveExportsFromChains' `_good_` handling plus the income-source push at 1977-1995.  
  _Fix:_ Unify on the `${tier}_good_${name}` namespace everywhere (or have the store emit `_export_`/`_import_` keys); delete whichever reader paths are not meant to be user-controllable.
- **[high] Economic viability is fed the terrain resource POOL (mixed vocabulary), not the settlement's selected resources** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:31-38; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:71-106,160-196; src/data/geographyData.js:54,131,213`  
  generateNarratives.js:31-38 passes TERRAIN_DATA[terrain].allowedResources.slice(0,7) as nearbyResources into generateEconomicViability. Two problems: (1) it is the terrain's potential pool, not config.nearbyResources actually chosen, so 'Opportunity: process X' suggestions and resource-supply issues describe resources the settlement may not have; (2) allowedResources vocabulary is inconsistent — coastal/riverside use free text ('fish','shellfish','pearls','vegetables', geographyData.js:54-66,131-142) while mountain uses RESOURCE_DATA keys ('iron_deposits', geographyData.js:213-225). computeFactionPowers fuzzy-compares these against chain.resource display labels ('Grain fields', 'Iron ore deposits') via slice(0,6/8) (economicGenerator.js:73-79,165-169): snake_case keys never match, free text sometimes matches. So chain suggestions fire for coastal terrains but silently never for mountain ones, and 'no viable resource supply' issues rely entirely on the keyword/trade-access fallbacks.  
  _Fix:_ Pass effectiveConfig.nearbyResources (RESOURCE_DATA keys) into generateEconomicViability and match via RESOURCE_DATA[key].label or a key-to-chain map (RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS already exists); normalize TERRAIN_DATA.allowedResources to RESOURCE_DATA keys.
- **[high] Corrupted DM-facing string: 'weavers and fullers convert SEVERITY to cloth'** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1919`  
  The 'Wool & Textile Trade' income description reads 'Local flocks provide raw wool; weavers and fullers convert SEVERITY to cloth sold across the region.' (economicGenerator.js:1919). A refactor find/replace replaced a word (likely 'it'/'fleece') with the imported constant name SEVERITY. This text is displayed verbatim in the Economics tab/PDF — immediately visible nonsense to the DM audience.  
  _Fix:_ Restore the sentence ('…convert fleece to cloth…') and grep the repo for other SEVERITY-in-prose artifacts.
- **[medium] Economy-output multiplier cancels itself in income normalization** (math_error) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1996-2010`  
  Income weights are computed as percentage * priorityToMultiplier(economyOutput) (economicGenerator.js:1997-1998), then normalized by the total (1999-2002). Since every entry is multiplied by the same constant, it divides out exactly — the economy slider has zero effect on displayed income percentages through this path. The slider's only income influence is the Math.round(economyOutput/N) magnitudes inside individual resource-income entries. Dead math that looks load-bearing.  
  _Fix:_ Remove the multiplier from normalization, or apply it asymmetrically (e.g. only to commerce-type sources) so it actually shifts the mix.
- **[medium] getUpgradeChain confuses trade route with tier: luxury/from-higher import tables unreachable** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1385-1406,1171-1382; src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:347-442`  
  getUpgradeChain branches on `route === 'city' || route === 'metropolis'` and `route === 'metropolis'` (economicGenerator.js:1392-1395), but route is a trade-route key (road/river/port/crossroads/isolated) — never a tier. Both call sites also hardcode isFromHigher=false (877, 1125). Result: UPGRADE_GOODS_BY_TIER's town.fromCityOrMetropolis (luxury textiles, spices, banking…), city.fromMetropolis, and village.fromHigher branches are unreachable; town/city always use fromHinterland. The whole 200-line UPGRADE_GOODS_BY_TIER table (1171-1382) is also a hard fork of IMPORT_GOODS_BY_TIER (tradeGoodsData.js:347-442), and since primaryImports are overwritten by chainImports, its only surviving output is the entrepôt 'transit' list.  
  _Fix:_ Delete UPGRADE_GOODS_BY_TIER and the dead branches; derive transit goods from IMPORT_GOODS_BY_TIER directly, or wire the city/metropolis branches to a real 'nearest higher tier' input if that concept matters.
- **[medium] Isolated settlements still receive structural and finished-goods imports (and service exports)** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:560-630; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1503-1576,2217-2242`  
  deriveImportsFromChains suppresses imports only for isolated thorp/hamlet/village (computeActiveChains.js:562-564). Isolated towns/cities/metropolises with no teleportation still get tier-structural imports — 'Bulk grain and foodstuffs', 'Luxury textiles and exotic goods', 'Bulk raw materials' (610-618) — and computeFinishedGoodsDemand (economicGenerator.js:1503-1576, invoked at 2217) pushes incense/arms/reagent imports with no route gate, including into an isolated village's just-emptied import list. Isolated villages also keep institutional service exports ('Financial services (letters of credit)') because serviceExports are appended (2222-2224) and only thorp/hamlet are cleared (2231-2242). This contradicts the same function's narrative ('cannot source specialist goods', 1027) and getInstitutionServices returning [] for isolated (906).  
  _Fix:_ Gate tier-structural imports and computeFinishedGoodsDemand on route!=='isolated' || hasMagicTrade, and extend the subsistence clear (or service-export suppression) to isolated villages and non-magic isolated towns.
- **[medium] Necessity-import gates are backwards: having a processor suppresses the raw-material import** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:902-935`  
  getInstitutionServices adds 'Iron' to city/metropolis imports only if NO smith/metalworker exists (economicGenerator.js:917-921), 'Timber' only if NO carpenter/sawmill (928-933), and 'Grain' is suppressed by any institution containing 'farm' (922-927). Processors CONSUME raw inputs — a city with smiths and no iron_deposits needs iron imports more, not less; one 'farm' keyword should not erase a metropolis's grain demand. TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS models this correctly in the opposite direction (institution present + resource absent → dependency), so the two layers actively disagree about who needs imports.  
  _Fix:_ Flip the gates: suppress the import when the local RESOURCE (iron_deposits/managed_forest/grain_fields) exists, not when the consuming institution exists — or drop this function and let TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS + chain imports own necessity imports.
- **[medium] RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS uses nonexistent need prefixes for desert/mountain resources** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1557-1567`  
  Chain activation ids must be `${needKey}.${chainId}` (computeActiveChains.js:78-97). RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS entries for the desert/mountain expansion reference need keys that don't exist: 'agricultural.food_processing'/'agricultural.brewing' (date_palms, supplyChainData.js:1559), 'agricultural.food_processing' (desert_salt, 1561), 'agricultural.livestock' (camel_herds, 1562), 'agricultural.livestock'/'agricultural.textiles' (alpine_pasture, 1565), 'services.hospital' (hot_springs_mineral, 1567). Real keys are food_security/manufacturing/healing_medicine. So these resources never set activatedByResource: their chains display 'operational' instead of 'running', deriveLocalProductionFromChains skips their outputs, and the sort/status logic treats them as resource-less. Alpine pasture activates nothing at all.  
  _Fix:_ Re-key to existing chains (food_security.livestock, food_security.grain/brewing, manufacturing.textiles, healing_medicine.herbalism) or add the missing chains.
- **[medium] Finished-goods demand model: pure suppliers can never export, and overlapping keywords double-count supply** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1516-1576; src/data/economicData.js:922-1083`  
  computeFinishedGoodsDemand skips a category when totalDemand===0 (economicGenerator.js:1538) BEFORE computing supply, so a town of three weaponsmiths with no garrison can never emit the military exportBonus (1572) — the strongest surplus-export case is the one excluded. Supply keywords also overlap: 'blacksmith' AND 'blacksmiths (3-10)' both substring-match one 'Blacksmiths (3-10)' institution → 2+3=5 supply; 'specialized metalworkers' + 'specialized metal' → 10 (economicData.js:945-953); 'apothecary' + 'apothecary district' similarly (1069-1071). This inflates supply and under-reports imports. And the luxury category lists 'luxury goods' as a supplier keyword (1044) which matches the 'luxury goods quarter' CONSUMER (1033) — demand 3, supply 3, the quarter permanently self-cancels and never imports silk/dyes.  
  _Fix:_ Compute supply before the early-continue and allow demand-0 exportBonus; make supplier matching take the single best (longest) keyword per institution; remove 'luxury goods' from luxury suppliers.
- **[medium] config.mustImport viability block is doubly dead (never populated + case-impossible match)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:244-278`  
  generateStabilityScore reads config?.mustImport (economicGenerator.js:245), but nothing ever copies TERRAIN_DATA.mustImport into config — the only writers are terrain data (geographyData.js) and resourceGenerator reading terrain.mustImport directly. Even if populated, hasProcessor lowercases names then checks .includes('Mill'), .includes('Sawmill'), .includes('Smith'), .includes('Smelter') with capitals (248-253) — always false. So the 'Imports timber/metal' dependency warnings and their two plot hooks (timber blight, wartime iron shortage — good DM material) are unreachable.  
  _Fix:_ Thread terrain.mustImport into effectiveConfig (or pass terrain in), and lowercase the keyword literals; or delete the block and move the hooks onto chain-derived imports.
- **[medium] Case-sensitive requiredInstitution names in GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER never match the catalog** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:452-832 vs src/data/institutionalCatalog.js; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1151-1168`  
  getGoodsModifiers matches required institutions case-sensitively (`w.name === reqInst || w.name.includes(reqInst)`, economicGenerator.js:1162-1163). GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER requires "Hunter's Lodge", "Charcoal Burner", "Peat Cutter", "Fisher's Landing", "Dairy Farmer", "Cobbler's Guild", "Tailor's Guild" (tradeGoodsData.js:477,484,498,505,588,680,687) but the catalog generates "Hunter's lodge", 'Charcoal burner', 'Peat cutter', "Fisher's landing", 'Dairy farmer', "Cobbler's guild", "Tailor's guild" (institutionalCatalog.js:162-192,227,1134,1141). Those goods (Game meat, Charcoal, Peat fuel, Fresh fish, Fresh milk and dairy, Quality boots and shoes, Finished garments) can never roll. The town 'Enslaved persons' entry uses an alien schema (institutions/routeBoost, no p/on — tradeGoodsData.js:594-600) the reader can't evaluate, and EXPORT_GOODS_BY_TIER's twin uses the misspelled key 'requiresInstitution' (tradeGoodsData.js:135,207).  
  _Fix:_ Lowercase both sides of the match; normalize the slave-trade entries to the standard schema (or delete); unify 'requiresInstitution' → 'requiredInstitution'.
- **[medium] Three diverging copies of the tier-goods table; the SERVICE_TIER_DATA reader expects the wrong schema** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:27,452; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:491; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:947-965`  
  The same goods catalog exists three times: EXPORT_GOODS_BY_TIER (tradeGoodsData.js:27, used only for the editor's add-export picker), GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER (tradeGoodsData.js:452, live in generateTradeIncomeStreams), and SERVICE_TIER_DATA (servicesGenerator.js:491) with a different field schema (baseChance/defaultEnabled instead of p/on). getHistoryModifiers (economicGenerator.js:947-965) iterates SERVICE_TIER_DATA expecting .on/.p/.requiredInstitution — all undefined — so it always returns [] (it is only called by the dead _computeIncomeStreams, but it reads as live code). - **[medium] Export-vs-necessity-import filter is a no-op; 'hasSaltLocal' is named backwards** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1117-1124`  
  generateTradeIncomeStreams filters exports with `!necessityImports.includes(item.name)` (economicGenerator.js:1120) but getGoodsModifiers returns plain strings, so item.name is undefined and nothing is ever filtered — a settlement can list the same good as export and necessity import in the heuristic layer (which still feeds income-source derivation at 1865+). The adjacent salt logic works but the flag is inverted in name: hasSaltLocal (1118) is true when Salt appears in necessityImports, i.e. when there is NO local salt. The downstream rule (no salt-preserved exports without local salt unless entrepôt) is right; the name guarantees a future maintainer breaks it.  
  _Fix:_ Filter on the string itself (`!necessityImports.includes(item)`), and rename hasSaltLocal → mustImportSalt.
- **[medium] Commodity vocabulary errors: coal yields 'timber', livestock/dairy map to 'grain'** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/resourceData.js:264; src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:845-847; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:913-933`

COMMODITY_CATEGORY_MAP maps livestock/dairy/'game meat' → 'grain' (tradeGoodsData.js:845-847), so a pure pastoral settlement registers grain localProduction: it skips Grain necessity imports (economicGenerator.js:922-927) and can earn a 'Grain Sales' income source with no grain fields (1891-1905). - **[low] Depleted-resource and timber-income maps reference keys that don't exist; mountain/desert resources omitted** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1939,2196-2212`

- **[low] Unreachable 'Bandit Raids' hook and ratio-as-stock 'days of reserves' math** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:203-241,484`  
  In generateStabilityScore the first branch captures route==='isolated'||'road' (economicGenerator.js:211), so the nested `route === 'road' && hasDeficit` Bandit Raids hook inside the `else if (route !== 'isolated')` branch (235-240) can never execute — road settlements get only the generic starvation hook, ports get richer material. Also, 'days of reserves' is computed as (dailyProduction/dailyNeed)*30 (232, 484) — that's a production ratio scaled to a month, not a stock level; a settlement producing 50% of need is told it has '15 days of reserves' regardless of storage. Granaries (which the code checks elsewhere) don't influence it.

- **[low] Systematically misleading names: food balance lives in buildFactionList, NPC roles live in HISTORY_EVENTS** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:66,203,284,793,1409; src/data/historyData.js`

- **[low] 'Subsistence' prosperity label never survives, and its remap distribution contradicts its own comments** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1062-1068,2293,2402-2404`

- **[low] Prosperity inputs and chain plumbing inconsistencies: raw slider vs compound flag, duplicate chain id, dead trace needKeys** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2311; src/data/supplyChainData.js:292,347; src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:240-263`

  _Fix:_ Use economyOutput in both places; rename one chain id (coastal_shipbuilding); fix the trace switch keys.
- **[low] Mill/granary plausibility checks have arbitrary edges; CRITICAL-severity items parked where they can't affect viability** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:518-545,807-820; src/data/resourceData.js:688-694`  
  The 'No Milling Facility' check fires only for 1000<population<5000 (economicGenerator.js:535) — a 50,000-person metropolis grinding grain with no mill (and no 'Access to external mill') raises nothing, while the granary check (519-531) applies to all town+ with no analogous carve-out. Both are pushed with severity SEVERITY.CRITICAL into the warnings array, but buildConflict counts criticals only from issues (53-58), so 'critical' food-storage findings can never flip the viability verdict — the severity vocabulary says one thing, the plumbing another. INDUSTRY_WATER_NEEDS messages also read waterNeed.description (815) but the data field is named 'reason' (resourceData.js:692), so the specific explanation never displays.  
  _Fix:_ Extend the mill check to city+ (accepting flour imports as the escape hatch), decide whether granary/mill gaps are issues or warnings and label severity accordingly, and read .reason.

Strengths: The chain-first derivation spine is genuinely coherent: nearbyResources → RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS activation → computeActiveChains (tier gates, magic=0 suppression, substitution, depletion) → deriveExportsFromChains / deriveImportsFromChains / deriveLocalProductionFromChains, with three well-judged gate layers (RESOURCE_EXTRACTION_GATES so cities don't 'mine' ore with courthouses; RESOURCE_GOOD_INST_GATES and CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES so finished goods require their processor). Exactly the receipts-for-WHY structure the product promises.; Multi-order chain logic is real, not decorative: upstream dependencies cascade in two passes, missing upstream converts into named intermediate-good imports (UPSTREAM_IMPORT_LABELS), and the external-mill banalité rule (food secure but surplus captured by the lord's mill toll, computeActiveChains.js:148-162) is outstanding DM-grade medieval realism.; Magic-as-supplement is implemented consistently as a booster, not a parallel economy: hasTeleportationInfra is the single gate reused everywhere isolation matters (viability text, dependency severity, prosperity route base, import phrasing); food deficits get tiered magical offsets (druid 65% > divine 40% > arcane 30%) with attributed notes; income has a three-tier arcane ladder (apothecary → spellcasting services → arcane industry) gated by priority+institution+tier, plus an Enchanted Goods Premium that cross-boosts mundane craft exports.; The finished-goods demand-gap layer (INSTITUTION_FINISHED_GOODS_DEMAND) is a smart middle band between raw-resource dependencies and exports: consumers/suppliers per category with gap-scaled import labels ('Replacement arms' → 'bulk contract'), and finishedGoodsCategoryOf lets cross-settlement trade bridge a custom good to a neighbour's generic demand.; Income sources almost all trace to a real institution or flag, with stress-aware variants (Military Extraction under stateCrime, theocratic tithes vs plain tithes, Magical Trade Revenue replacing Market Taxes under teleport isolation), and the criminal income share reuses safetyProfile.blackMarketCapture so the Shadow Economy numbers agree across the dossier.; Stress handling is threaded end-to-end and consistent: siege/famine modify production multipliers, add Grain/Salt/Iron imports, collapse or annotate exports ('naval route only', 'taxed by occupation' — re-implemented correctly in the chain layer), and cap prosperity; foodGenerator's terrain-structural nuance (mountain/desert food imports are design, not crisis) is exactly right for the audience.; The §14 custom-content extension points (custom food producers/consumers, finishedGoodsSupply, confirmed chains promoting trade endpoints, satisfies-category folding) are uniformly inert-by-default with deterministic ordering — durable to custom content as the thesis demands.

### supply-chains

Supply chains work end to end as: catalog (SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS) -> computeActiveChains gates (tier, institution substring match, fuzzy resource-label resolution, entrepôt route, mundane substitutes, depletion) -> status assignment (operational/running/entrepot/vulnerable/impaired from trade dependencies) -> two overlapping upstream cascades -> magic substitution -> export/import/localProduction derivation -> stored on economicState.activeChains; domain consumers re-derive canonical statuses (stable/strained/scarce/...) via deriveSupplyChainState, which layers live regional pressure. The architecture is sound and the domain-side read path is genuinely unified, but the data layer is full of broken mappings: seven chains (the entire entrepôt-luxury, magic-item, and smuggling economy) can never activate because their processor lists are empty; RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS references nonexistent need keys and omits every newer terrain chain, splitting 'can run' from 'counts as running'; civic/healing chains are backed by absurd institutions (bathhouse adjudicating trials, foundling home as the divine healer) while the real churches and hospitals in the catalog back nothing; the needKey literals 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' used by NEED_HEURISTICS, trade-connectivity scoring, and the smuggling clock match nothing, severing trade chains from the causal loop; statuses 'magically_sustained' and 'unexploited' canonicalize to 'stable' (magic-degraded chains read as healthy in food scores) while 'substituted'/'blocked'/'captured' have zero producers; subsumption deletes sole chain processors and export-gate institutions (merchant guilds erase the salt chain); and a third, fully vocabulary-incompatible chain model (RESOURCE_CHAINS in resourceGenerator) ships dead analysis to the Viability/Resources tabs. Magic is a real supplement (substitution, teleport imports) but never a booster of healthy chains, and its recovery magnitude is display-only.

- **[high] Seven catalog chains can never activate (empty processingInstitutions vs hard gate)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:528-560,644-710,1047-1083,1207-1222`  
  computeActiveChains requires at least one matched processing institution (matchedInsts.length === 0 -> return), but seven chains declare processingInstitutions: [] — trade_entrepot.spices_dyes, trade_entrepot.silk_luxury_textiles, trade_entrepot.transit_finance, manufacturing.luxury_goods, arcane_magical.magical_goods, arcane_magical.planar, criminal_economy.smuggling. These are the headline entrepôt chains plus the entire magic-item/planar economy and smuggling — none can EVER appear in any settlement. RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS still points resources at them (crossroads_position -> spices_dyes/transit_finance, precious_metals/gemstone_deposits -> luxury_goods, magical_node -> magical_goods, deep_harbour -> transit_finance), so those resources silently feed nothing. A DM generating a port metropolis gets no silk, spice, luxury, banking, magic-item, or smuggling chain.  
  _Fix:_ Give each dead chain real processors (merchant guilds/customs house for spices+silk, banking house for transit_finance, jeweller for luxury_goods, mages' guild/enchanter for magical_goods, planar trader for planar, thieves' guild for smuggling), or let entrepot-only chains pass the institution gate when isEntrepotRoute holds.
- **[high] RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS references nonexistent need keys ('agricultural.*', 'services.hospital')** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1556-1568`  
  The desert/mountain resource entries map to chain ids whose needKey does not exist in SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS: date_palms -> agricultural.food_processing/agricultural.brewing, desert_salt -> agricultural.food_processing, camel_herds -> agricultural.livestock, alpine_pasture -> agricultural.livestock/agricultural.textiles, hot_springs_mineral -> services.hospital. Valid keys are food_security, manufacturing, etc. These ids enter chainActivatedByResource and match nothing, so the newer terrain resources activate fewer chains than intended and never produce 'running' status. The dedicated terrain chains that DO exist (date_palm_harvest, alpine_wool, camel_caravan, oasis_agriculture, desert_glasswork, mountain_timber_harvest, harbour_trade, river_milling, floodplain_agriculture, crossroads_trade, mountain_pass_trade) are entirely absent from RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS.  
  _Fix:_ Rewrite the desert/mountain entries to the real composite ids (e.g. date_palms -> ['raw_extraction.date_palm_harvest','food_security.brewing'], alpine_pasture -> ['raw_extraction.alpine_wool','food_security.livestock'], hot_springs_mineral -> ['arcane_magical.alchemy','healing_medicine.divine_healing']) and add every terrain chain to the lookup.
- **[high] Two disagreeing resource->chain mappings: activatedByResource flag vs fuzzy label runnability** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:13-23,78-91,120-144,182,647; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1472-1568`  
  Chain activation has two parallel resource mappings that disagree. Runnability uses fuzzy matching of the chain's resource LABEL ('Managed woodland' -> managed_forest) while the 'running' status uses RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS composite ids. Consequences: (a) mountain_timber maps to raw_extraction.timber in RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS, but the timber chain's label resolves to managed_forest, so near mountain timber the timber chain is flagged activated-by-resource yet is NOT runnable; (b) all terrain chains missing from RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS (river_milling, floodplain_agriculture, alpine_wool, etc.) run with activatedByResource=false, so they show 'operational' (the pass-through look) instead of 'running' and are excluded from deriveLocalProductionFromChains (filters c.activatedByResource), so their outputs never appear in localProduction.  
  _Fix:_ Derive activatedByResource from the same resolved resourceKey used for runnability (single source of truth), keeping RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS only for multi-chain fan-out, and add a build-time assert that every catalog chain id appears in the lookup.
- **[high] Civic/healing chains are backed by absurd institutions; outputs lists contain institution names** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:905-932,1095-1129,1030-1040`  
  religion_civic.parish ('Parish & Faith') is processed only by Almshouse/Foundling home and gated on an 'Ancient grove' resource — yet Parish church / Cathedral / Wayside shrine institutions exist in the catalog and are not processors, so most villages with a church have no faith chain, while one near a grove with an almshouse does. law_governance ('Law & Governance') is processed by Workhouse and Public bathhouse — a bathhouse producing criminal trials. healing_medicine.hospital is processed by Almshouse/Foundling home while 'Small hospital'/'Major hospital' institutions exist but never activate it; divine_healing requires Hot springs and is processed only by Foundling home. The outputs arrays even contain institution names as goods: divine_healing outputs "Mages' guild"; spellcasting outputs "Wizard's tower" and "Mages' guild" — institutions leaking into the goods vocabulary.  
  _Fix:_ Re-author processors from the actual institution catalog (parish -> Parish church/Cathedral/Wayside shrine; law -> Courthouse/Moot hall; hospital -> Small/Major hospital; divine_healing -> temples), drop the Ancient-grove gate on parish, and strip institution names from outputs.
- **[high] NEED_HEURISTICS and trace downstream switch use a needKey vocabulary that does not exist** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:107-155; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:240-263`  
  NEED_HEURISTICS keys 'trade', 'energy', 'arcane' never match real needKeys ('trade_entrepot', 'arcane_magical'; 'energy' has no chains — fuel lives under raw_extraction). So every trade, arcane, defense, healing, knowledge, religion, entertainment, and criminal chain falls back to generic beneficiaries/victims ('settlement residents') and the non-answer failure consequence 'The settlement adapts; specifics depend on context' — exactly the receipts a DM wants when an entrepôt or arcane chain fails. The same dead vocabulary is repeated in generateEconomy's downstreamEffects switch (cases 'trade', 'energy', 'arcane'), so 8 of 11 need categories trace to the generic 'economy' target.  
  _Fix:_ Key both tables on the actual need keys and add entries for the six uncovered categories (defense_security, healing_medicine, knowledge_information, religion_civic, entertainment_culture, criminal_economy).
- **[high] Trade connectivity and the smuggling clock filter on needKey 'trade' — matches nothing, ever** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/causalState.js:360; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/hookEscalation.js:430`  
  causalState.deriveTradeConnectivity filters chains where c.needKey === 'trade'; the real key is 'trade_entrepot', so entrepôt/trade chain health (stable +5, blocked/collapsing -18) is computed over an always-empty list — a blocked caravan or warehouse chain never moves trade_connectivity, breaking the chains->causal.scores->sim loop for the entire trade domain. hookEscalation.deriveEscalationClocks has the same comparison, so the smuggling_rise escalation clock can never trigger from a disrupted trade chain (only bread_riot works, because food_security is spelled correctly).  
  _Fix:_ Change both comparisons to 'trade_entrepot' and add a shared NEED_KEYS constant (or a test that every needKey literal in src matches Object.keys(SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS)).
- **[high] 'magically_sustained' and 'unexploited' statuses canonicalize to 'stable'; 'substituted'/'blocked'/'captured' have zero producers** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2236-2241; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:57-79; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/components/new/SupplyChainsPanel.jsx:192,259`  
  chainMagicSubstitution emits status 'magically_sustained' and economicGenerator emits 'unexploited' (subsistence-isolated trade chains), but canonicalSupplyChainStatus knows neither, so both default to 'stable'. A grain chain running at 50-70% output via druidic magic (exportable stripped) reads +6 'runs normally' in capacityModel and +8 in causalState foodSecurity — the wrong direction, and it erases the magic story from every canonical consumer. Meanwhile the canonical states built for exactly this ('substituted') plus 'blocked' and 'captured' are priced by consumers (capacityModel -15, causalState -20, deriveRegionalState 0.85/0.7) but NO code path ever produces them — corruption/faction capture never marks a chain 'captured' despite the vocabulary existing. SupplyChainsPanel also checks a status 'broken' that nothing emits.  
  _Fix:_ Map magically_sustained -> 'substituted' and unexploited -> 'strained' (or a dedicated dormant state) in LEGACY_TO_CANONICAL; wire a 'captured' producer from the corruption/faction layer; delete the 'broken' checks.
- **[high] Subsumption deletes the only institutions that activate chains or pass export gates** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:38,61-66; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:352-444`  
  subsumptionPass runs before generateEconomy and removes 'lesser' institutions with no awareness of chain processors or export-gate keywords. Concrete breaks: 'Merchant guilds (3-8)' subsumes 'Salt works' — Salt works is the salt chain's ONLY processor, so any settlement with merchant guilds (most villages+) loses the Salt & Preservation chain entirely; 'Tanner (established)' subsumes 'Tannery', but CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES requires the substring 'tannery' for Leather goods/armour/boots — upgrading the institution removes leather export rights; 'Specialized metalworkers' and 'Luxury goods quarter' subsume 'Jeweller' while Jewellery/Cut gemstones gates require 'jewel'; 'Smelter' subsumes 'Mine (open cast)' while the 'Raw gemstones' gate requires 'mine'; Butchers subsume Shepherd/Dairy farmer, starving textiles/alpine_wool/livestock processor lists. Bigger institution -> less economy is backwards.  
  _Fix:_ Make every 'greater' institution satisfy the chain-processor and gate keywords its 'lesser' satisfied (add greater names to the gate keyword lists, or resolve gates through the subsumption rules), and never subsume an institution that is a chain's sole processor.
- **[high] resourceGenerator's RESOURCE_CHAINS analysis is a third, vocabulary-incompatible chain model fed the wrong inputs** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/resourceGenerator.js:18-26,35-36,146-161; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:31-34; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/resourceData.js:424-553`  
  resourceData.RESOURCE_CHAINS uses rawResource values like 'wool', 'grain', 'iron ore', 'glass sand' and processor names like "Weavers' guild", 'Winery', "Coppersmiths' guild". evaluateEconomicActivity tests nearbyResources.includes(chain.rawResource) — exact match against keys like grain_fields — so virtually no chain ever activates (alpineWool, whose rawResource is literally the key 'alpine_pasture', is the exception). Processor checks use exact i.name === name against a catalog that spells these institutions differently ('Weavers/Textile workers'). Worse, generateNarratives feeds it TERRAIN_DATA.allowedResources (generic words: 'fish','salt','pearls') instead of the settlement's actual nearbyResources. The resulting resourceAnalysis (exploitation, gaps with 'high' severity 'X exists but lacks access to grain', availableResources) is shown in Resources/Viability tabs and the PDF — a parallel universe disconnected from economicState.activeChains.  
  _Fix:_ Either delete RESOURCE_CHAINS and re-derive the viability/exploitation report from economicState.activeChains (one chain model), or translate it to resource keys + catalog institution names and pass config.nearbyResources.
- **[medium] defenseGenerator reads raw legacy chain statuses, so live regional pressure never reaches defense** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:479-535; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:829-842`  
  Food and trade capacity read chains through deriveAllSupplyChainStates (canonical statuses including post-generation regional-pressure escalation), but defenseGenerator reads settlement.economicState.activeChains raw and matches only legacy strings ('operational','running','vulnerable','impaired'). A mid-campaign regional route shock that escalates the food_processing or garrison chain to 'scarce'/'collapsing' in every other consumer leaves defense readiness untouched, because the frozen legacy status on the stored chain still says 'running'. Also the 'fortification' chain it reads has empty outputs/services and requires a LOCAL stone-quarry resource to exist at all, so a walled city without a quarry silently gets neither the +6 maintained-walls bonus nor the -4 penalty.  
  _Fix:_ Have the defense chain-linkage consume deriveSupplyChainState statuses (stable/strained/scarce) like capacityModel does, and let the fortification chain run via a substitute (imported stone / brickmaker) when walls exist without a quarry.
- **[medium] Mundane resource substitution is mislabeled 'magical substitute'; magic substitution reports no substitutes** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:128-134,183; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:286-297; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/state/deriveSystemState.js:259`  
  computeActiveChains sets substituteActive when a MUNDANE resource substitute covers the gap (e.g. River fisheries standing in for Fishing grounds). deriveSupplyChainState's inferSubstitutes then reports 'active magical / alternative substitute in use' for that flag — a DM reading the dossier is told fish are conjured when the village just fishes the river. Conversely, chains genuinely sustained by magic (magicNote/magicRecovery from chainMagicSubstitution) never set substituteActive, so their canonical substitutes list is empty and deriveSystemState's 'vulnerable supply chains' counter (resourceDepleted || substituteActive) counts mundane substitution but not magical dependence. Producer and consumer disagree about what the flag means.  
  _Fix:_ Carry the substitute's NAME on the chain (substituteResource) and have inferSubstitutes report it verbatim; set a separate magicSustained flag from chainMagicSubstitution and include it in vulnerability counts.
- **[medium] Two parallel, contradictory upstream-dependency graphs** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:236-276,287-334; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js (upstreamChains fields)`  
  Downstream cascade is computed twice from different sources of truth: the hardcoded CHAIN_DEPS table in computeActiveChains and the catalog's per-chain upstreamChains. They disagree: caravan_trade depends on ['animal_husbandry','grain'] in CHAIN_DEPS but ['warehouse_logistics'] in the catalog; weapons_armor is ['iron','smelting'] vs ['smelting']; leather_goods ['leather','livestock','hunting'] vs ['livestock']; CHAIN_DEPS references upstream ids ('forage' for beekeeping, 'reed_marsh' for ceramics) the catalog never declares. Both passes run, plus a third 'second pass' re-propagation, so which note/status a chain ends with depends on pass order rather than one declared dependency model. The UPSTREAM_IMPORT_LABELS import fallback only fires for catalog upstreamChains, so CHAIN_DEPS-only dependencies degrade status without generating the matching import.  
  _Fix:_ Delete CHAIN_DEPS and move its extra edges into the catalog's upstreamChains so one declared graph drives both the status cascade and the import derivation.
- **[medium] Duplicate chain ids and near-duplicate chains double-count and shadow each other** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:56-135,292-304,347-358,1504`  
  raw_extraction contains TWO chains with id 'shipbuilding' ('Shipbuilding & Boatwright' resource Managed woodland, and 'Shipbuilding and Timber' resource Coastal Timber). 'Fishmonger' is also listed twice inside the fishing processors array.  
  _Fix:_ Rename the coastal chain id (e.g. 'coastal_shipbuilding'), merge fish/fishing into one chain (keep river_fishing as the substitute variant), and add a uniqueness assert on (needKey, id).
- **[medium] Custom/discovered chains carry no needKey and a hardcoded 'vulnerable' status** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/inferSupplyChains.js:215-240; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:49-97`  
  inferSupplyChains emits chains with needLabel 'Custom' but NO needKey, so canonical ids become 'chain.unknown.*' and every need-keyed consumer (heuristics, food/trade filters, downstream traces) treats them as uncategorized. Status is hardcoded 'vulnerable' — reasonable for unconfirmed discoveries, but confirmed chains persisted via generateEconomy keep status (default 'running') in a display-only economicState.customChains that is deliberately never merged into activeChains. Net effect: a DM's confirmed custom supply chain can never strain food security, trade connectivity, defense, or escalation clocks — custom content is excluded from the causal loop entirely, while its exports/imports DO enter the real trade lists (asymmetric integration).  
  _Fix:_ Let the user pick a need category at confirm time (default by output type), store it as needKey, and merge confirmed chains into activeChains behind their verification state so they participate in capacity/causal reads.
- **[medium] Chain 'services' tags are produced everywhere and consumed nowhere** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js (services fields); C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:177; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:173-187,346`  
  Every catalog chain declares services tags (food, equipment, transport, employment, legal, information, magic, healing, criminal, entertainment, lodging, security, trade, crafts, construction, fuel, military, textiles). They are copied through computeActiveChains and deriveSupplyChainState, but the ONLY consumer is the regional-condition text haystack (searchableChainText). They never feed availableServices, the services generator, or any capacity lens — and the tag vocabulary is itself ad-hoc (crafts/construction/fuel/textiles/military/security appear once or twice; servicesGenerator uses a different type-key set). A DM would expect 'this chain is why the leatherworker service exists' linkage; instead services and chains are derived independently from institutions.  
  _Fix:_ Either normalize the tags to the availableServices type keys and use them to annotate/justify services (chain -> service receipts), or delete the field.
- **[medium] settlement.supplyChainState.failures is read but never written** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/summary/tonightAtTheTable.js:95; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/components/map/RoutesToolbar.jsx:73`  
  tonightAtTheTable (the session-prep summary) and the map RoutesToolbar both read settlement.supplyChainState?.failures, but no code anywhere writes a supplyChainState object onto the settlement — the canonical derivation lives in deriveAllSupplyChainStates and is never persisted under that name. The failures array is therefore always empty: supply-chain failure beats never appear in 'tonight at the table' and route-failure badges never render, even when chains are scarce/collapsing. This is a producer that simply doesn't exist for two real consumers.  
  _Fix:_ Derive failures on the fly from deriveAllSupplyChainStates(settlement).filter(c => ['scarce','blocked','collapsing'].includes(c.status)) in both consumers, or actually persist a supplyChainState envelope at assembly.
- **[low] Dead config in the chain module: _INCOME_TO_CHAINS, _hasInst, 'clay_pits', unreachable 'high' severity branch** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:36-55,207-209; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2141,2197-2207`  
  computeActiveChains defines _INCOME_TO_CHAINS (income label -> chain ids 'for linkage display') and a _hasInst helper; neither is referenced anywhere — the EconomicsTab does its own income->chain matching by keyword. Half of _INCOME_TO_CHAINS points at the permanently-dead chains from the empty-processor bug ('Entrepôt Trade' -> spices_dyes/silk; 'Banking Fees' -> transit_finance). economicGenerator's DEPLETED_IMPORT_MAP includes key 'clay_pits', which is not a RESOURCE_DATA key (the real key is river_clay), so clay depletion never generates its import line.
