- **[medium] Salt pans, foraging, and other resources that should back chains but cannot** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:69-98,1556-1561; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/resourceData.js:362-373`  
  desert_salt ('Salt Pans', explicitly 'major trade commodity') cannot activate food_security.salt: the chain's resource is hard-wired to 'Salt flats' with no resourceSubstitutes, and RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS maps desert_salt only to dead ids — so a desert salt town has salt exports via tradeGoods but no salt chain, no preservation linkage, no chain receipts. food_security.forage's only processor is 'Elder Grove Council' (a druidic institution), so ordinary villages near foraging areas have no forage chain — foraging realistically needs no institution at all. oasis_water maps to raw_extraction.clay (clay from an oasis) instead of the oasis_agriculture chain. These are resources a DM placed deliberately that produce no visible chain consequence.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'Salt Pans' as a resourceSubstitute on the salt chain (or map desert_salt -> food_security.salt), give forage common processors (Weekly market, Village commons) or make it institution-free at low tiers, and point oasis_water at oasis_agriculture.
- **[low] Fuzzy institution matching lets the wrong institutions run chains** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:13-23,114-117,150-162`  
  Processor matching truncates each pattern to 12 chars and substring-matches: 'Mill' becomes 'mill', which matches ANY institution containing the substring — a Sawmill (and formerly 'Access to external mill', special-cased with a comment admitting the bug) activates the Grain & Bread chain with no grain mill present. resourceLabelToKey's word-overlap match is order-dependent: labels with no exact key ('Mountain Pass', 'Clay deposits') resolve to whichever RESOURCE_DATA key happens to score first in object-key order (defended_pass, river_clay today) — correct only by luck and silently re-mappable by reordering the data file.  
  _Fix:_ Match processors on word boundaries (or exact catalog names), and give every chain.resource an explicit resourceKey field instead of fuzzy label resolution; assert resolution uniqueness in a test.
- **[low] Locally-produced entrepôt goods exported with a '(transit)' label on non-hub routes** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:514-517`  
  deriveExportsFromChains adds '<output> (transit)' for every active chain with entrepot:true regardless of route. Chains that are entrepot-flagged but resource-backed (salt, furs_north, camel_caravan, crossroads_trade) can activate via their LOCAL resource on a plain road route, where nothing is actually transiting — the goods are locally produced, yet get the transit annotation. The dedupe pass hides it whenever the bare label was already exported, so the bug surfaces only for outputs unique to the entrepôt slice, which makes it look intermittent to a DM comparing settlements.  
  _Fix:_ Only emit the transit label when the chain ran as pass-through (isEntrepotOnly or entrepot-without-local-resource on a hub route); resource-backed activations should export their outputs unannotated.
- **[low] Divine tradition gate is a redundant double-check that excludes parish-church-only settlements** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:68-75; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:60,165`  
  The divine magic tradition (which unlocks chain magic substitution — temple granaries filling food gaps) requires hasTradition over two nearly identical institution lists ANDed together; the comment admits the second was meant to proxy a religionInfluence check that isn't threaded here. The first list includes 'parish church', the second doesn't — so a village whose only religious institution is a Parish church (the most common case) gets NO divine substitution unless it also rolled a 'Priest (resident)'. Meanwhile foodGenerator's own divine magicOffset uses a different gate (hasDivine institutions + priorityReligion >= 55), so the two magic-food models can disagree about whether the temple helps.  
  _Fix:_ Collapse to one list including 'parish church', and thread the same religion-priority signal both magic-food paths use so chain substitution and the food ledger agree.
- **[low] Horse & Animal Trade classified as food security** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:163-175; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/causalState.js:168; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/hookEscalation.js:418`  
  food_security.animal_husbandry outputs cavalry mounts, draft horses, hunting dogs, and trained falcons with services ['transport','employment'] — but because its needKey is food_security, a stable horse-trading chain adds +8 to causalState foodSecurity and +6 to capacityModel food supply, and a disrupted one triggers the bread_riot escalation clock. A horse market going under should pressure transport/military, not bread prices. Its processors are also only merchant guilds — no Stable master/Horse market, which ARE processors of the separate livestock chain instead.  
  _Fix:_ Move animal_husbandry under a transport/trade need (or exclude non-caloric chains from food scoring by id), and swap its processors with the stable/horse-market institutions.
- **[medium] Magic boosts only rescue failing chains — healthy chains get no magical amplification, and magicRecovery is display-only** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:24-109; C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:96-167`  
  The owner frames magic as a supply-chain SUPPLEMENT and BOOSTER. The substitution pass only fires when a chain is already 'impaired' or resourceDepleted — a high-magic settlement with a druid circle gets zero chain-level benefit while its chains are healthy (no extra exportable surplus, no status upgrade, no output annotation). The numeric magicRecovery (0.2-0.7) is consumed ONLY by the EconomicsTab badge; capacityModel, causalState, food ledger, and exports all ignore the magnitude, so 25% and 70% recovery are mechanically identical. foodGenerator has a parallel magicOffset that does scale, but it never reads the chain pass — the two magic-food systems are independent computations that happen to use similar rates.  
  _Fix:_ Add a positive path (high magicPriority + tradition boosts healthy chain output/exportability with a magicBoost note), and feed magicRecovery into the food ledger's magicOffset so the chain story and the caloric math agree.
- **[low] Regional pressure inference matches chains by 4-character token overlap** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:189-224`  
  conditionMatchesChain falls back to splitting the chain's searchable text into tokens of length >= 4 and testing substring inclusion against the condition's label/description/causes text. Tokens like 'food', 'security', 'trade', 'goods', 'services' appear in many condition descriptions, so a regional_conflict_pressure condition whose prose mentions 'trade' can escalate unrelated chains; conversely needKey-based matching (the precise path) only works when the condition's affectedSystems uses chain needKeys, which regional archetypes only sometimes do. The status escalation that follows (strained/scarce/collapsing) then feeds capacityModel and causal scores, so fuzzy text overlap quietly becomes mechanical pressure.  
  _Fix:_ Require archetype->needKey mapping (regional_import_shortage -> trade_entrepot/food_security, etc.) and drop the free-text token fallback, or raise the token floor and require 2+ token hits.

Strengths: Single canonical read path on the domain side: capacityModel, causalState, dailyLife, hookEscalation, deriveRegionalState, explanation, and counterfactual all consume chains through deriveAllSupplyChainStates rather than poking raw generator output — the conserved-ledger discipline genuinely holds for chains (capacityModel.js:53,392; causalState.js:167).; The deliberate orthogonality between the frozen food ledger (generation-time deficitPct) and live chain status (post-generation regional pressure) is explicitly documented with a do-not-fold-away comment (capacityModel.js:386-391) — honest receipts about why two food lenses coexist.; Regional pressure escalation (supplyChainState.js:226-246) is a clean, monotonic, damped ladder: already-bad states need TWO severe pressures to worsen, substituted chains resist longer, and the failureConsequences string names the pressing conditions — exactly the why-receipt a DM wants.; Magic-as-supplement is mechanically real, not flavor: teleportation infrastructure downgrades trade-dependency severity with bespoke impact text (economicGenerator.js:2126-2148), magically sustained chains lose exportability (no free lunch), recovery rates are tradition-ranked (druid > divine > arcane) and roughly agree with foodGenerator's independent magicOffset rates, and arcane chains are fully suppressed at magic=0 (computeActiveChains.js:106-111).; Chain activation logic encodes defensible economic reasoning: tier gates, extraction gates (no iron exports without a mine), output gates (no leather exports without a tannery), depletion semantics (runs locally, nothing to export), the feudal external-mill banalité special case with narrative note, and subsistence isolation clearing trade — all legible, gameable consequences.; Upstream cascade closes the loop end to end: missing upstream chains downgrade status AND generate the matching import label (UPSTREAM_IMPORT_LABELS covers every catalog upstream id), and defenseGenerator reads garrison/fortification/mercenary/food_processing chains into military/economic scores — chains actually feed defense, food, trade, escalation clocks, and per-chain generation traces (generateEconomy.js:193-273).

### subsumption

The subsumption layer is three overlapping name-string dedup systems (UPGRADE_CHAINS exact-match at assemble, SUBSUMPTION_RULES substring-match at step 6, custom subsumes) plus a cascade pass that is currently 100% dead code because it reads `data.p` from a catalog that only defines `baseChance`. Subsumption itself keys on raw substring inclusion with no protection for required/forced/custom institutions and no transfer of the absorbed institution's services, goods gates, or chain roles — chains survive upgrades only where supplyChainData happens to list the greater, and several rules are outright destructive: five self-delete their own greater (courts, brewing, minting vanish), one deletes a city's required parish churches, and a cluster runs backwards by letting consumers (smelter, merchant guilds, butchers, harbour master) absorb their upstream producers, killing the salt, fuel, wool, and wine chains. Faction-pulled institutions are added after the economy is derived, bypassing both subsumption and all chain/service mappings. The receipts/trace architecture and pipeline ordering are strong; the fixes are mostly vocabulary hygiene, one schema rename, protection flags, and an alias rule so greaters inherit their lessers' mappings.

- **[high] Entire supply-chain cascade pass is dead code (schema drift: data.p vs baseChance)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/cascadeGenerator.js:110-116; src/generators/steps/cascadePass.js:30-31; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js (baseChance schema)`  
  cascadeGenerator.js reads `const baseChance = data.p || 0` but institutionalCatalog.js has 296 `baseChance:` fields and ZERO `p:` fields. So cascadeChance is always 0, `_rng() < 0` never passes, and applyCascadeInstitutions always returns []. cascadePass.js then gates EVERYTHING on `if (cascadeAdditions.length > 0)` — so the airship maritime override (lines 58-88) and the post-cascade re-subsumption (93-118) are also unreachable. The owner's named 'cascade logic' (chain-adjacent institutions pulled in by demand, e.g. smelter pulls charcoal burner) never fires once, no cascade traces are ever emitted, and CASCADE_CAPS/boost tuning is all dead tuning.  
  _Fix:_ Read `data.baseChance` (or normalize the catalog to one field). Move the airship override and re-subsumption OUT of the `cascadeAdditions.length > 0` guard. Add a smoke test asserting cascade adds >0 institutions for a seeded city with a smelting/textile roster.
- **[high] Five subsumption rules delete their own greater (substring self-match)** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:81-92 (rules at 28,37,39,40,41)`  
  applySubsumption matches lessers by `inst.name.includes(lesser)` over ALL institutions, including the greater itself. Wherever the greater's name contains the lesser string, the rule self-destructs: 'multiple courthouses'⊃'courthouse' (rule line 28), 'brewery'⊃'brewer' (37), "cobbler's guild"⊃'cobbler' (39), "tailor's guild"⊃'tailor' (40), 'mint (official)'⊃'mint' (41). A city that rolls Multiple courthouses ends with NO court: Legal services income (computeActiveChains.js:664) and the requiredInstitution:'Multiple courthouses' good (servicesGenerator.js:651) silently vanish. Mint (official) deletes itself + Mint + Assay office, killing every 'mint'-keyed coin gate (computeActiveChains.js:362,421). The emitted trace even names an absorber that no longer exists in the dossier.  
  _Fix:_ Skip the greater's own index when removing lessers (compare resolved greater indices, or require lesser-match AND not greater-match on the same institution). Add a rule-table lint: no greater string may contain one of its lesser strings.
- **[high] Subsumption ignores required:true — cathedral deletes a city's required parish churches** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:25,84-91 vs src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:399-414; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:1687`  
  UPGRADE_CHAINS dedup (assembleInstitutions.js:399-404) and custom subsumption (409-414) both protect source==='required'; SUBSUMPTION_RULES protects nothing — required, forced, and custom institutions are all spliceable. Concrete: the 'cathedral' rule's lesser 'parish church' substring-matches every variant, including 'Parish churches (10-30)' which is required:true at city tier (institutionalCatalog.js:1687). Any city that rolls 'Cathedral (10,000+ only)' (baseChance 0.3) loses ALL its parish churches — violating the catalog's own required contract and medieval realism (cathedrals coexist with parishes; the catalog clearly intends both at city tier). Same hole lets a user-forced or required institution be silently deleted by any rule.  
  _Fix:_ Skip institutions with source 'required'/'forced'/'custom' in applySubsumption (mirroring UPGRADE_CHAINS), and narrow the cathedral rule's lessers to singular 'parish church'/'wayside shrine', not the (N-M) city variants.
- **[high] Backwards subsumption: downstream consumers absorb their upstream producers, killing chains** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:42,49,61,64-68; src/data/supplyChainData.js:75,241,584,733`  
  Several rules remove a producer because its CUSTOMER exists — the opposite of supply-chain logic: smelter subsumes charcoal burner + mine (open cast) (rules 42,61) — cascadePass.js:36 even documents the intended opposite ('you got a smelter, so you also got a charcoal burner'); the fuel chain (supplyChainData.js:241) loses its processor. 'merchant guilds (3-8)' subsumes salt works (66) — Salt works is the SOLE processor of the salt chain (75), so every settlement with merchant guilds loses salt preservation. Merchant guilds/brewery subsume vintner (67-68), threatening wine_spirits (733). Butchers subsume dairy farmer + shepherd (64) — with the tailor's-guild self-destruct this kills the wool chain (584). Craft guilds subsume dairy farmer (65). Harbour master's office subsumes the actual docks (49). The greater provides none of the removed production; the chain just dies.  
  _Fix:_ Delete the producer-absorbing rules (smelter→charcoal/mine, merchant guilds→salt works/vintner, butchers→dairy/shepherd, craft guilds→dairy, harbour master→docks, brewery→vintner). Subsumption should only collapse same-function scale ladders; cross-function adjacency belongs to the cascade (which should ADD, not remove).
- **[high] Subsumed institutions transfer nothing — chains/goods survive only by accident of processor lists, and gate vocabulary misses the greater** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:116; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:359-444,657-706; src/data/supplyChainData.js:963`  
  Removal is a plain splice; no logic says 'the greater now provides the lesser's services/chain roles'. Most chains survive only because supplyChainData happens to list greater AND lesser. Where it doesn't, upgrades silently destroy output: 'Tanner (established)' subsumes 'Tannery' (rule 38) but every leather gate keys on 'tannery' (computeActiveChains.js:359,409-413) — so having the BIGGER tanner kills 'Leather goods/armour/Boots/Saddles' exports. Jeweller subsumed by luxury goods quarter/specialized metalworkers (62-63), but the 'jewel' gates (362-363,422-423) match neither — city+ settlements can never export jewellery or cut gemstones. Harbour master (after absorbing docks) matches no pattern in the port service map (computeActiveChains.js:691: 'docks/port','major port','navy') — Port Revenue lost. Wizard's tower→Mages' guild (20) kills the research chain (supplyChainData.js:963) whose only procs are tower + sage's quarter.  
  _Fix:_ Either (a) make gates/patterns include every greater that subsumes a gated lesser (add 'tanner','jewel'-bearing greaters, 'harbour' to port patterns, Mages' guild to research chain), or (b) make subsumption record an alias so name-matching consumers treat the greater as also matching the absorbed lesser's vocabulary.
- **[high] Faction-pulled institutions bypass subsumption AND the entire economy** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/factionCorrelationPass.js:50-83; src/generators/steps/index.js:16-19; src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:104-170`  
  factionCorrelationPass (step 12) pushes institutions AFTER generateEconomy (step 9) has already derived activeChains, exports, imports, services, and spatial layout (economicGenerator.js:2160-2190). Pipeline order: assemble→subsume→cascade→isolate→ECONOMY→power→factions. So a faction-pulled 'Thieves' guild chapter' or Defense institution appears in the dossier but contributes zero to chains/goods/services/ledgers. Dedup is exact-name only (factionCorrelation.js:104-130), so it can add a lesser beside its greater ('Thieves' guild chapter' + 'Thieves' guild (powerful)') — exactly what subsumption forbids — and additions carry no tags (160-168), so tag-based consumers (arcane strip, downstream-effect inference) can't classify them. Also stripArcaneInstitutions runs here, AFTER economy: in a no-magic edge case an arcane institution can shape the economy at step 9 then vanish at step 12, leaving income with no backing institution.  
  _Fix:_ Move faction boosts before generateEconomy (deps allow it: it only needs powerStructure — split economy into pre/post if needed), or re-run a light subsumption + chain refresh after additions. Copy tags/desc from the catalog def when pushing.
- **[medium] Six dead subsumption rules from vocabulary that exists nowhere in the catalog** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:21,23,29,30,50,60; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:728; src/generators/structuralValidator.js:106,110`  
  Greaters that can never appear: 'major port' (rule 29) — no catalog name contains it (also dead in the port service patterns and structuralValidator.js:110); 'university' (30) — no University anywhere, which also makes servicesGenerator.js:728 (requiredInstitution:'University') a permanently dead good and structuralValidator.js:106 a dead prereq; 'mages district' (21) never matches catalog "Mages' district" — apostrophe mismatch. Dead lessers: 'pit fights' (50) vs catalog 'Fighting pits'; "adventurers' guild chapter" (23) — not in catalog; 'stone quarry (hamlet)' (60) — both quarry entries are plain 'Stone quarry'. These rules silently do nothing, so the upgrade stories they encode (university absorbs the academy, gladiator school absorbs pit fighting) never happen.  
  _Fix:_ Fix the three typo-class entries ('mages' district', 'Fighting pits', drop the (hamlet) variant), and either add University/Major port to the catalog or delete every reference. Add a startup assertion that every rule string substring-matches at least one catalog name.
- **[medium] Three parallel dedup systems with different keys, protections, and transitivity** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:135-160,398-414; src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:74-117; src/generators/steps/cascadePass.js:93-118`  
  Institution collapse happens in three places with three contracts: (1) UPGRADE_CHAINS — exact name, protects required (assembleInstitutions.js:135-160,398-404); (2) SUBSUMPTION_RULES — substring, protects nothing (subsumptionPass.js); (3) customDeps.subsumedBy — exact, protects required (assembleInstitutions.js:409-414). Pairs are duplicated across systems with different semantics: Wizard's tower→Mages' guild is in both (1) and (2); Courthouse→Multiple courthouses is exact-deduped at assemble, then the greater self-destructs at subsumption; craft/merchant guild ladders appear in both. The cascadePass re-subsumption recomputes `names` per rule (cascadePass.js:94) while subsumptionPass snapshots once (75), giving different transitive behavior if the cascade is ever revived. A DM reading traces can't predict which system removed what.  
  _Fix:_ Collapse to one subsumption table with one matcher and one protection policy (skip required/forced/custom), applied at assemble AND re-applied after any later institution addition.
- **[medium] Subsistence mode strips militia and palisade but preserves bandits** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:99-121; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:310-324`  
  applySubsistenceMode's keep-list fallback (isolationGenerator.js:114-116) treats any institution whose tags aren't in keepTags as trade and removes it. keepTags omits 'defense'/'military'/'fortification' but INCLUDES 'criminal'. Catalog tags: Citizen militia ['defense','military'], Palisade or earthworks ['defense','fortification'] (institutionalCatalog.js:310-324) — both stripped from isolated thorps/hamlets — while Bandit affiliate, Fence, and Smuggling waypoint (tags ['criminal']) all survive. So the most exposed settlements in the world lose their only defenses and keep their criminal ties. A DM expects the inverse: isolation increases defense salience.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'defense','military','fortification' to keepTags (and consider whether 'criminal' really belongs there, or is intentional flavor — if intentional, document it).
- **[medium] Cascade additions drop catalog metadata (tags/desc/source), breaking downstream classification** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/cascadeGenerator.js:116-118; src/generators/steps/cascadePass.js:52-54`  
  applyCascadeInstitutions pushes {name, category, tier, cascadeAdded, cascadeBoost} even though the catalog `data` in scope has desc/tags/priorityCategory (cascadeGenerator.js:117). cascadePass.js:52-54 then reads add.tags for downstream-effect traces — always undefined, so cascade traces never carry effects. If the dead-cascade bug (finding 1) is fixed, untagged additions misbehave everywhere tags are read: subsistence-strip's fallback treats untagged institutions as trade and deletes them (isolationGenerator.js:116), arcane strip can't tag-match them, and tagsToDownstream yields nothing. They also lack `source`, the field every other creation path sets.  
  _Fix:_ Spread the catalog def into the pushed object: { name, category, tier, ...data fields (desc, tags, priorityCategory), source: 'cascade', cascadeAdded: true, cascadeBoost }.
- **[medium] Seven chains have empty processingInstitutions and can never activate — including the flagship magical_goods chain** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:534,651,667,684,1052,1074,1213; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117`  
  computeActiveChains requires ≥1 matched processor (computeActiveChains.js:114-117), but these chains declare processingInstitutions: [] — luxury_goods (supplyChainData.js:534), spices_dyes (651), silk_luxury_textiles (667), transit_finance (684), magical_goods (1052), planar (1074), smuggling (1213). They are orphans: produced in config, never consumable. Yet _INCOME_TO_CHAINS (computeActiveChains.js:36-47) links 'Entrepôt Trade' and 'Banking Fees' incomes to them, and magical_goods ('Magical Items & Enchanting' — weapon enchantment, warding) is exactly the owner's 'magic as supply-chain booster' — while Enchanter's shop, Mages' guild, and Academy of magic sit in the catalog backing nothing. The entrepot:true flag shows they were meant to run on logistics/arcane institutions.  
  _Fix:_ Give each a processor list (magical_goods: Enchanter's shop, Mages' guild/district, Academy of magic; transit_finance: Banking houses/district, Money changers; smuggling: fences/smuggling network; entrepôt goods: warehouse district, docks, caravan exchange) or add an entrepot-only activation path that doesn't require processors.
- **[medium] Catalog schema drift (baseChance vs p/on) silently breaks two more consumers beyond the cascade** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:147,154; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:947-965,1151-1168; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:540-560`  
  Same root cause as finding 1 in two more places: factionCorrelation.js:147,154 reads `def.p || 0.5` — every faction signature institution rolls a flat 0.5 base regardless of actual rarity, and the 'sort by baseChance descending' comment is a no-op (all values identical), so candidates are tried in catalog insertion order. getHistoryModifiers and getGoodsModifiers (economicGenerator.js:947-965,1151-1168) read `h.on` and `h.p` while SERVICE_TIER_DATA entries use `defaultEnabled`/`baseChance` (servicesGenerator.js:540-560) — so those export paths only function via user toggles, never by default. Three independent subsystems mis-reading one schema is a single canonical-field fix.  
  _Fix:_ Pick one probability field name (baseChance) and one enabled field (defaultEnabled), normalize the catalog + SERVICE_TIER_DATA, and grep-ban the legacy names.
- **[medium] User custom institutions can be silently deleted by substring subsumption** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:84-91; src/generators/steps/assembleInstitutions.js:376-414`  
  Custom institutions enter at assembleInstitutions.js:383 with source:'custom', then subsumptionPass's substring matcher (subsumptionPass.js:86) deletes any whose NAME merely contains a lesser string — a custom 'Mint Street Counting House' ('mint'), 'Tailor's Row' ('tailor'), 'Old Waystation Shrine' ('waystation'), 'Shepherd's Rest Inn' ('shepherd') — whenever the corresponding greater exists. There is no isCustom/source guard, so user-authored canon vanishes with only a subsumed trace. This directly violates the 'durable to custom content' product goal. The inverse hole: custom `subsumes` declarations run only at assemble time (409-414), so they never apply to faction-boost additions made at step 12.  
  _Fix:_ Skip source==='custom' (and 'forced'/'required') in applySubsumption; if a DM wants a custom institution absorbable, let the custom schema opt in explicitly.
- **[low] Four different fuzzy name-matchers over the same vocabulary, with collisions** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:115; src/generators/cascadeGenerator.js:15; src/data/supplyChainData.js:1016`  
  The whole institution mapping layer keys on free-text names with four matchers: exact (UPGRADE_CHAINS, custom subsume, faction dedup), full substring (SUBSUMPTION_RULES, service maps, export gates), slice(0,12) prefix (chain processors, computeActiveChains.js:115), and slice(0,16) prefix (cascade map, cascadeGenerator.js:15) — where 'Merchant guilds (3-8)'/'(15-40)'/'(50-100+)' all collide to one node. Concrete casualty: the alchemy chain lists 'Wizard Tower' (supplyChainData.js:1016) which never matches catalog "Wizard's tower" under any matcher. instId() canonicalization exists but only for traces. Nearly every bug in this audit is downstream of name-string matching.  
  _Fix:_ Adopt instId()-style canonical ids as the join key across catalog, chains, rules, and gates; keep display names separate. Short-term: fix 'Wizard Tower' and add a CI check that every chain processor resolves to ≥1 catalog name.
- **[medium] Airship maritime override is mis-gated even apart from the dead cascade** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/cascadePass.js:31,58-118; src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:49`  
  The airship→docks/harbour-master override sits inside `if (cascadeAdditions.length > 0)` (cascadePass.js:31-88), but airship docking comes from main generation or isolation forcing — unrelated to whether the cascade added anything. Even with finding 1 fixed, an airship city whose cascade added nothing gets no aerial port infrastructure. Worse, the very next block re-runs subsumption (93-118), and rule 49 (harbour master subsumes docks) immediately deletes the Docks/port facilities the override just added — so the override can at best yield a harbour master's office with no docks, which then matches no port service pattern (finding 5). Three layers of logic fighting each other.  
  _Fix:_ Hoist the airship override out of the cascade-additions guard; drop the harbour-master-subsumes-docks rule (they are complementary, not a ladder).
- **[medium] Arcane upgrades silently weaken magic-as-booster: academy/guild not wired into the chains the lesser fed** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1030; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:679,699-701; src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:20-22`  
  Subsumption upgrades arcane institutions (academy of magic absorbs wizard's tower + mages' guild, rule 22; mages' guild absorbs wizard's tower + alchemist shop, rule 20), but the consumers don't know the greaters: the spellcasting chain's processors are Wizard's tower / Mages' guild / Mages' district / Hedge wizard — NOT Academy of magic (supplyChainData.js:1030), so an academy metropolis can lose its spellcasting chain while keeping Arcane Services income (computeActiveChains.js:679) — incoherent dossier. Mages' guild absorbing the alchemist shop drops the Alchemical Trade service patterns ('alchemist quarter','alchemist shop' only, computeActiveChains.js:699-701) when no quarter exists. Net effect: the MORE magical a settlement becomes via upgrades, the fewer magic chains/services it shows — the exact opposite of magic as supply-chain supplement.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'Academy of magic' (and Mages' district) to the spellcasting chain processors, and add mages' guild/academy to the alchemy service patterns — or implement the alias mechanism from finding 5.
- **[low] Isolation magic floor ignores the magic dial between 1 and 79** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:17-54; src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:68,100`  
  applyTeleportationInfrastructure forces a permanent teleportation circle + resident arcane maintainer for ANY isolated town+ (isolationGenerator.js:17-54). Only magicExists===false or priorityMagic exactly 0 escapes (coerced to 'road' at resolveConfig.js:100). So a world dialed to priorityMagic=1 still guarantees every isolated town a working teleport circle — the dial's only effect is circle vs airship at ≥80 (line 24). For a low-magic campaign this is a realism break a DM will notice immediately: the rarest magic in the world is routine municipal infrastructure. The design comment ('ANY isolated town+ MUST have magical trade infrastructure') is coherent at default magic but should degrade at low magic.  
  _Fix:_ Below a threshold (e.g. priorityMagic < 20), coerce isolated→road the same way noMagic does, or substitute a mundane lifeline (seasonal caravan, river barge) with the same trace receipt.

Strengths: Honest receipts are real: every subsumption removal records WHICH greater absorbed which lesser (subsumptionPass.js:77-114), and isolation/faction/strip passes all emit per-institution traces with causes and downstream effects — exactly the product thesis.; Pipeline ordering is mostly right and legible: explicit deps/provides (steps/index.js) put subsume→cascade→isolate BEFORE economy/power, so chains, ledgers, and the dossier read one post-dedup roster (the faction pass is the lone violation).; Chain data shows the correct instinct for subsumption survival: most processor lists include both lesser and greater (spellcasting 1030, maritime 339, leather 599, criminal 1229), so the common upgrade paths keep their chains running.; The isolation story is genuinely coherent magic-as-trade-supplement: forced circle + named maintainer + _magicTradeOnly flag threads into imports (deriveImportsFromChains hasMagicTrade), demand imports (factionCorrelationPass.js:32-47), and dependency notes — and no-magic worlds correctly coerce isolated→road (resolveConfig.js:100).; Custom content gets a first-class subsumption hook (customDeps.subsumedBy) with required-institution protection and deterministic iteration order for seed stability (assembleInstitutions.js:373-414).; Anti-inflation tuning is deliberate: tier-scaled cascade caps, faction boost caps of 0 below town, and the 0.45 cascade chance ceiling all show conscious restraint so derived institutions supplement rather than dominate.; Subsistence and arcane strips protect required/forced institutions (isolationGenerator.js:109,135), so the safety nets cannot delete the settlement's mandatory skeleton.

### economy-power-institutions

The economy↔power↔institution core is structurally sound: a coherent five-domain instFlags model feeds faction powers, all 15 stressors have bespoke faction consequences, legitimacy is a conserved ledger, and the power→economy feedback (faction-pulled institutions, faction demand imports) is real and traced. The big problems are broken connective tissue rather than bad design: three load-bearing field-name mismatches mean the neighbour relationship never modulates instFlags or power narratives (config.neighborRelationship never exists; tradeRoute hardwired null), the governing faction never inherits public legitimacy in profiles/traces (governingName never set), and neighbour prosperity never affects anything (prosperityLevel vs prosperity). Several vocabulary gaps cause silent drops: governing factions that name-match domain keywords lose their authored relationships, 'Bloc'/'Underground' keyword inference miscategorizes stress factions (a persecuted congregation can become THE criminal faction), 'Thriving' and 'Lightly Defended' are checked-but-never-produced / produced-but-never-mapped, and noble factions are orphaned from both correlation loops. Five stress archetypes are computed and consumed nowhere, the income multiplier cancels itself, the assembly-time legitimacy patch desyncs from faction powers, and five shipped narrative strings contain 'SEVERITY' where 'it' should be. Each fix is small; together they would close most of the gap between what the system computes and what the DM is shown.

- **[high] Neighbour relationship multipliers in getInstFlags can never fire** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:349-355,372-377; src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:58`  
  getInstFlags reads config.neighborRelationship?.relationshipType to apply neighborMilMult (hostile +20% military) and neighborEconMult (hostile -12% economy). But no config object anywhere ever carries neighborRelationship — it is only assembled onto the final settlement object (assembleSettlement.js:58), never onto effectiveConfig or the saved config. So both multipliers are permanently 1.0 in every generation and every later UI call. The neighbour DOES shape institutions (institutionProbability) and exports (_neighbourEconBias), but the documented neighbour→military-readiness and neighbour→economy-output couplings are dead. A DM creating a settlement with a 'hostile rival' neighbour gets zero effect on militaryEffective/economyOutput, hence zero effect on Military/Guard faction power.  
  _Fix:_ In resolveNeighbour/resolveConfig, copy the resolved relationshipType onto effectiveConfig.neighborRelationship (and into the saved config) so getInstFlags sees it; add a regression test that a hostile neighbour raises militaryEffective.
- **[high] powerStructure.governingName never set — governing faction never inherits legitimacy in profiles/traces** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/factionProfile.js:176-195; src/generators/steps/generatePower.js:44-52`  
  generatePowerStructure returns {factions, stability, recentConflict, publicLegitimacy, factionRelationships, criminalCaptureState}; governing status lives only on faction.isGoverning. But factionProfile.legitimacyFor checks power.governingName / power.governingFactionName (factionProfile.js:181-184) — both nonexistent — so deriveFactionProfile gives EVERY faction legitimacy 50, and the documented 'governing faction inherits public legitimacy via governanceLedger' path never executes. Likewise generatePower.js:44-52 reads powerStructure?.governingName, so isGoverning is always false: the trace never emits result:'governing' nor the 'inherits public legitimacy' cause. Power→legitimacy mapping is authored on both ends but the connecting field name doesn't exist.  
  _Fix:_ Check faction.isGoverning in legitimacyFor and in generatePower's trace; or have generatePowerStructure set powerStructure.governingName from the isGoverning faction.
- **[high] Neighbour prosperity read via wrong field — economicStrength always 0.5** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/neighbourGenerator.js:107-111; src/generators/institutionProbability.js:227-230`  
  extractNeighbourProfile computes economicStrength from PROSPERITY_RANK[econ.prosperityLevel] (neighbourGenerator.js:111), but economicState carries `prosperity`, never `prosperityLevel` (no producer exists anywhere). So every neighbour has economicStrength 0.5 regardless of wealth, and the neighbour-market multiplier in institution probability (institutionProbability.js:229, 0.8+strength*0.4) is always exactly 1.0. Additionally the rank table itself is wrong for the generator's vocabulary: it puts 'Struggling' (0.3) above 'Poor' (0.2) though Struggling is the worse label, and includes 'Modest'/'Affluent' which are never produced.  
  _Fix:_ Read econ.prosperity; fix rank order (Struggling ≤ Poor); drop or map the unproduced labels.
- **[medium] generatePowerStructure tradeRoute param hardwired null — external-threat stability/conflict paths unreachable** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generatePower.js:30-34; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:1819-1824,1959-1960`  
  The only caller passes null as tradeRoute (generatePower.js:30-34). Inside generatePowerStructure, the stability branch for hostile/cold-war/tense neighbours ('Tense (external threat)', powerGenerator.js:1819-1824) and the recent-conflict line `Ongoing tensions with ${tradeRoute.neighborName}` (powerGenerator.js:1959-1960) therefore never execute. Combined with the dead neighborRelationship multipliers, a hostile neighbour leaves no trace at all in the power structure — no stability shift, no conflict line — which a DM configuring a rival neighbour would reasonably expect.  
  _Fix:_ Pass the resolved neighbourProfile (or its relationshipType + name) as the third argument, or delete the dead branches.
- **[medium] computeFactionRelationships drops relationships when the governing faction name matches domain keywords** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionDynamics.js:191-216,222-301,394-409`  
  merc/crim use findNonGov, but mil/rel/noble/craft use plain find() which also matches the governing faction's name/category (factionDynamics.js:191-216). When governance is 'Military Council', find('military') returns the governing faction itself, the self-pair guard skips it, and the gov↔Military/Guard relationship vanishes — even though powerGenerator explicitly creates a separate Military/Guard faction described as 'operationally distinct from the command council' (powerGenerator.js:1074-1078). Same for 'Church Council'/'Ecclesiastical Council' (the authored govIsTheocratic narrative at factionDynamics.js:282-285 is unreachable in its primary case) and 'Noble Governorship' vs Noble Houses. The most flavourful governments lose exactly the relationships that define them.  
  _Fix:_ Use findNonGov for mil/rel/noble/craft lookups (the govIsTheocratic special case should then compare gov name against the religious faction found among non-gov factions).
- **[medium] inferFactionCategory keyword-order misclassifies stress factions (Bloc→economy, Underground Old Faith→criminal, Occupation/Resistance→military)** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:481-595,2150-2153; src/generators/factionDynamics.js:149-172,435-460`  
  Categories are assigned by first keyword hit in fixed order (powerGenerator.js:481-595). 'Bloc' is an economy keyword, so 'Loyalist/Reform Noble Bloc', 'Claimant Bloc A/B' and 'Third Bloc (Neutrals)' become economy factions (eligible for merchant demand imports and Economy/Crafts institution boosts). 'Underground' is a criminal keyword, so the persecuted 'Underground Old Faith' congregation is categorized criminal — it receives the crime legitimacy multiplier (factionDynamics.js:438,453) and can be selected as THE criminal faction by computeCriminalCaptureState (factionDynamics.js:150) when no thieves guild exists, producing 'corrupted/capture' narratives about a hidden congregation. 'Occupation'/'Resistance' map to military, so under occupation find('military') can pair the governing council with the Occupation Authority as its 'executive arm'.  
  _Fix:_ Tag stress-injected factions with explicit category at push time (they're all created in known branches) instead of relying on name inference; remove 'Bloc' and 'Underground' from the generic keyword lists.
- **[medium] Five stress-flag outputs computed but consumed nowhere** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:462-464,484-487,522-545,547-568`  
  getStressFlags computes and returns secularBrutalism, magicMilitarized, mageTheocracy, stateCrimeIntensity, and heresyIntensity, but a repo-wide search shows zero consumers outside priorityHelpers.js itself (heresyIntensity is used internally to gate heresySuppression; the exported field is unread). These are exactly the archetypes a DM would expect to surface ('militarized magic', 'mage theocracy' — both directly relevant to the owner's magic-as-booster theme), yet they change no faction power, no narrative, no income source. They also inflate anyActive, so an otherwise-quiet settlement can be flagged 'archetype active' by a flag that produces no visible consequence.  
  _Fix:_ Either wire them into powerGenerator stability/faction descs and economy income (magicMilitarized → garrison enchanting income; mageTheocracy → Arcane Council flavor) or delete them and drop them from anyActive.
- **[medium] Income normalization makes incomeMultiplier a mathematical no-op** (math_error) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1997-2003`  
  Stage 3 multiplies every income source's percentage by the same incomeMultiplier = priorityToMultiplier(economyOutput), then normalizes weights to sum to 100 (economicGenerator.js:1997-2003). A constant factor cancels exactly in w_i/Σw_j, so economyOutput has zero effect on the income-source mix despite the code's apparent intent that stronger economies reshape revenue. (economyOutput does feed individual percentages earlier, so the distribution still varies — but this particular dial is dead weight that misleads anyone tuning it.)  
  _Fix:_ Delete the multiplier, or apply it only to commerce-type sources (market taxes, trade) so high economyOutput genuinely shifts share away from agrarian rents.
- **[medium] Legitimacy patch at assembly updates score/label but not faction powers or relationships** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:92-116; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:2181-2199`  
  generatePowerStructure computes legitimacy with a provisional defense label, applies applyLegitimacyMultipliers to faction powers, and computes factionRelationships from those powers (powerGenerator.js:2160-2199). assembleSettlement then patches publicLegitimacy with the real defense readiness — score, label, govMultiplier, crimMultiplier all updated (assembleSettlement.js:92-116) — but never re-applies the multipliers or recomputes relationships. A settlement whose real readiness crosses a band (e.g. provisional 'Defensible' → real 'Fortress' pushes Tolerated→Approved) displays govMultiplier 1.15 while its governing faction's power was actually multiplied by 1.00, and relationship directions (e.g. crime 'declining' only when isEndorsed) reflect the stale band. The receipts disagree with the numbers they explain.  
  _Fix:_ When the band changes, rescale the governing/criminal faction powers by (newMult/oldMult) and rerun computeFactionRelationships; or compute defenseProfile before generatePower and drop the provisional path.
- **[medium] 'Lightly Defended' missing from both DEFENSE_CONTRIB maps — non-monotonic legitimacy** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionDynamics.js:43-49; src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:31-34; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:438-443`  
  defenseGenerator produces six readiness labels including 'Lightly Defended' (readiness 24-37, defenseGenerator.js:441). Both DEFENSE_CONTRIB tables (factionDynamics.js:43-49 and assembleSettlement.js:31-34) list only five labels, so 'Lightly Defended' falls to `?? 0` — the same legitimacy contribution as 'Defensible' (38-54) and BETTER than 'Vulnerable' (-5, readiness 12-23). The provisional label generator also emits 'Lightly Defended' (powerGenerator.js:2170-2179) with the same hole. Result: improving defenses from Lightly Defended to Defensible changes nothing, and the patch step computes a wrong delta for these settlements.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'Lightly Defended': -3 (between Vulnerable -5 and Defensible 0) to both maps.
- **[medium] safetyContrib vocabulary misses several produced safety labels** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionDynamics.js:30-40; src/generators/safetyProfile.js:76,106-112,131,199-260`  
  computePublicLegitimacy's safety contribution matches substrings (factionDynamics.js:30-40), but safetyProfile produces compound labels it can't see: 'Controlled — Occupation Curfew' and 'Controlled — Authoritarian' (stateCrime) → 0, same as 'Moderate', though residents 'face more risk from the authorities themselves'; 'Quarantined —/Restricted — Plague Conditions' → 0 while the worse-guard plague label ('Dangerous') scores -20; 'Critical — Slave Revolt' → 0 while the milder 'Tense — Slave Revolt' scores -12. So the WORST slave-revolt safety state contributes more legitimacy than the mildest one — backwards. ('Famine'/'Siege' compounds are caught via their substrings.)  
  _Fix:_ Add 'controlled', 'quarantined', 'restricted', and 'critical' to safetyContrib with deliberate values (critical ≤ -20; controlled slightly negative — order without consent).
- **[medium] 'Thriving' prosperity checked but never produced; 'Prosperous' misses dominant-merchant treatment** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:348,983-986; src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:839`  
  The prosperity generator emits only Struggling/Subsistence/Poor/Moderate/Comfortable/Prosperous/Wealthy (economicGenerator.js:1062, 2293). Yet powerGenerator gates 'Merchant Guilds (dominant)' on prosperity === 'Wealthy' || 'Thriving' (powerGenerator.js:983-986), genSuccessionNarr checks Wealthy||Thriving (348), and narrativeGenerator.js:839 includes 'Thriving'. 'Thriving' is dead vocabulary (it survives only in UI color maps), and the practical effect is that 'Prosperous' settlements — the second-richest real band — never get the dominant-merchant faction labeling or its 1.25x power bonus, a band gap a DM tuning the economy slider will feel.  
  _Fix:_ Replace 'Thriving' with 'Prosperous' in the three generator checks (keep Wealthy).
- **[medium] Noble factions orphaned from both power→economy feedback loops** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:12-19,52-59; src/generators/demandProfile.js:10-97,175`  
  Noble Houses/Landed Gentry/Manor Household (category 'noble') are frequently the #2-3 faction by power (powerGenerator.js:996-1053), yet both correlation systems exclude them: FACTION_TO_CATALOG and CATEGORY_THRESHOLDS have no 'noble' entry (factionCorrelation.js:12-19,52-59 — threshold defaults to 99, never passes), and FACTION_DEMAND has no 'noble' class (demandProfile.js:10-97) even though its own comment assigns 'nobles… prestige display goods' to the government class nobles don't map to. So a dominant noble faction pulls in no signature institution and demands no luxury imports — while a weaker merchant faction does both. For a DM, the most prestige-hungry consumer class in the setting is economically invisible.  
  _Fix:_ Map noble → ['Government'] (manor/estate institutions) with a ~20 threshold, and either add a noble demand table or alias noble→government in computeDemandImports.
- **[medium] applyFactionInstitutionBoosts reads def.p but catalog entries use baseChance** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/factionCorrelation.js:147-167`  
  Catalog entries carry `baseChance` (institutionalCatalog.js), but the boost pass sorts eligible candidates by `b[1].p || 0.5` and seeds getBaseChance with `def.p || 0.5` (factionCorrelation.js:147,154-157). Since `p` doesn't exist on any catalog entry, the 'boost most likely candidates first' sort is a no-op (all 0.5) and every candidate gets a flat 0.5×multiplier base regardless of whether its real baseChance is 0.05 or 0.9 — so the dominant faction's signature institution is effectively chosen by object-iteration order with uniform coin flips. The pushed addition also persists `p: def.p || 0.5` instead of the real baseChance. Comment/code mismatch too: 'strong gets 1.5x, mild 1.2x' vs actual 1.3/1.1.  
  _Fix:_ Use def.baseChance throughout (sort, getBaseChance seed, persisted field) and align the comment with the 1.3/1.1 constants.
- **[medium] Faction-boosted institutions added after economy/power — no economic or power footprint** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/factionCorrelationPass.js:20-78; step deps in src/generators/steps/*.js`  
  factionCorrelationPass (deps: generateEconomy + generatePower via neighbourFactions) pushes boost institutions into the shared institutions array (factionCorrelationPass.js:50-57), but economicState, instFlags, safetyProfile, services, and faction powers were all computed from the pre-boost list and are never recomputed. A Thieves'-Guild-pulled 'Black market' shows in the dossier yet contributes nothing to blackMarketCapture, criminal income, criminalEffective, or capture state; a military-pulled garrison doesn't move militaryEffective or defense. Only population/NPC steps (which run after) see it. The trace honestly says 'pulled in', but the institution is economically inert — a coherence gap between the institution list and every ledger that should consume it.  
  _Fix:_ Either run the boost pass before generateEconomy (compute boosts from priorities instead of final powers), or mark boosted institutions and apply a targeted post-pass (e.g. recompute safetyProfile/income entries for criminal/military additions).
- **[medium] DM-facing prose corrupted: the word 'it' replaced by 'SEVERITY' in five strings** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1919; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:343,345,388; src/data/spatialData.js:49`

- **[medium] Thieves' Guild institution can exist with no criminal faction behind it** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:606-611,1143-1159`  
  The criminal faction gate requires criminalEffective > 42 AND (city/metropolis OR criminalEffective > 58) (powerGenerator.js:608-611). Then computeCriminalCaptureState returns 'none', no gov↔crime or crime↔military relationship exists, no Shadow-Economy capture pressure — the power web and the institution list tell contradictory stories. - **[low] Government-institution → governing-faction map misses several catalog names** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:647-668; src/data/institutionalCatalog.js (Government sections)`  
  The W lookup (powerGenerator.js:647-668) maps government institution names to governing-faction types, but catalog names "Lord's reeve" (thorp), 'Village headman' (hamlet), 'Town council' (town), and 'City administration' (city) match no key, so those settlements fall through to generic tier defaults. - **[low] generateEconomicScore's governance-aware phrasing dead (_govFacName never set); issue param unused** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:164-189,2414-2433`  
  generateEconomicScore (conflict plot hooks) branches on d._govFacName containing 'Feudal/Steward/Noble/Lord' or 'Church/Theocrat/Bishop' to phrase the deadline as "the lord's next court hearing" or 'the next chapter assembly' (powerGenerator.js:164-170). d is the instFlags object from getInstFlags, which never carries _govFacName (repo-wide: only this read exists), so every settlement gets 'the next council session' — including royal seats and theocracies. The third parameter (the conflict issue object) is also accepted and never used, so hooks ignore what the conflict is about.

- **[low] demandProfile category resolution conditional is a no-op** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/demandProfile.js:175`  
  computeDemandImports line 175: `(faction.category === 'government' && !faction.isGoverning) ? 'government' : faction.category || 'government'` — both branches yield the same value whenever category is set, so the expression reduces to `faction.category || 'government'`. The shape suggests the intended rule was the opposite: map the GOVERNING faction to the 'government' (prestige goods) demand class regardless of its inferred category, so a governing Merchant Council demands prestige display goods. As written that intent never executes.  
  _Fix:_ Replace with `faction.isGoverning ? 'government' : (faction.category || 'government')` if that was the intent, else simplify to remove the misleading conditional.
- **[low] STRESS_FLAVOR table omits the five newer stressors** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:194-205,440-470`  
  genRelNarrative weights NPC relationships toward stress-appropriate types using STRESS_FLAVOR (powerGenerator.js:194-205, used at 440-470), which covers the original ten stressors but not insurgency, mass_migration, wartime, religious_conversion, or slave_revolt — even though the rest of powerGenerator gives those five full faction treatments. - **[low] NPC faction-assignment matchers use stale/greedy vocabulary ('order', 'crafts')** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/npcGenerator.js:755-800,905-918`  
  relFaction matching includes name.includes('order') (npcGenerator.js:761-765 region), so 'Arcane Orders' — when it outranks Religious Authorities in the power-sorted array — is selected as the religious faction and priests/clergy NPCs get linked to the mage faction. - **[low] Crafts/Infrastructure/Entertainment institution categories feed no power or instFlag signal; Craft Guilds faction ungated on craft institutions** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:30-67; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:612-615,1128-1142`  
  Of the catalog's categories, Crafts (29 entries), Infrastructure (26), and Entertainment (17) contribute to no instFlag and no faction power: getInstitutionNames keys only on military/economy/religious/magic/criminal name fragments (priorityHelpers.js:30-67), and Craft Guilds faction power is purely economyOutput-derived (powerGenerator.js:612-615, M = 17×mult(economyOutput×0.75+10)). Crafts does at least feed the prosperity depth bonus (economicGenerator.js:2343). Given the owner ruled out a craft ledger this is acceptable noise — but the faction/institution disconnect is the one piece a DM will notice in the Power tab.  
  _Fix:_ Scale the Craft Guilds multiplier by a count of Crafts-category institutions (cheap, no new ledger): e.g. M × (0.7 + 0.1×min(5, craftCount)).
- **[low] Viability helper names describe the wrong domain (food analysis named buildFactionList, etc.)** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2456-2563`  
  In generateEconomicViability, the de-minified helper names are systematically wrong: buildFactionList = food/supply viability, computeFactionPowers = resource-chain analysis, buildPowerNarrative = water-dependency checks, buildConflict = summary builder (economicGenerator.js:2460-2554). Behavior is correct, but anyone auditing power↔economy mappings (this audit included) must read bodies to learn that 'computeFactionPowers' has nothing to do with factions — a live maintenance hazard in the exact cross-domain seam the owner cares about. Also sortBySeverity's rank map lacks the literal 'warning' severity pushed at line 2519, yielding NaN comparisons (harmless but undefined ordering).  
  _Fix:_ Rename to analyzeFoodViability/analyzeResourceChains/analyzeWaterDependencies/buildViabilitySummary; add 'warning' to the severity rank map.
- **[low] Duplicated tier condition in governing power base** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/powerGenerator.js:604`  
  powerGenerator.js:604: `tier === 'metropolis' || tier === 'metropolis' ? 35 : tier === 'city' ? 33 : …` — the second disjunct is a verbatim duplicate, suggesting a lost tier label (or simply dead code). Harmless today but it reads like an unfinished edit at the single most load-bearing constant in faction power (the governing faction's base).  
  _Fix:_ Drop the duplicate (or restore the intended second tier).

Strengths: Conserved governance ledger is exactly right: governanceLedger.js is a single read-point for publicLegitimacy with legacy bare-number handling and explicit rationale for NOT folding governing-faction power in — the cleanest cross-domain seam audited.; The five-domain instFlags core (priorityHelpers.js:253-421) is genuinely coherent: crime degrades military/economy/religion, economy funds garrison quality, magic is boosted by economy and degraded by crime, and the circular crime↔military influence is resolved in a deliberate, stable order — honest, explainable math for a DM.; All 15 stressor types get bespoke power-structure consequences (War Council, Occupation Authority + Resistance Network, Claimant Blocs, Quarantine Council, Conversion Enforcement Office, Revolt Leadership + Abolitionist Network) with per-faction power rebalancing and appended desc receipts — exactly the gameable consequences the audience wants (powerGenerator.js:1181-1555).; Faction relationship matrix (factionDynamics.js) bands every pair by power ratio with distinct narratives, direction arrows tied to stress/legitimacy, and dmNote prompts ('Ask: which officials have arrangements…') — receipts written for table use, not just display.; Power→economy correlation is closed-loop AND traced: faction boosts and demand imports record 'why is this institution/import here' causes (factionCorrelationPass.js recordTrace), and CHAIN_SUPPRESSES keys all match real chain ids so locally-produced goods correctly suppress faction demand (demandProfile.js).; Legitimacy contributions are tier-scaled (factionDynamics.js:79-88) so a 'Vulnerable' hamlet isn't scored as a governance failure — a thoughtful realism calibration; PROSPERITY_CONTRIB covers both prosperity vocabularies (Struggling and Subsistence).; applyLegitimacyMultipliers preserves rawPower for display and the Power tab renormalizes shares, so post-multiplier powers not summing to 100 never lies to the user (PowerTab.jsx:27,157).; ensureFactionStructuralNpcs guarantees each faction archetype has its pillar role-holders via the shared canonical archetype detector, so kill/succession events always have real targets (factionRoles.js).; Magic-as-booster is threaded through the economy in tiers a DM can feel: three-tier magic income (apothecary → spellcasting services → arcane industry) plus an Enchanted Goods Premium on craft exports at high effective magic, and teleportation infrastructure consistently substitutes for trade access across viability, dependency, and prosperity logic.; Defensive details done right: 'access to X' institution names excluded from religious-faction detection, faction-name dedup with retry + suffix, self-pair and duplicate-pair guards in the relationship matrix, and inferFactionCategory falling back to 'other' instead of dumping into government.

### magic-supplement

Magic-as-supplement is conceptually right and mostly well-gated at generation time — defenseGenerator and the magic-trade pricing are exemplary — but the model frays at the seams between its FOUR parallel implementations. The same druid/divine/arcane food offset is implemented three times (foodGenerator, economicGenerator's buildFactionList copy, chainMagicSubstitution) with different institution matchers and different gates, so the food ledger, viability tab, and chain display can disagree about the same settlement. The flagship dead-magic guarantee has a confirmed leak: chain substitution's divine tradition has no magicExists/priority gate, so no-magic worlds still get 'Temple granaries blessed' magicRecovery; capacityModel and magicProfile likewise report strained/purchasable magic in worlds where it doesn't exist; and servicesGenerator's priorityMagic strip is dead code (`0||50`). On the sim side the booster is largely invisible: 'magically_sustained' canonicalizes to 'stable' (the purpose-built 'substituted' status is unreachable), foodSecurity.magicSupplement is a cosmetic number that no deriver consumes while the actually-applied offset has no receipt, and the upstream-propagation pass can erase the sustained status it just granted. Add the forced-teleport-vs-66-gate contradiction, two never-activatable arcane chains, and a nine-value undocumented threshold zoo, and the verdict is: right architecture, one canonical tradition-detector and one offset table away from coherent.

- **[high] 'magically_sustained' status is invisible to the simulation — maps to 'stable'** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:57-79,294-297; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83`  
  chainMagicSubstitution emits status 'magically_sustained' (chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83). The sim-side adapter's LEGACY_TO_CANONICAL (supplyChainState.js:57-63) has no entry for it, so canonicalSupplyChainStatus() falls through to the default 'stable' (line 78). The canonical vocabulary even defines 'substituted' explicitly for "alternative path (e.g. magic substitute)" (line 49) — it is unreachable, and the 'substituted' branch in applyRegionalPressureToStatus (line 240-242) is dead. inferSubstitutes (line 294-297) also only reports resource substituteActive, never magic substitution. Net effect: a grain chain held together by druids at 65% recovery reads as a perfectly stable chain to every domain consumer (capacity context, conditions, dossier, hasDisruptedChains), erasing exactly the fragility a DM should see.  
  _Fix:_ Add magically_sustained → 'substituted' to LEGACY_TO_CANONICAL and have inferSubstitutes report chain.magicNote/magicRecovery as the active substitute.
- **[high] Dead-magic leak: divine tradition bypasses every magic gate in chain substitution** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:49,70-72; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:49-55,91-98`  
  traditions.divine in computeActiveChains.js:70-72 has NO magicPriority and NO magicExists gate (comment admits 'religionInfluence check not available here'). In a magicExists=false world the pipeline passes magicPriority=0, which correctly kills druid (>=30), arcane (>=35) and alchemy (>=15) — but a monastery/cathedral still fires divine, so impaired food chains get magicRecovery 0.40 with the note 'Temple granaries blessed; divine provision fills the gap' and healing chains get 'Divine healing supplements mundane medicine' (chainMagicSubstitution.js:49-55,91-98). So the owner's question — does magicExists=false zero ALL magic boosts — is answered no. Compounding: computeActiveChains defaults magicPriority=50 (line 49), so any caller that omits it gets full magic substitution silently.  
  _Fix:_ Thread magicExists (or a relPri + magicOn pair, matching defenseGenerator.js:109) into computeActiveChains and gate traditions.divine on it; drop the =50 default in favor of an explicit required arg.
- **[high] Three parallel magic-food-offset implementations with divergent gates and matchers** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:96-167; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:417-447; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:39-67`  
  The same druid/divine/arcane food offset is implemented three times: (1) foodGenerator.js:161-167 — druid pm>=30 with BROAD matcher ('druid','grove','warden'), divine needs priorityReligion>=55 AND magicActive (pm>25), arcane pm>=50; (2) economicGenerator buildFactionList copy at economicGenerator.js:417-447 — same rates but compound matchers ('druid circle','grove shrine'...) and divine WITHOUT the pm>25 requirement; (3) chainMagicSubstitution with chain-level rates and ungated divine. Concrete divergence: an institution named 'Druid Grove' gets the 65% offset in foodSecurity but not in the viability foodBalance or chain substitution; a pm=10/rel=70 monastery town gets 40% divine offset in viability but 0 in foodSecurity. The Economics tab, Viability tab, and chain display can therefore disagree about the same settlement's food deficit.  
  _Fix:_ Extract one detectMagicTraditions(institutions, config) helper (defenseGenerator.js:97-124 is the best model) and one offset table; have all three callers consume it.
- **[high] foodSecurity.magicSupplement is a cosmetic number; the applied offset has no receipt** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:96-104,161-167,286; src/domain/foodLedger.js:27,64`  
  foodGenerator computes TWO unrelated magic numbers: magicSupplement (line 98-104, tier-scale × institution multiplier, max 0.35) which drives magicNote and is persisted/forwarded by foodLedger.js:64 — but never enters the deficit math; and magicOffset (line 161-167) which actually reduces deficitPct/foodRatio but is NOT returned, so there is no receipt for it. A settlement can display 'Significant magical food supplement' while the applied offset is 0, and vice versa. Worse, the magicInstMult fallthrough of 0.4 (line 100) grants a 'Trace magical food contribution' note to settlements with NO magic institutions at all. foodLedger.magicSupplement is read by no deriver (capacityModel.js:407, causalState.js:196, deriveSystemState.js:80 all read deficit/surplus only) — a produced-but-never-consumed quantity carrying the wrong semantics in the conserved ledger.  
  _Fix:_ Return magicRatio (the applied offset as % of need) as the persisted magicSupplement, derive magicNote from it, and delete the parallel cosmetic formula.
- **[medium] magical_goods and planar chains can never activate (empty processingInstitutions)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1047-1084; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117`  
  supplyChainData.js defines arcane_magical.magical_goods (line 1047) and arcane_magical.planar (line 1069) with processingInstitutions: []. computeActiveChains.js:114-117 requires matchedInsts.length >= 1 before any runnable logic, so both chains are unreachable dead data — even with a magical_node resource (RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS line 1555 feeds magical_goods), an Enchanter's shop, Planar traders, or a planar embassy. The institutions still produce income via INSTITUTIONAL_SERVICE_MAP (computeActiveChains.js:679-705 'Arcane Services'/'Planar Commerce'), so the income layer works while the chain layer silently doesn't: a high-magic metropolis shows planar income with no corresponding supply chain to disrupt, capture, or trace.  
  _Fix:_ Give magical_goods processors ['Enchanter', "Mages' guild", 'Academy of magic'] and planar processors ['Planar trader', 'Planar embassy', 'Teleportation circle'].
- **[medium] Forced teleportation circle contradicts the 66+ magic gate it's supposed to respect** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:20-54; src/generators/institutionProbability.js:131-137,158-166; src/generators/steps/resolveConfig.js:101`  
  institutionProbability.js:158-166 zeroes teleportation/planar/airship below priorityMagic 66 ('Institutions requiring high magic'), and the 4× isolation boost requires >=70 (line 131-137). Yet isolationGenerator.js:20-54 force-injects a Teleportation circle for ANY isolated town+ at any priority >= 1, maintained by a hedge wizard. So a priorityMagic=5 world hosts permanent teleportation infrastructure the probability model says cannot exist below 66. There is also a cliff: at priority 0 the isolated city is rerouted to 'road' (resolveConfig.js:101), at priority 1 it gets a teleport circle. And isolationGenerator.js:22 uses `priorityMagic || 50`, turning a 0 dial into 50 for the airship decision. The design principle ('any isolated town+ MUST have magic trade') is documented, but the priority gates around it disagree with it.  
  _Fix:_ Below a magic floor (e.g. 26), reroute isolated town+ to 'road' like the noMagic case instead of forcing infrastructure the world can't plausibly maintain; fix `|| 50` to `?? 50`.
- **[medium] servicesGenerator no-magic strip: `(priorityMagic || 50) === 0` is always false** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1938`  
  servicesGenerator.js:1938: `const _noMagicSvcs = d.magicExists === false || (d.priorityMagic || 50) === 0;` — `0 || 50` evaluates to 50, so the right-hand clause can never be true. The intended `??` semantics ('strip magic services when the dial is 0') is dead; only magicExists===false triggers the strip. Compare resolveConfig.js:68 and priorityHelpers.js:93 which both correctly use `(priorityMagic || 0) === 0` / `?? 50` patterns. Today this is masked because a 0 dial also zeroes magic institutions upstream, but any forced/custom arcane institution in a magicExists=true, dial=0 world will emit magic-category services through this dead gate.  
  _Fix:_ Change to `(d.priorityMagic ?? 50) === 0` (or reuse the noMagicWorld() helper from magicFilter.js:40-45, which already implements exactly this check).
- **[medium] Dead-magic world still reports a 'strained' Magical capacity and buyable-magic profile** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:579-622; src/domain/magicProfile.js:66-148`  
  capacityModel.deriveMagical (capacityModel.js:579-622) never checks magicLedger().magicExists: in a magicExists=false world the band is 'none' → supply 40-8=32 vs demand 45 → ratio 0.71 → 'strained'. The dossier thus reports a magical-supply shortage in a world where magic does not function. defenseGenerator already solved this exact problem by excluding the magical dimension from readiness in no-magic worlds (defenseGenerator.js:425-427) — the capacity model is inconsistent with it. Similarly magicProfile has no magicExists handling: 'none' yields availability 'rare', cost 'extortionate', legality 'restricted' (magicProfile.js:66-148), implying spellcasting is purchasable-but-pricey rather than nonexistent. magicProfile also defaults a missing magicLevel to 'low' (line 67) while magicLedger defaults to 50→'medium' — two different defaults for the same unknown.  
  _Fix:_ Short-circuit both on magicLedger(s).magicExists===false: capacity → an explicit 'absent' profile excluded from summaries; magicProfile → availability 'absent'/cost 'n/a'.
- **[medium] Upstream-propagation pass overwrites 'magically_sustained' back to 'vulnerable'** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:279,320-334`  
  applyMagicSubstitution runs at computeActiveChains.js:279, then the second upstream pass (line 320-334) skips only chains already 'vulnerable' or 'impaired' (line 323). A 'magically_sustained' chain with any impaired/vulnerable upstream is downgraded to 'vulnerable', erasing the substitution status while magicNote and magicRecovery remain on the object. The UI then renders a 'vulnerable' chain carrying a '✦ ... 65% recovery' badge (EconomicsTab.jsx:128-133) — a contradictory display state. It is also backwards logically: druidic regrowth substitutes the chain's INPUT, which is precisely why the upstream shortage should matter less. The comment at line 285 ('runs after magic substitution so magic recovery already applied') shows the ordering was intentional but the status guard forgot the new status value.  
  _Fix:_ Add `chain.status === 'magically_sustained'` to the early-return guard at line 323 (and to the first pass at 302/309 for symmetry).
- **[medium] Divine food gate inconsistency: foodSecurity demands priorityMagic>25, defense/viability don't** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:98,163-165; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:109-114; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:425-431`  
  foodGenerator wraps all magic offsets, including divine, in magicActive = magicExists && priorityMagic > 25 (foodGenerator.js:98,163), so a low-magic/high-faith world (pm=10, rel=80, monastery) gets ZERO divine food offset. defenseGenerator gates divine on magicOn && relPri>=55 only (defenseGenerator.js:109-114) and grants monster/economic defense boosts; economicGenerator's viability copy likewise grants the 40% divine food offset with no magic-dial requirement (economicGenerator.js:425-431). The same theological premise — does divine provision scale with the arcane dial or the religion dial? — is answered differently per subsystem. For a DM building a 'miracles but no wizards' setting, food security contradicts both defense and viability.  
  _Fix:_ Pick one rule (defenseGenerator's magicOn && relPri>=55 is the most defensible) and apply it to foodGenerator's divine branch.
- **[medium] Terrain-specific food/timber chains excluded from magic substitution** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:6-13; src/data/supplyChainData.js:360-438`

TIMBER_CHAIN_IDS (line 11) omits mountain_timber_harvest (386). So druids sustain a depleted 'grain' or 'timber' chain but cannot sustain a depleted oasis, floodplain, or mountain-timber chain — settlements on the very terrains where magical supplementation is most narratively expected (desert oasis, mountain logging) are the ones excluded. EXTRACT_CHAIN_IDS similarly omits precious_metals_mining (defensible) and desert_glasswork. This is silent drift: new chains were added to the data file without updating the substitution lists.

- **[medium] Tradition matcher vocabulary drift across the four magic-tradition detectors** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:59-61; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:68-75; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:97-124; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:421-435`  
  Druid: foodGenerator matches broad substrings 'druid','grove','warden' (foodGenerator.js:59) — 'warden' also matches a mundane game warden (the hunting extraction gate at computeActiveChains.js:394 uses 'warden' for ordinary hunting), a false-positive druid; the other three detectors require compound names ('druid circle', "warden's lodge"). Result: the same institution roster activates different tradition sets in food, chains, defense, and viability.

- **[low] resourceTaxonomy.magicLevelScore uses the stale band vocabulary magicLedger was built to kill** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/worldPulse/resourceTaxonomy.js:31-38,91`

- **[low] Famine stress probability ignores the magic food supplement** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/stressGenerator.js:101-150`

- **[low] Spellcasting chain lists institution names as outputs; alchemy processor never matches "Wizard's tower"** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1016,1032-1040; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117,176`

- **[low] Healing substitution sets no magicRecovery; lone status-only envelope** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:91-98`  
  Food, timber, and extraction substitutions all write the triple {status, magicNote, magicRecovery, exportable:false}. - **[low] hasTeleportationInfra doc claims a >=66 gate that doesn't exist; _isolationInfraType never consumed** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:71-77,172-182; src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:91; src/generators/foodGenerator.js:64-66`
