Also note foodGenerator's inline teleport matcher (line 64-66) omits 'extradimensional', which hasTeleportationInfra includes — minor matcher drift between the two.  
  _Fix:_ Fix the doc comment (the gate was deliberately dropped when injection became unconditional), delete _isolationInfraType or consume it in the maintainer description, and have foodGenerator call hasTeleportationInfra instead of its inline copy.
- **[low] Magic threshold zoo: nine-plus gate values, several straddling the documented band edges** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/constants.js:34-38; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:56,78,103; src/generators/institutionProbability.js:131,164,173; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:325,1814; src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:24`  
  Canonical bands are 0 none / 1-25 low / 26-65 medium / 66-100 high (constants.js:34-38). Gates in the wild: >25 (foodGen magicActive), >=30 (druid), >=35 (arcane traditions), >=50 (arcane food, scrying), >=55 (timber arcane, arcane guild), >=65 (extraction substitution, arcane industry income), <66/> =66 (institutionProbability hi-magic zero/boost, structuralValidator band), >=70 (isolation teleport boost), >75 (viability agri boost), >=80 (airship), >85 (auto-add wizard). The >=65 gates sit INSIDE the medium band while the >=66 gates define high — so a dial of exactly 65 gets 'high-tier' extraction substitution and arcane-industry income while being classified medium everywhere else, and 66-69 settlements pass the hi-magic institution gate but fail the isolation teleport boost. None of these intermediate thresholds are documented anywhere.  
  _Fix:_ Define named constants (MAGIC_GATE.druid=30, .arcane=35, .high=66, ...) in constants.js next to getMagicLevel and snap the 65s to 66.
- **[low] institutionProbability divides by undefined priorityMagic (NaN-poisons chance)** (math_error) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/institutionProbability.js:75,158`  
  institutionProbability.js:75 computes `config.priorityMagic / 50` with no default, while line 158 in the same file uses `config.priorityMagic ?? 50`. If a caller ever passes a config without the dial (only resolveConfig guarantees it; structuralValidator.js:882 defaults independently), magicMult is NaN, chance becomes NaN, and the final clamp `Math.min(Math.max(NaN,0),1)` returns NaN — an institution probability that is neither 0 nor 1 and fails every comparison. Latent today because the pipeline always materializes priorityMagic, but it is the only priority in the function read without `?? 50` (priorityEconomy/Military/Religion/Criminal at lines 38,45,55,67,101,109 are equally unguarded — but those are always present; the magic dial is the one that legacy saves omit).  
  _Fix:_ Use `(config.priorityMagic ?? 50) / 50` at line 75 to match line 158.
- **[low] Hedge wizard maintaining a metropolis lifeline strains fantasy realism** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/isolationGenerator.js:10-14,61-87`  
  isolationGenerator's maintainer fallback prefers a hedge wizard for ANY tier (isolationGenerator.js:63-67 — 'Prefer hedge wizard (self-sufficient)'), while MAINTAINER_DESC (line 10-14) correctly scales the description: town=hedge wizard, city=resident wizard, metropolis='a tower of wizards'. Because the institution PICK ignores tier but the description text assumes scaling, an isolated metropolis can end up with a literal 'Hedge wizard' institution whose desc claims a tower of wizards — and at low magic priority, foodGenerator then routes up to 30% of a 40,000-person city's caloric imports through that one hedge wizard's circle (foodGenerator.js:147-152). Within fantasy bounds, a settlement-killing single point of failure should at least scale its maintainer institution with tier the way the flavor text already does.  
  _Fix:_ For city/metropolis, prefer wizard/mage/academy entries before the hedge fallback so the institution matches MAINTAINER_DESC's scaling.

Strengths: defenseGenerator is the reference implementation for magic-as-booster: a single magicOn gate (config.magicExists !== false) zeroes magPri, every tradition (druid 30 / arcane 35 / guild 55 / alchemy 15 / divine relPri 55) is consistently gated, boosts are tier- and dial-scaled rather than flat, and the magical readiness dimension is excluded from the average in no-magic worlds so settlements aren't penalized for a dimension that can't exist (defenseGenerator.js:86-124,425-427).; resolveConfig collapses magicExists=false to priorityMagic=0 once at pipeline entry and writes it into effectiveConfig (resolveConfig.js:48-49,132), so most downstream generators inherit a correct zero dial without local checks — a sound single-choke-point design.; No-magic worlds have defense-in-depth: magicFilter strips the catalog, institutionProbability's priorityMagic/50 multiplier organically zeroes arcane institutions, stripArcaneInstitutions is a safety net, and isolated town+ is rerouted to 'road' so the forced-teleport path never fires (resolveConfig.js:87-101).; Magic substitution sets exportable=false on sustained chains (chainMagicSubstitution.js:66,86,107) — magic keeps the settlement alive but cannot manufacture export surplus. That is exactly the right 'supplement, not engine' semantics the owner wants, and it correctly propagates into deriveExportsFromChains.; Magic trade imports for isolated settlements are priced honestly: 0.30 coverage versus 0.35 for a plain road ('real but expensive', foodGenerator.js:144-152), and prosperity caps are softened to penalties rather than removed (lines 218-228) — magic mitigates, never erases, the structural problem.; magicLedger itself is well-built: canonical band folding of the stale moderate/common/pervasive vocabulary, effective-dial zeroing for dead-magic worlds, and the shared ARCANE_INSTITUTION_PATTERN ended the capacityModel/magicProfile matcher divergence it documents (magicLedger.js:26,44-72).; The three-tier magic economy (apothecary 15 / spellcasting 35 / arcane industry 65, each with matching institution and settlement-tier gates, economicGenerator.js:1765-1817) gives DMs a legible ladder from hedge magic to arcane industry, and chain substitution rates (druid > divine > arcane for food; arcane-only for extraction) encode sensible tradition specializations with flavorful, specific receipts ('Conjure Animals produces fish').

### resources-terrain

The terrain→resource→chain→good spine is mostly real and well-gated: resources resolve from terrain/route correctly in random mode, every resource maps to chains/institutions/trade goods, label-to-key resolution is verified correct across all 52 chains, and extraction/processing gates give honest receipts. The breakage concentrates in three seams. (1) Depletion state has three uncoordinated stores (nearbyResourcesDepleted, nearbyResourcesState key-form, nearbyResourcesState label-form from events) — the DEPLETE_RESOURCE event writes a key no generator or world-pulse reader matches, RECOVERED_RESOURCE has no mutation at all, same-seed regens erase sim-acquired depletion, and food security ignores depletion entirely. (2) Manual resource mode is badly broken: marking one resource abundant/depleted silently drops all plain selections, and terrain-specific resources the UI offers are filtered out by a missing terrain argument. (3) A legacy parallel layer (resourceGenerator + RESOURCE_CHAINS + SPECIAL_RESOURCES) feeds the dossier's resource analysis from generic terrain words instead of actual rolled resources. Plus data rot: 9 dead RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS refs gut desert/mountain chain activation, and the coal-as-timber commodity hack makes coal seams renewable. Magic currently only rescues broken chains — there is no healthy-chain booster, and food's two magic terms disagree.

- **[high] DEPLETE_RESOURCE event writes label-keyed state; everything else keys by resource key** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/events/mutate.js:314-325; src/domain/events/batch.js:292-295; src/domain/worldPulse/tierResourceDynamics.js:218-223`  
  depleteResource (mutate.js:314-325) keys nearbyResourcesState by labelFromTarget(), which replaces underscores with spaces (batch.js:292-295): depleting resource.grain_fields writes nearbyResourcesState['grain fields']='depleted'. Every other consumer keys by the raw resource key: world-pulse resourceState() reads nearbyResourcesState[resource] with resource='grain_fields' (tierResourceDynamics.js:219-223) so it misses the DM's depletion, can emit a duplicate depletion candidate for the same resource, and the recovery path can never see it as depleted; resolveResources manual mode (resolveResources.js:99-110) matches against catalog keys so the space-keyed entry never matches; world-pulse's own writer uses the key form (tierResourceDynamics.js:434-444). Only deriveResourcePressure (counts any 'depleted' value) and deriveRegionalState (normalizeGood) tolerate the mismatch.  
  _Fix:_ In depleteResource, keep the raw targetId tail (the resource key) instead of labelFromTarget(); also add the key to config.nearbyResourcesDepleted so the event path matches the world-pulse writer (applyResourceOutcomeToSettlement).
- **[high] RECOVERED_RESOURCE has no mutation — depletion via events is a one-way door** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/events/mutate.js:51-124; src/domain/events/registry.js:112,560; src/components/settlement/EventComposer.jsx:53`  
  The composer offers RECOVERED_RESOURCE (EventComposer.jsx:53), the registry declares it recomputes ['resources','activeChains','economicState'] (registry.js:112) and gives it stateDeltas (resilience +9, resourcePressure -7, registry.js:560), but mutate.js's switch (lines 51-124) has no RECOVERED_RESOURCE case. The dimension numbers move, yet config.nearbyResourcesState stays 'depleted', so deriveResourcePressure keeps counting the depleted resource, the regional graph keeps reporting the depleted good, and chains stay flagged. A DM who narrates 'the mine reopens' gets a dossier that still says exhausted everywhere except the two abstract dials.  
  _Fix:_ Add a recoverResource mutation that sets nearbyResourcesState[key]='allow' and removes the key from nearbyResourcesDepleted — symmetric with depleteResource after the key-form fix.
- **[high] Manual resource mode silently drops every plain-'allow' selection once any resource is marked abundant/depleted** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:99-113; src/components/ConfigurationPanel.jsx:153-172`  
  In manual mode, if nearbyResourcesState has ANY entry, membership is rebuilt solely from the state map: nearbyResources = allCompatible.filter(k => resourceState[k] is allow|abundant|depleted) (resolveResources.js:99-103). But the UI never writes 'allow' into the state map — Off→Allow only appends to config.nearbyResources (ConfigurationPanel.jsx:160-162); state entries exist only for abundant/depleted. So a DM who selects six resources and marks one 'abundant' generates a settlement with ONE resource; the other five vanish without warning. config.nearbyResources is ignored entirely in this branch.  
  _Fix:_ Union the state-map keys with config.nearbyResources when rebuilding membership (treat selected-but-stateless as 'allow'), or have the UI write 'allow' entries on selection.
- **[high] Manual mode drops terrain-specific resources the UI let the user pick** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:96; src/generators/terrainHelpers.js:36-73; src/components/ConfigurationPanel.jsx:174-183`  
  The configuration panel calls getCompatibleResources(route, terrain) and explicitly shows desert/mountain resources when a terrain override is set (ConfigurationPanel.jsx:175-183). The pipeline's manual branch calls getCompatibleResources(tradeRoute) with NO terrain argument (resolveResources.js:96), so all 8 terrain-gated resources (oasis_water, date_palms, glass_sand, desert_salt, camel_herds, alpine_pasture, mountain_timber, hot_springs_mineral) come back compatible:false ('Requires X terrain override', terrainHelpers.js:50-54) and are filtered out of allCompatible — the user's hand-picked desert economy silently evaporates. The water-terrain unlock (coastal road hamlet can fish) is likewise lost in manual mode. Random mode passes terrain correctly (resolveResources.js:43-45).  
  _Fix:_ Pass the resolved terrain override into getCompatibleResources in the manual branch, same as the random branch does.
- **[high] Dossier resourceAnalysis is computed from generic terrain words, not the settlement's actual resources** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:31-34; src/generators/resourceGenerator.js:14-26,169-188; src/data/resourceData.js:424-686`  
  generateNarratives passes TERRAIN_DATA[terrain].allowedResources (generic words: 'fish','salt','timber','grain') as the nearbyResources argument and [] as specialResources (generateNarratives.js:31-34). So the whole legacy analysis layer (resourceGenerator.js) — active RESOURCE_CHAINS, exploitation report, viability imports, export products — is a function of terrain+institutions only; the resources actually rolled in resolveResources are never consulted. A town that rolled iron_deposits gets no iron chain in its analysis unless the terrain word list happens to contain 'iron ore'; a town WITHOUT fishing_grounds still reports fish chains on coastal terrain. The terrain-specific RESOURCE_CHAINS entries (alpineWool, camelCaravan, etc., rawResource = key forms like 'alpine_pasture') can never match terrain word lists, so they are dead. specialResources=[] also kills SPECIAL_RESOURCES featureEffects (tourism/pilgrimage) permanently.  
  _Fix:_ Feed ctx.nearbyResources (mapped to chain rawResource vocabulary) and the actual special resources (ancient_ruins/hot_springs/magical_node present in nearbyResources) into generateResourceAnalysis, or retire the legacy layer in favor of computeActiveChains output.
- **[medium] RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS contains 9 dead chain references (agricultural.*, services.hospital, wrong-need beekeeping)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1529-1567; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:78-81,645-648`  
  Verified against SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS: date_palms → 'agricultural.food_processing','agricultural.brewing'; desert_salt → 'agricultural.food_processing'; camel_herds → 'agricultural.livestock'; alpine_pasture → 'agricultural.livestock','agricultural.textiles'; hot_springs_mineral → 'services.hospital'; foraging_areas and ancient_grove → 'food_security.beekeeping_wax' (beekeeping_wax lives under manufacturing). No 'agricultural' or 'services' need exists. Consequences: those chains never get activatedByResource → status shows 'operational' instead of 'running', they sort lower, and deriveLocalProductionFromChains (computeActiveChains.js:645-648) filters on activatedByResource so desert/mountain settlements under-report local production from exactly the chains that justify their existence. Both alpine_pasture refs are dead, so it activates nothing.  
  _Fix:_ Rewrite to existing ids: food_security.livestock, food_security.brewing, manufacturing.food_processing, manufacturing.textiles, manufacturing.beekeeping_wax, healing_medicine.hospital, plus the terrain chains (raw_extraction.alpine_wool, raw_extraction.date_palm_harvest, trade_entrepot.camel_caravan).
- **[medium] Resource depletion never affects food security or stress probabilities** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:34,44,71-76,108-116; src/generators/stressGenerator.js:71-75`  
  foodGenerator reads config.nearbyResources only (foodGenerator.js:34,44); nearbyResourcesDepleted/nearbyResourcesState are never consulted. A settlement whose grain_fields rolled depleted (or was depleted by event/world-pulse) still gets the full +0.25 agriMod (line 110) and full 'Grain & agriculture' chain credit (line 71). stressGenerator's hasGrain/hasFish/hasTimber flags (stressGenerator.js:71-75) ignore depletion the same way. Meanwhile the export side respects depletion strictly (deriveExportsFromChains skips depleted, computeActiveChains.js:484). So the dossier can say 'fishing grounds exhausted' and 'food: Surplus from fishing' simultaneously — the cross-domain consequence a DM most expects from depletion is missing, and registry.js:90's claim that DEPLETE_RESOURCE recomputes foodSecurity is hollow (recompute yields identical output).  
  _Fix:_ Pass depleted set into generateFoodSecurity; depleted food resources should drop or halve their agriMod and chain-flag contributions.
- **[medium] Terrain-specific food resources feed nothing in the food model** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/foodGenerator.js:27-30,71-76,108-116`  
  The food chain flags and agriMod recognize only grain_fields, fertile_floodplain, grazing_land, fishing_grounds, river_fish, river_mills, hunting_grounds, foraging_areas (foodGenerator.js:71-76,110-114). date_palms ('productive desert agriculture'), oasis_water, camel_herds, alpine_pasture, and marshlands (waterfowl) contribute zero food capacity and zero source-chain diversity. Desert terrain gets agri 0.3 and mountain 0.4 (line 27-30), and the system compensates with a blanket 'terrain-structural import' waiver (lines 150-151, 209-217) — so a desert town with date palms + oasis is fed by the same hand-wave as one with nothing, and its food panel shows fewer source chains than the resource list implies. The compensating resources exist in data precisely for these terrains but are orphaned from the food model.  
  _Fix:_ Add date_palms/oasis_water to the grain chain flag, camel_herds/alpine_pasture to pastoral, marshlands to hunting/foraging, and give each a modest agriMod so desert/mountain food security traces to actual resources.
- **[medium] coal_deposits commodities:['timber'] hack leaks into taxonomy, local production, and the commodity map** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/resourceData.js:260-270; src/domain/worldPulse/resourceTaxonomy.js:11-14,18-29; src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:854`  
  coal_deposits declares commodities:['timber'] (resourceData.js:264) — presumably to reuse the fuel pathway. Three leaks: (1) resourceTaxonomy.textFor folds commodities into the classification text, and /timber/ is a RENEWABLE pattern, so coal deposits classify renewable/natural-recovery (verified: classifyResource('coal_deposits') → renewable) — coal seams regrow when world-pulse pressure drops; (2) deriveLocalProductionFromChains lists 'timber' as local production for a coal town (computeActiveChains.js:639-643); (3) COMMODITY_CATEGORY_MAP's 'coal'→'fuel' entry (tradeGoodsData.js:854) is dead because no resource emits a 'coal' commodity.  
  _Fix:_ Give coal_deposits commodities:['coal'] (already mapped to fuel) and add coal/peat to the NONRENEWABLE-only path; spot-check the other shoehorned commodities (magical_node/hot_springs → 'medicinal_herbs', ancient_ruins → 'trade_access').
- **[medium] Positional resources (crossroads, mountain pass) can roll 'depleted' — at generation and via world-pulse** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:91-92; src/domain/worldPulse/tierResourceDynamics.js:267-295; src/domain/worldPulse/resourceTaxonomy.js:66-74`  
  Generation's tier-weighted depletion rolls over ALL selected resources with no kind exclusion (resolveResources.js:92: 70% per resource at metropolis), and tierResourceDynamics.resourceCandidatesFor similarly considers every resource (tierResourceDynamics.js:267-295). So 'Strategic Crossroads', 'Mountain Pass', and 'Deep Natural Harbour' can be 'present_but_depleted' or get the headline 'crossroads_position may be depleted — consuming it faster than it recovers'. Taxonomy classifies these strategic/limited/manual-recovery (verified), so once depleted they never come back without DM intervention. A position cannot be consumed; for a DM this reads as engine nonsense. magical_node is also a generation-depletion candidate at 70% metro rate while recovery requires high/pervasive magic — harsher than likely intended.  
  _Fix:_ Exclude kind==='strategic' positional resources (crossroads_position, defended_pass, deep_harbour) from depletion rolls and depletion candidates, or reframe their 'depleted' state as 'contested/blockaded' with a different recovery story.
- **[medium] City+ tier bypasses the pressure gate — every city resource is a depletion candidate every tick** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/worldPulse/tierResourceDynamics.js:267-295`  
  tierResourceDynamics.js:273: state !== 'depleted' && (effectivePressure >= 0.64 || rank >= tierRank('city')). The rank clause makes EVERY resource of every city/metropolis a depletion candidate each tick regardless of actual pressure. With calm pressure ~0.2, severity ≈ 0.2*0.55 + 0.8*0.35 + 0.1 ≈ 0.49 → probability ≈ 0.05+0.49*0.34 ≈ 0.22 per resource per tick, applyMode 'auto' (below the 0.78 proposal threshold). A healthy city with 6 resources expects >1 auto-depletion per tick; exhaustibles (iron, stone, gems) never recover. Combined with generation's 55-70% city/metro depletion prior, long-running city saves trend toward all-depleted resource panels. This is the same class of runaway the corruption system got a soak-test guard for.  
  _Fix:_ Make tier raise effectivePressure (e.g. +0.1 per rank above town) rather than bypassing the >= 0.64 gate, and soak-test resource counts over ~100 ticks like the corruption loop.
- **[medium] Same-seed regen erases world-pulse/event depletion state in random mode** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:39-92; src/store/settlementSlice.js:726-768; src/domain/worldPulse/tierResourceDynamics.js:430-445`  
  Every DM edit triggers a full same-seed regen (settlementSlice.js:726-768). resolveResources' random branch ignores nearbyResourcesState entirely and overwrites nearbyResourcesDepleted with a fresh rng roll (resolveResources.js:39,92). World-pulse outcomes write both nearbyResourcesState and nearbyResourcesDepleted onto config (tierResourceDynamics.js:430-445) — and the same-seed roll reproduces only the GENERATION-time depletions, so accumulated sim history (a mine the world-pulse exhausted three ticks ago) silently un-depletes the next time the DM adds an institution or stressor. Manual mode preserves state but hits the key-form and membership bugs above. There is no branch that treats config-carried depletion as authoritative across regens.  
  _Fix:_ In the random branch, merge config.nearbyResourcesState 'depleted' entries (and nearbyResourcesDepleted) into the rolled depletion set instead of overwriting, so sim-acquired state survives regeneration.
- **[medium] deriveResourcePressure misses generation-time depletion (reads only nearbyResourcesState)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/state/deriveSystemState.js:243-263; src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:92,149`  
  deriveResourcePressure counts depleted resources solely from config.nearbyResourcesState (deriveSystemState.js:248-254). Random-mode generation — the default — records depletion only in nearbyResourcesDepleted, never in the state map. So a freshly generated metropolis with four depleted resources shows no 'N depleted resources' risk driver in the system-state dossier; the dimension only moves via the weaker vulnerable-chain proxy (lines 256-263, capped +15 vs +25). The two depletion stores disagree about which one is canonical, and each derived reader picks a different one (tierResourceDynamics reads both; deriveSystemState reads one; foodGenerator reads neither).  
  _Fix:_ Read the union of nearbyResourcesState 'depleted' entries and nearbyResourcesDepleted, ideally via one shared accessor used by all depletion consumers.

- **[low] Custom resource feedsChains can flag but never activate a chain** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:83-91,119-144`  
  Custom resources' feedsChains ids are added to chainActivatedByResource (computeActiveChains.js:86-91), but the runnable check (lines 139-142) only tests resourceActive (label-matched stock resources), resourceAvailable, substitutes, and entrepôt routes — it never consults chainActivatedByResource. - **[low] 'Abundant' resource state has no downstream effect** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/resolveResources.js:104-110; src/components/ConfigurationPanel.jsx:143-149; src/domain/worldPulse/tierResourceDynamics.js:321`

- **[low] SPECIAL_RESOURCES is runtime-dead and bizarrely re-exported as RELATION_TYPES** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/resourceData.js:604-686; src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:34; src/generators/structuralValidator.js:15-16`

- **[low] Commodity vocabulary half-orphaned on both sides of COMMODITY_CATEGORY_MAP** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:834-866; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:826-857; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:636-651`  
  RESOURCE_DATA emits commodities with no COMMODITY_CATEGORY_MAP entry — maritime_access, trade_access, processed_textiles, luxury, gems, honey, medicinal_herbs, furs, water, dates, glass — so they pass through getInstitutionEconomicBonus as raw strings (economicGenerator.js:829-844) and deriveLocalProductionFromChains prints 'trade access' / 'maritime access' as locally produced commodities (computeActiveChains.js:639-643), which reads oddly in the dossier. Conversely the map carries producer-less keys: flax, silk cocoons, silver, gold, amber, clay, coal, game meat, forest herbs, raw leather, candle wax (tradeGoodsData.js:834-866) — vocabulary from a producer set that no longer exists.  
  _Fix:_ Reconcile the two vocabularies once: map every RESOURCE_DATA commodity, drop dead keys, and exclude access-type commodities (trade_access, maritime_access) from 'local production' display.
- **[medium] Magic is damage-control only, never a booster; food's two magic terms disagree** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:24-109; src/generators/foodGenerator.js:96-104,160-167; src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:136-144`  
  The owner wants magic as supply-chain supplement AND booster. The substitution pass only fires on impaired/depleted chains (chainMagicSubstitution.js:31-32,71-72,101-103) — a healthy grain chain near a magical_node gets nothing; magical_node feeds only magic-presence defense (priorityHelpers.js:141), institution selection bias, and the arcane chains. In food, two parallel magic variables exist: magicSupplement (tier/tradition-scaled, foodGenerator.js:98-104) feeds the foodLedger and the narrative note but NOT the deficit math; magicOffset (different thresholds, lines 161-167) feeds the math but not the ledger. An arcane town at priorityMagic 40 reports a positive magicSupplement in the ledger while magicOffset is 0 (needs ≥50) — the receipt and the computation disagree. Neither term reads magical_node.  
  _Fix:_ Unify on one magic-food term consumed by both ledger and math; add a small healthy-chain booster (e.g. magical_node or magically_sustained traditions add +0.05-0.1 agriMod / one extra export) so magic supplements rather than only rescues.
- **[low] Magically-sustained status can be silently overwritten by the second upstream pass** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:278-334; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:62-66`  
  applyMagicSubstitution runs before the multi-order upstream resolution (computeActiveChains.js:279-334). The second propagation pass skips chains already 'vulnerable'/'impaired' (line 323) but not 'magically_sustained', so a druid-sustained brewing chain whose grain upstream is impaired gets downgraded back to 'vulnerable', losing the magicNote framing the DM just earned. The order comment says substitution runs first 'so magic recovery already applied' — but the later pass undoes it.  
  _Fix:_ Treat 'magically_sustained' as terminal in both upstream passes (skip alongside vulnerable/impaired).
- **[low] Salt flats classify as exhaustible-with-manual-recovery** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/worldPulse/resourceTaxonomy.js:11-14; src/data/resourceData.js:62-72`  
  classifyResource('salt_flats') → nonrenewable/exhaustible/manual (verified) because /salt/ is a NONRENEWABLE pattern and nothing in its text matches a renewable pattern. Coastal evaporation pans are the textbook renewable resource — sun and tide refill them. Once world-pulse depletes a salt town's flats they never recover without DM action, while the neighboring fishery bounces back naturally. desert_salt (ancient seabed deposits) being exhaustible is fine; the shared /salt/ pattern just overreaches for the coastal variant.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'evaporation|pans' to the renewable patterns or special-case salt_flats as managed/natural.

Strengths: Label-to-key fuzzy resolution is fully correct: all 52 chain.resource labels in SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS resolve to the intended RESOURCE_DATA key (verified by executing resourceLabelToKey against every chain), including tricky cases like 'Mountain Pass'->defended_pass and 'Coastal Timber'->shipbuilding_timber.; Every one of the 33 RESOURCE_DATA resources has a RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS entry, instBoosts that (with the noted mason/caravanserai-class exceptions) match real catalog institution names, tradeGoods consumed by the export deriver, and commodities consumed by localProduction — the core resource->institution->chain->good loop is genuinely closed.; The extraction/processing gate system (RESOURCE_EXTRACTION_GATES, RESOURCE_GOOD_INST_GATES, CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES in computeActiveChains.js:352-444) is excellent DM-grade realism: no iron-ore exports without a mine, no flour exports under the external-mill banalite (with a historically literate note), surface-collectable resources deliberately ungated.; Depletion is respected consistently on the trade side: depleted resources are skipped for raw exports, depleted-chain outputs are withheld, and town+ settlements gain matching imports ('Iron ore — local mines exhausted') — a coherent consequence loop.; resolveResources emits per-resource causal traces (terrain-specific cause, depletion-roll cause, instBoost downstream effects) — the 'why is this a fishing town' receipt the product thesis demands.; Magic substitution is well-tiered (druid > divine > arcane rates per chain family, priority thresholds, tier gates) and magically-sustained chains correctly become non-exportable — subsistence miracles don't create export economies.; The water-terrain override in getCompatibleResources (coastal road hamlet can still fish, river-only resources stay river-locked) and the terrain-weighted route pools in resolveConfig are thoughtful terrain-to-economy coherence.; The resource taxonomy (renewable/managed/exhaustible/strategic/magical with recovery modes, magical recovery requiring high magic) is a strong DM-facing concept that the world-pulse recovery path actually honors via canRecoverResource.

### cross-mapping-matrix

Verdict on the headline question: the matrix is about 70% clean at the joins that matter most (institutions -> services, resources -> institutions, institutions+resources -> chains -> exports/imports, institutions -> income/power flags), but it is held together by substring matching over free-string names with no validation layer, and every join has leaks. The strongest path is config -> resources -> institution biasing -> chains -> exports/imports/income, which is genuinely causal with honest receipts (extraction/processing gates, the external-mill banalité note, stress reshaping). The weakest areas: (1) the entrepôt layer is dead — seven chains (spices, silk, finance, luxury, magical goods, planar, smuggling) have empty processor lists and can never activate, so 'magic as a trade booster' exists only in income sources, not in chains; (2) the reverse resource->chain index is rotten (9 dead chain ids, ~29 chains never resource-flagged, all desert/mountain chains orphaned); (3) magic substitution emits a status ('magically_sustained') the canonical chain-state vocabulary doesn't recognize, so magically-sustained chains read as 'stable' downstream — the one receipt the owner explicitly asked about is lost; (4) several religion/healing/governance chains list nonsense processors (almshouses run parishes, bathhouses run courts); (5) subsumption logic sometimes deletes upstream producers its own chains depend on (smelter removes charcoal burner and mine; butchers remove shepherds; merchant guilds remove the salt works), and substring matching makes a cathedral erase all parish-church districts; (6) a legacy third vocabulary (RESOURCE_CHAINS/SPECIAL_RESOURCES in resourceGenerator) still feeds the narrative step with phantom data. Services map to institutions nearly exhaustively (1 orphan of 270) but through a half-rotten override table (57 dead redirect targets) and two divergent rule paths. Most fixes are data alignment plus one build-time join validator; the architecture itself (gates, ledgers, traces, demand-gap model) is sound and worth keeping.

- **[high] Entrepôt/magic/criminal chains can never activate (empty processor lists)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:534,651,667,684,1052,1074,1213 and src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117`  
  computeActiveChains requires at least one matched processing institution (matchedInsts.length===0 -> return). Seven chains declare processingInstitutions: [] and therefore can NEVER appear: manufacturing.luxury_goods, trade_entrepot.spices_dyes, trade_entrepot.silk_luxury_textiles, trade_entrepot.transit_finance, arcane_magical.magical_goods, arcane_magical.planar, criminal_economy.smuggling. The entire entrepôt model the data file documents (entrepotNote prose about ports/crossroads profiting from spice, silk, finance, magical-item and planar flows) is dead, as is the smuggling chain. For the owner's magic question: the two chains that make magic a trade BOOSTER (Magical Items & Enchanting, Planar Trade) never fire even with a magical_node + Mages' district + port.  
  _Fix:_ Give each chain real processors (e.g. luxury_goods: Jeweller/Specialized metalworkers/Luxury goods quarter; transit_finance: Banking houses/Banking district; magical_goods: Enchanter's shop/Mages' district; planar: Planar traders/Planar embassy; smuggling: Smuggling operation/network/waypoint), or special-case entrepot-only chains to activate on route+logistics institutions.
- **[high] RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS points at nonexistent chain ids; desert/mountain resources orphaned** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1472-1568`  
  Reverse index entries reference need-categories that don't exist: 'agricultural.food_processing', 'agricultural.brewing', 'agricultural.livestock', 'agricultural.textiles', 'services.hospital'; and 'food_security.beekeeping_wax' (chain lives under manufacturing). Result: date_palms, desert_salt, camel_herds, alpine_pasture, hot_springs_mineral activate nothing or the wrong thing (oasis_water -> raw_extraction.clay!), and foraging_areas/ancient_grove never light up beekeeping. Symmetrically, ~29 chains are never referenced by any resource (all the dedicated desert/mountain chains: alpine_wool, mountain_timber_harvest, oasis_agriculture, date_palm_harvest, desert_glasswork, camel_caravan...), so they can run but never reach 'running'/activatedByResource status — the DM-facing receipt says 'operational' instead of 'running off the Alpine Pastures you selected'.  
  _Fix:_ Fix the five dead prefixes to real ids and add reverse-index entries for every chain whose resource exists (validate in a test: every RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS value resolves to a needKey.chainId; every chain with a resource appears in the index).
- **[high] Magic substitution status 'magically_sustained' is unknown to the canonical chain-state vocabulary** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83 vs src/domain/supplyChainState.js:57-79,294-297`  
  chainMagicSubstitution sets chain.status='magically_sustained' when druidic/divine/arcane traditions rescue an impaired/depleted chain. supplyChainState.canonicalSupplyChainStatus knows only operational/running/entrepot/vulnerable/impaired and defaults unknown values to 'stable'. So the exact state the owner cares about — magic supplementing a supply chain — reads downstream as a perfectly stable chain; the purpose-built canonical status 'substituted' is unreachable, and inferSubstitutes only checks chain.substituteActive, which magic substitution never sets (it sets magicNote/magicRecovery). The dossier/AI overlay loses the 'this town eats because druids bless the fields' receipt. Also computeActiveChains' sort rank map lacks the status (sorts last, rank 5).  
  _Fix:_ Map 'magically_sustained' -> 'substituted' in LEGACY_TO_CANONICAL, set substituteActive=true in applyMagicSubstitution, and surface magicNote in inferSubstitutes.
- **[high] Religion/healing/governance/tavern chains list nonsense processors — churches, hospitals, courts not in their own chains** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:911,926,1100,1122,1161`  
  religion_civic.parish is 'processed' by Almshouse and Foundling home — no parish church, cathedral, or monastery, so a thorp with 'Access to parish church' shows no parish chain while a city's chain credits the orphanage. healing_medicine.hospital is processed by Almshouse/Foundling home, never Small/Major hospital or Hospital network (a city with a Major hospital but no almshouse has no hospital chain). divine_healing's only processor is Foundling home. law_governance is processed by Workhouse and Public bathhouse — not Courthouse/Town hall/City hall. tavern_social only matches 'Inns and taverns (district)' + Public bathhouse, so village inns/taverns never form the chain. These are exactly the receipts a DM reads.  
  _Fix:_ Replace processor lists with the real institutions (parish: Parish church variants/Cathedral/Monastery; hospital: Small/Major hospital, Hospital network; law: Courthouse/Town hall/City hall/Multiple courthouses; tavern_social: Inn/Travelers' inn/Taverns (5-20)).
- **[high] Subsumption deletes upstream producers its own chains depend on** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:42,61,64-68`  
  Rules treat complements as substitutes: Smelter removes Charcoal burner AND Mine (open cast) — but the fuel chain's processors are exactly Charcoal burner/Peat cutter and CHAIN_DEPS marks smelting dependent on fuel, so building a smelter kills its own fuel source and triggers 'Needs imported Charcoal and fuel'. Butchers (3-8) remove Dairy farmer and Shepherd (livestock/alpine-wool/textiles processors); Merchant guilds (3-8) remove Salt works (the salt chain's ONLY processor — the salt chain dies when a merchant guild appears) and Vintner (wine_spirits processor); Craft guilds (5-15) remove Dairy farmer. A bigger downstream institution should never erase the upstream producer it buys from.  
  _Fix:_ Delete these rules (or convert to 'employs/absorbs' annotations). Add a guard test: no SUBSUMPTION_RULES lesser may appear in any chain's processingInstitutions unless the greater also matches that chain.
- **[medium] Substring subsumption: a cathedral erases all parish-church districts** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:25,81-91`  
  applySubsumption matches lesser names with includes(): rule {greater:'cathedral', lesser:['parish church',...]} removes not just 'Parish church' but 'Parish churches (2-5)', 'Parish churches (10-30)', and 'Parish churches (50-100+)' because each contains the substring 'parish church'. A metropolis with a Great cathedral loses its 50-100 parish churches — historically backwards (cathedral cities had the MOST parishes) and it strips the religious institutions other systems key on (religion income, INSTITUTION_FINISHED_GOODS_DEMAND.religious consumers, getInstitutionNames.hasChurch is saved only by the cathedral itself).  
  _Fix:_ Match lesser names exactly (case-insensitive equality), and scope the cathedral rule to the singular village 'Parish church'/'Wayside shrine' only.
- **[low] Dead subsumption rules (name mismatches / institutions that don't exist)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:21,30,50,60`  
  Four rules can never fire: greater 'mages district' never matches catalog "Mages' district" (apostrophe); greater 'university' — no University institution exists anywhere in the catalog; lesser 'stone quarry (hamlet)' and lesser 'pit fights' name institutions that don't exist (catalog has 'Fighting pits'). The mages-district rule's absence means a Mages' district city keeps a redundant Wizard's tower + Mages' guild + Alchemist quarter stack the rule was written to clean up.  
  _Fix:_ Fix the apostrophe ("mages' district"), change 'pit fights' to 'fighting pits', and remove the university/stone-quarry-(hamlet) rules or add those institutions.
- **[medium] Leather exports die when Tannery is subsumed by Tanner (established)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:409-413,359 and src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:38`  
  CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES and RESOURCE_GOOD_INST_GATES gate 'Leather goods', 'Leather armour', 'Boots and shoes', 'Saddles and harness', 'Tanned leather' on an institution whose name contains 'tannery'. Subsumption rule {greater:'tanner (established)', lesser:['tannery']} removes Tannery when the LARGER Tanner (established) is present — and 'tanner (established)' does not contain the substring 'tannery', so every leather output is export-blocked precisely when the settlement upgrades its tanning industry. Same family of bugs as the case-sensitive goods gates: two subsystems using different name vocabularies for the same concept.  
  _Fix:_ Gate on 'tanner' (matches both) or use a keyword list ['tannery','tanner'].
- **[medium] 'mason' gate keyword matches no institution — 'Building materials' can never be exported** (mapping_gap) — `C:/users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:361,427,434 and src/data/resourceData.js:111,232`  
  RESOURCE_GOOD_INST_GATES stone_quarry gates 'Building materials' on 'mason'; CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES gates 'Building materials' on 'mason' and 'Quarried stone' on ['quarry','mason','stonemason']. The catalog contains NO institution whose name includes 'mason' or 'stonemason' at any tier (verified). 'Quarried stone' survives via 'quarry', but the 'Building materials' trade good is permanently gated off. resourceData instBoosts mason/stonemason (river_clay, stone_quarry) are likewise orphan boosts that bias nothing.

- **[medium] Case-mismatched requiredInstitution names silently kill seven tier goods** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/tradeGoodsData.js:477,484,491,498 (and village/town entries); src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1158-1164`  
  getGoodsModifiers compares requiredInstitution case-sensitively (w.name === reqInst || w.name.includes(reqInst)). GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER names "Hunter's Lodge", "Charcoal Burner", "Peat Cutter", "Fisher's Landing", "Dairy Farmer", "Cobbler's Guild", "Tailor's Guild" — the catalog spells them "Hunter's lodge", "Charcoal burner", "Peat cutter", "Fisher's landing", "Dairy farmer", "Cobbler's guild", "Tailor's guild". The gate therefore always fails and Game meat, Charcoal, Peat fuel, Fresh fish (hamlet), Fresh milk and dairy (village), Quality boots and shoes, Finished garments (town) never enter v.exports. Today v.exports mostly feeds income-source attribution (chain exports overwrite the list), so the visible damage is missing income labels — but it's a pure vocabulary bug.  
  _Fix:_ Lowercase both sides of the comparison, and add a test asserting every requiredInstitution resolves against the catalog.
- **[high] Legacy RESOURCE_CHAINS analysis runs on a third vocabulary — mostly dead, and fed the wrong resource list** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/resourceGenerator.js:18-26,35-44,169-188; src/generators/steps/generateNarratives.js:31-34; src/data/resourceData.js:424-686`  
  resourceGenerator's evaluateEconomicActivity tests nearbyResources.includes(chain.rawResource) where rawResource is a commodity word ('wool','iron ore','fish') that is never a RESOURCE_DATA key — only the 7 terrain-specific chains whose rawResource happens to be a real key can ever activate. evaluateInstitutions then requires EXACT name equality against processors like "Weavers' guild", 'Fulling mill', 'Cheesemaker', 'Salters' guild' — none exist in the catalog, so even activated chains read 'unexploited'. Worse, generateNarratives calls it with TERRAIN_DATA.allowedResources.slice(0,7) (a mixed commodity/key pool) instead of the settlement's actual nearbyResources, and always passes specialResources=[] so SPECIAL_RESOURCES/evaluateResourceChain never runs (its INSTITUTION_TAGS.MAGIC reference is undefined anyway). The resourceAnalysis narrative is built on phantom data.  
  _Fix:_ Either retire resourceGenerator/RESOURCE_CHAINS in favor of computeActiveChains output (the narrative step can read economicState.activeChains), or translate it to RESOURCE_DATA keys + catalog names and feed it config.nearbyResources.
- **[medium] Canonical arcane-institution regex misses Mages' guild, Mages' district, Academy of magic** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/magicLedger.js:26 (consumed at src/domain/capacityModel.js:599, src/domain/magicProfile.js:25)`  
  magicLedger's ARCANE_INSTITUTION_PATTERN /(tower|sanctum|college|conclave|circle|guild.*mage|enclave|atheneum|library.*arcane)/i — billed as 'one source of truth' for the conserved-ledger refactor — fails on the catalog's flagship arcane institutions: "Mages' guild" and "Mages' district" (the alternation requires 'guild' BEFORE 'mage'), and 'Academy of magic' (no 'academy' token). It false-positives 'Bardic college' (entertainment), 'Druid Circle' is debatable, and 'Teleportation circle' matches. capacityModel.deriveMagical and magicProfile both consume it, so a city whose magic rests on a Mages' district contributes no institutional arcane supply while a bardic college does.  
  _Fix:_ Use /(tower|sanctum|college|conclave|circle|mages?[''s]*\s*(guild|district)|academy of magic|enclave|atheneum|library.*arcane)/i and exclude 'bardic college'; add a fixture test against catalog names.
- **[low] worldPulse magic recovery scores a stale magicLevel vocabulary** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/worldPulse/resourceTaxonomy.js:31-38,90-99`  
  resourceTaxonomy.magicLevelScore awards points for magicLevel 'pervasive' (4), 'high' (3), 'common' (2), 'moderate' (1) — but the generator emits only none/low/medium/high (magicLedger.js explicitly documents pervasive/common/moderate as the stale lens vocabulary it folds away). Net effect: magical resource recovery (ley nodes) requires exactly 'high'; a 'medium' world scores 0 and the three dead words can never occur. The intent (graded recovery) is unreachable.  
  _Fix:_ Score the canonical bands (high=3, medium=1) or read magicLedger(settlement).priorityMagic directly.
- **[medium] servicesGenerator's no-magic gate is a tautology — magic services survive priorityMagic=0** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1938 vs src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:111 and steps/resolveConfig.js:68`  
  const _noMagicSvcs = d.magicExists === false || (d.priorityMagic || 50) === 0 — the second clause can never be true: priorityMagic=0 is falsy, so (0||50)===0 is false. computeActiveChains uses the correct form (magicPriority === 0) and resolveConfig computes noMagic correctly ((config.priorityMagic || 0) === 0). So with priorityMagic=0 but magicExists undefined, arcane CHAINS are suppressed while arcane SERVICES still render — the two halves of the dossier disagree about whether magic exists. (Mitigated only when callers consistently pass magicExists:false.)  
  _Fix:_ Change to (d.priorityMagic ?? 50) === 0, or better, thread the resolveConfig noMagic flag through.
- **[medium] Exact-match and fuzzy-match service paths apply different rules to the same data** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:812-830 vs 860-903`  
  getServicesForInstitution has two code paths. Fuzzy path: p>=1 services always included, requiredTradeRoute honored, {allow,force} object overrides supported, and a guaranteed at-least-one-service fallback. Exact path (taken for ~116 catalog institutions whose names equal an INSTITUTION_SERVICES key): every service rolls _rng() < p * tierChance even at p=1.0 (a village Mill has a 50% chance of offering NO grain milling), requiredTradeRoute ignored, object-form overrides break (treated as truthy boolean), no fallback. Which ruleset an institution gets is an accident of key spelling. Also lines 819-820 compute the same toggle key twice (M and A identical) — the canonical-key variant was lost.  
  _Fix:_ Collapse both paths into one implementation (resolve key first, then one shared roll/override/fallback block).
- **[medium] LOCALE_SERVICE_OVERRIDES: 57 redirects target service keys that don't exist, bypassing exact blocks** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/servicesData.js (override table) and src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:806,812,855`  
  57 override targets ('Black Market', 'Town Watch', 'Great Library', 'Merchant Warehouses', 'Docks/Port Facilities', 'Banking District', 'Hedge Wizard', 'Smuggling Operation', 'Street Gang', 'Red Light District', 'Gambling Den', 'Mercenary Quarter', 'Planar Embassy', 'Golem Workforce'...) are Title-Case keys absent from INSTITUTION_SERVICES — the real keys exist in catalog casing ('Black market', 'Town watch', ...). Because getServicesForInstitution skips the exact-match path whenever ANY override exists (the !l guard), these institutions are diverted past their own exact service blocks into fuzzy matching, which usually-but-not-provably lands back on the right block. The override layer is half-rotten and silently changes which rule path (see exact/fuzzy finding) applies.  
  _Fix:_ Normalize override targets to real keys (case-insensitive resolve) and add a test that every override target exists in INSTITUTION_SERVICES.
- **[medium] Semantically wrong service redirects: carpenters get blacksmith services, aqueducts get tavern services** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/servicesData.js:19-20,68,158,201,226 and granary entries`  
  Overrides that shoehorn institutions into the wrong service block, producing DM-visible wrong receipts: 'carpenter (part-time)'/'carpenters (5-15)' -> Blacksmith (a carpenter offering Horseshoeing and Armour repair); 'aqueduct or water system' -> Inn/Tavern and 'advanced water infrastructure' -> Inn/Tavern District (water infrastructure selling Lodging and Meals); 'teleportation circle' -> Airship; 'bakers (5-15)' and 'subsistence farming' -> Mill (bakers offering 'Sawing timber'; subsistence farmers offering milling that the thorp's own catalog entry says is illegal at home); 'town granary'/'city granaries'/'state granary complex' -> 'Merchant Warehouses' which doesn't exist (falls to fuzzy).  
  _Fix:_ Author small dedicated service blocks (Carpenter, Waterworks, Granary, Bakery, Teleportation circle) instead of redirecting to the nearest-looking block.
- **[medium] Chain 'services' tags use a vocabulary no consumer recognizes** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:368,394,407,420,433,446,771,785,799,871`  
  Chains tag the service categories they support, but many values aren't in the canonical 11-bucket service vocabulary (lodging/food/equipment/magic/information/healing/transport/legal/employment/entertainment/criminal): 'crafts' (river_milling, desert_glasswork), 'construction'+'fuel' (mountain_timber_harvest), 'textiles' (alpine_wool), 'trade' (oasis_agriculture, date_palm_harvest, crossroads_trade, camel_caravan), 'military' (shipbuilding#2, mountain_pass_trade), 'security' (adventuring_escort). chain.services is carried through computeActiveChains and deriveSupplyChainState verbatim, so any consumer keying on category names silently drops these. Nothing validates the join.  
  _Fix:_ Map to the canonical buckets (crafts/textiles/construction -> equipment; fuel -> equipment; trade -> legal or transport; military/security -> employment) and add an enum check.
- **[low] Institutions listed as chain OUTPUTS (goods)** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:927,1036-1039,1432-1435`  
  arcane_magical.spellcasting lists "Wizard's tower" and "Mages' guild" among its outputs; healing_medicine.divine_healing outputs include "Mages' guild"; ITEM_CATEGORIES.service likewise lists "Wizard's tower" and "Mages' guild" as service items. Since deriveExportsFromChains exports outputs.slice(0,2), a spellcasting settlement can show the building 'Mages' guild' as a trade export. Category error between institution and good vocabularies.  
  _Fix:_ Replace with real outputs ('Spellcasting services', 'Divine healing') and add a validator that no chain output equals a catalog institution name.
- **[medium] Duplicate chain id 'shipbuilding' inside raw_extraction** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:292,347 (and 56-135 fish/fishing); src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:240`  
  Two chains share id 'shipbuilding' (Managed woodland river version at line 292; Coastal Timber version at line 347). Both can be active simultaneously (two rows with the same chainId), chainById/Object.fromEntries keeps only the last for CHAIN_DEPS upstream propagation, RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS 'raw_extraction.shipbuilding' is ambiguous, and chainMagicSubstitution's TIMBER_CHAIN_IDS treats them as one. Also redundant overlapping chains 'fish' vs 'fishing' (both resource 'Fishing grounds', near-identical) produce doubled fish rows in the dossier.  
  _Fix:_ Rename the coastal one 'coastal_shipbuilding' (updating RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS/CHAIN_DEPS) and merge the fish/fishing twins.
- **[low] '(transit)' export label fires for local production on non-hub routes** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:514-517`  
  deriveExportsFromChains step 3 appends '<output> (transit)' for EVERY active entrepot-flagged chain regardless of trade route. Entrepot-only chains are route-gated at activation, but chains with a resource + entrepot:true (salt, furs_north, camel_caravan, magical_goods if ever fixed) activate via local resource on a plain road — a salt-flat village on a road exports 'Preserved foods (transit)' although nothing transits anything. The transit receipt contradicts the route.  
  _Fix:_ Gate step 3 on ['crossroads','port','river'].includes(route).
- **[medium] supplyChainState beneficiary/victim heuristics keyed to wrong needKeys** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:107-155`  
  NEED_HEURISTICS keys 'trade', 'energy', 'arcane' match no needKey (actual keys: trade_entrepot, arcane_magical; there is no energy category — fuel lives in raw_extraction), so those three entries are dead config. And eight real categories (trade_entrepot, arcane_magical, defense_security, healing_medicine, knowledge_information, religion_civic, entertainment_culture, criminal_economy) have no entry, so every such chain reports generic 'settlement residents' as both beneficiaries and victims and a stock failure consequence — flattening exactly the 'who profits / who suffers' receipts this adapter exists to provide.  
  _Fix:_ Rekey to the real SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS keys and fill the missing eight.
- **[medium] Tier import tables: city/metropolis branches unreachable (route vs tier vocabulary)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1385-1406 (and servicesGenerator.js:426)`  
  getUpgradeChain selects the goods-source branch with (route === 'city' || route === 'metropolis') — but route is the trade-route vocabulary (road/river/port/crossroads/isolated/mountain_pass), never a tier name. So UPGRADE_GOODS_BY_TIER.town.fromCityOrMetropolis (luxury textiles, spices, banking services), city.fromMetropolis (international banking, political legitimacy), and village.fromHigher (isFromHigher is always passed false) are unreachable; towns/cities always take fromHinterland. These imports feed v.imports and, for entrepôts, the returned 'transit' list — so crossroads towns show hinterland staples as their transit goods and never the luxury flows the table intended. The parallel _UPGRADE_CHAINS copy in servicesGenerator (line 426) is entirely dead.  
  _Fix:_ Branch on neighbour tier or settlement tier (e.g. fromCityOrMetropolis when a larger neighbour exists), and delete the dead copy.
- **[low] Dead parallel goods/services tables and dead income-stream twin** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:860-899,946-965,1450-1486; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:491; src/data/supplyChainData.js:1278; src/generators/structuralValidator.js:16`  
  Four parallel near-identical data tables exist for the same concepts, two of them dead: SERVICE_TIER_DATA (servicesGenerator) duplicates GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER (tradeGoodsData) with defaultEnabled instead of on; its only generator consumer is getHistoryModifiers, which reads h.on (undefined for this table) — and getHistoryModifiers' sole caller _computeIncomeStreams has no callers. _getUpgradeOpps is a byte-identical dead twin of getUpgradeOpportunities. ITEM_CATEGORIES in supplyChainData (190 lines) is neither exported nor referenced. structuralValidator re-exports SPECIAL_RESOURCES under the name RELATION_TYPES ('so existing importers don't break') — semantically wrong aliasing waiting to confuse.  
  _Fix:_ Delete _computeIncomeStreams/getHistoryModifiers/_getUpgradeOpps/ITEM_CATEGORIES/_UPGRADE_CHAINS; make TradeDynamicsPanel read GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER so one table remains.
- **[medium] priorityCategory miscoding: 34 craft institutions tagged 'government'; 'religion' never matches 'religious'; 'noble' matches nothing** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:171-197 (pattern repeats across tiers); src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1434-1437; src/generators/npcGenerator.js:1240-1250`  
  Catalog priorityCategory distribution shows systematic mistagging: 34 Crafts institutions (Hunter's lodge, Charcoal burner, Maltster, Peat cutter, Stable yard, ...) carry priorityCategory:'government'. Consumer getUpgradeOpportunities (NPC role candidates from HISTORY_EVENTS) treats a settlement as eligible for government-category roles if any institution has priorityCategory==='government' — so a hamlet whose only 'government' is a peat cutter spawns government NPC roles. HISTORY_EVENTS key 'religious' never equals priorityCategory 'religion' (saved only by the category-name fallback), and key 'noble' matches no catalog category or priorityCategory (noble roles are injected separately in npcGenerator, making the HISTORY_EVENTS.noble block dead there).  
  _Fix:_ Re-tag the 34 craft entries to 'crafts'/'economy', rename 'religion'->'religious' (or normalize in the comparator), and remove or wire the noble block.
- **[low] Service display categories shoehorn food into 'equipment' and religion/commerce into 'healing'/'legal'** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:1194-1456 (map), 952-1192 (defaults), 1460-1472 (bucket list)`  
  SERVICE_CATEGORY_MAP buckets are missing 'commerce' and 'religion', so: Butter, Honey, Soft cheese, Fresh fish, Game meat, Salted fish, 'Ale (barrel/jug)', 'Salt for preservation' -> equipment (while 'Meals and drink' -> food); 'Religious services', Sanctuary, 'Poor relief', Alms -> healing; markets, banks, granaries, auction houses, mints, money changers, 'Trade facilitation', Loans, 'Deposit accounts' -> legal. A DM scanning the services panel finds the brewery's ale under Equipment and the cathedral's mass under Healing. INSTITUTION_DEFAULT_CATEGORY mirrors the same shoehorning ('Town granary': legal, 'Parish church': healing, 'Brewer': food but 'Vintner': equipment).  
  _Fix:_ Add 'commerce' and 'religion' buckets (or rename 'legal' -> 'trade & law') and re-bucket consumable goods under food.
- **[low] Institution -> service coverage: one orphan institution; several unreachable service blocks** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/institutionServices.js (orphan keys); src/data/institutionalCatalog.js:95-101; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:725-731,744-750`  
  Of 270 catalog institutions, exactly one ('Communal root cellar') resolves to no service block at all (override/exact/fuzzy) — acceptable but unflagged. In the other direction, INSTITUTION_SERVICES blocks 'University', 'Spellcasting Services', 'Navy', 'Magic Item', 'Monster Part Dealers', 'Grove Shrine', 'Mining settlement' are reachable by no catalog institution via override or exact match (University/Specialist-craftsmen-quarters also break SERVICE_TIER_DATA's metropolis requiredInstitution gates, since neither exists in the catalog). Authored service content that can never surface.  
  _Fix:_ Add a root-cellar service (food storage), and either add University/Grove Shrine/etc. to the catalog or retarget their blocks to existing institutions.
- **[low] Loose 12-char prefix matching creates false chain processors** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117,193-197; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:73-105`  
  computeActiveChains matches processors with instNames.some(n => n.includes(p.toLowerCase().slice(0,12))) — generous substring matching produces false joins: 'Specialized craftsmen quarters' (glass_print) matches 'Specialized metalworkers'; 'Mill' matches 'Sawmill' and (explicitly patched around) 'Access to external mill'; 'Wizard Tower' fails on "Wizard's tower" (apostrophe) while 'Mills (2-5)' matches anything containing 'mills (2-5)'. The same slice trick in tradeDependency matching (slice(0,10)) and computeFactionPowers (slice(0,8)/slice(0,6)) makes the institution<->resource joins approximate in ways nobody validates. Cooper is a 'processor' of livestock and fish chains (a barrel maker neither raises cattle nor catches fish — gameable, but a receipt smell).  
  _Fix:_ Normalize names (strip punctuation, lowercase) and match whole names or curated keyword arrays; add a build-time check that every processingInstitution matches >=1 catalog name.
- **[low] Unmatched chain processors that should match existing institutions** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:46,156,472,519,570,599,820,835,949,993,1016,1175`  
  Processors naming institutions that don't exist under any spelling, so they contribute nothing: 'Horse market' (livestock), 'Village brewhouse' (brewing — the catalog has Brewer/Brewery/Alehouse, two of which are already listed, so minor), "Dyers' workshop" (textiles — catalog has 'Dyer'), 'Armourers' (weapons_armor), "Bowyer's shop"/'Specialist craftsmen' (bowyer_fletcher — catalog: 'Bowyer & fletcher', 'Specialist craftsmen quarters' absent), 'Leatherworkers' (leather_goods), 'Barracks (town)'/'City guard district' (garrison — catalog: 'Barracks'), 'City wall district'/'Town fortifications' (fortification — catalog: 'Town walls'/'City walls and gates'), 'Wizard Tower' (alchemy), 'Inn/Tavern District' (performance), 'Cartographers guild' vs "Cartographer's guild" spelled both ways across two chains.  
  _Fix:_ Align each to catalog spellings; enforce with the same build-time join check.
- **[low] Salt-need check misses desert salt; coal resource declares 'timber' commodity** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:912-915; src/data/resourceData.js:264,297,287`  
  getInstitutionServices flags a Salt import when nearbyResources lack 'salt_flat|salt_deposit|salt_mine' — 'desert_salt' (Salt Pans, explicitly 'major trade commodity') doesn't match, so a desert settlement sitting on salt pans is told to import salt. Separately, coal_deposits declares commodities:['timber'], so deriveLocalProductionFromChains lists 'timber' as the local production of a coal seam (the comment-free legacy of a copy-paste); magical_node and hot_springs both declare 'medicinal_herbs' as their commodity, so a ley-line node 'produces' herbs.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'desert_salt' to the salt check; give coal_deposits commodities:['coal','peat'] (add to COMMODITY vocabulary) and magical_node something arcane.
- **[medium] DM-expected mapping missing: services and chains never feed power/factions; chain.services is produced but never consumed** (missing) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:177; src/domain/supplyChainState.js:261-266,345; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:480-592`  
  The matrix has one-way joins where a DM would expect feedback: (a) generated services (generateAvailableServices) are display-only — no income source, faction, or capacity reads them; (b) chain.services tags are carried through computeActiveChains and deriveSupplyChainState but no consumer keys on them (compounded by the vocabulary mismatch finding); (c) active chains never influence powerStructure/factions — a town whose entire economy is one salt chain has no 'salt consortium' pressure; faction<->economy correlation runs off institution keywords only. Given the audience, (c) is the gap a DM feels: 'who controls the grain?' is answered by inferController picking the first processor string, not by the faction system.  
  _Fix:_ Feed dominant chains into faction generation (controller -> faction seat) and either consume chain.services (service availability boost) or drop the field.
- **[low] Magic-gate thresholds differ at every layer of the same dial** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/priorityHelpers.js:172-182; computeActiveChains.js:68-75,111; institutionProbability.js:156-177`  
  The magic slider gates differently per subsystem: chains suppress arcane only at exactly 0 (computeActiveChains:111); institutions zero hi-magic infra below 66 (institutionProbability:158-166) and scale others by slider*tierPenalty; income tiers gate at 15/35/65 (economicGenerator:1765-1815); chain traditions gate druid>=30, arcane>=35/50/55/65, alchemy>=15 (computeActiveChains:68-75, chainMagicSubstitution); hasTeleportationInfra ignores the slider entirely (priorityHelpers:172-182) despite its docstring claiming a >=66 requirement. Mostly intentional layering, but the docstring/behavior mismatch on hasTeleportationInfra and the 0-vs-low discontinuity (slider=1 behaves like 50 for chains) are incoherent edges a DM can hit by sliding magic to 'almost none'.  
  _Fix:_ Define named thresholds in constants.js (MAGIC_NONE=0, MAGIC_LOW=25, MAGIC_HIGH=66) and make hasTeleportationInfra honor its documented slider gate.

Strengths: The chain activation core (computeActiveChains) is genuinely causal and DM-explainable when its data is right: tier gates, resource activation, substitutes, depletion, extraction gates (no iron exports without a mine), processing gates (no flour exports without a mill), and the external-mill 'banalité' note (grain milled at the lord's mill cannot be exported) is exactly the kind of honest receipt the product promises.; INSTITUTION_FINISHED_GOODS_DEMAND is the best join in the system: tolerant lowercase matching, mixed institution/resource suppliers, graded import labels by gap size, export bonuses on surplus, and custom-content supply integration — a model for how the other joins should be written.; Magic-as-supplement is well designed where it's wired: chainMagicSubstitution gives tradition-specific recovery rates with flavour notes and sets exportable=false (magic sustains subsistence but doesn't industrialize exports); the three-tier magic income model (apothecary -> spellcasting -> arcane industry, with the Enchanted Goods Premium cross-boost on smiths/jewellers) and teleportation-replaces-trade-routes logic are threaded consistently through economy, viability, dependency, and prosperity code.; The conserved-ledger pattern (foodLedger/magicLedger as single read-points with canonical band folding and neutral defaults) directly fixes the historical read-side drift, and its doc comments candidly record the bugs it replaced.; Resource -> institution biasing closes the config loop: instBoosts plus EXTRACTION_BOOSTS make a fishing-grounds settlement actually grow fishmongers, with per-selection traces recording base chance and resource multiplier ('why is this a fishing town?' is answerable).; Subsumption and UPGRADE_CHAINS dedup emit per-removal traces naming the absorbing institution — receipts survive the cleanup pass.; inferSupplyChains (custom content) is deterministic, bidirectionally matched, seeds prebuilt nodes so mixed custom/built-in chains assemble end-to-end, and reconciles trade endpoints against a neighbour's imports/exports.; Stress propagation through the economy is coherent: one stress vocabulary drives economy/crime/military/religion multipliers (getInstFlags), siege/occupation reshape exports and imports, and depleted resources at town+ convert into specific import lines with reasons.; DM control is honored end-to-end: goods toggles force/exclude exports, income sources, and local production; institution toggles support require/forceExclude with exclusive-group handling; custom institutions/resources/goods inject deterministically with gold-tint provenance.; The repo contains its own cross-mapping audit scripts (audit_matrix.mjs and _audit*.mjs) replicating the joins' exact matching semantics — a self-auditing culture that made this exhaustive verification tractable.

### gen-to-sim-trace

End-to-end trace from generation config to simulation substrate. The architecture is sound — pipeline steps emit trace receipts, stressors promote to conditions, the five conserved ledgers close the gen→sim loop for food/defense/governance/magic/healing, and defense even reads chain state back. But the audit found a cluster of breaks at exactly the seams the owner asked about. (1) Subsumption logic has empirically verified self-deletion bugs (Brewery, Tailor's guild, Cobbler's guild, Mint can never exist) and backwards rules that delete the chain producers (Salt works, Charcoal burner, Shepherd) the supply-chain system then reports as missing. (2) A 'trade'/'trade_entrepot' (+ 'energy'/'arcane') needKey vocabulary mismatch means trade chains never feed trade_connectivity, the smuggling escalation clock never fires, and entrepôt/arcane chains get generic beneficiaries. (3) The magic-supplement feature loses its signal at the boundary: 'magically_sustained' maps to 'stable' instead of the canonical 'substituted'. (4) Stressor→condition promotion misses wartime/insurgency/mass_migration despite their archetypes existing. (5) The healing ledger's classifier doesn't recognize hospitals. Plus a dead-config stratum: 7 RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS ids that don't exist (deserts/mountains half-inert), 13 phantom chain processors, 10 dead trade-dependency keys, an unused income↔chain table, and a computed-then-wiped exports block (slave trade, military services). Most fixes are one-line vocabulary alignments; the subsumption rules and the duplicate fishing chains need actual rule edits.

- **[high] Subsumption rules self-delete Brewery, Tailor's guild, Cobbler's guild, Mint (official)** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:74-92 (rules at 17-69)`  
  applySubsumption matches 'lesser' names by substring against ALL institutions, including the greater itself. Because 'brewery'.includes('brewer'), "tailor's guild".includes('tailor'), "cobbler's guild".includes('cobbler'), and 'mint (official)'.includes('mint'), the greater institution is added to toRemove whenever it exists. Empirically verified: ['Brewery']→[], ["Tailor's guild"]→[], ["Cobbler's guild"]→[], ['Mint (official)']→[]. These four catalog institutions can NEVER survive generation. Knock-ons: Tailor's guild is a processor for manufacturing.textiles and textile_finishing chains; both mints gate the 'Coin minting' export (CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES['Coin minting']:'mint'), so precious-metal towns can never export coinage.  
  _Fix:_ Exclude the matched 'greater' institution's index from removal (skip when the same institution satisfied hasGreater), or switch lesser-matching to exact/whole-name comparison.
- **[high] Subsumption deletes upstream chain producers the supply-chain system requires** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:42,61,64-68`  
  Several rules treat complementary producers as redundant lessers: Smelter removes 'Charcoal burner' AND 'Mine (open cast)' (verified: ['Smelter','Charcoal burner','Mine (open cast)']→['Smelter']); 'Merchant guilds (3-8)' removes 'Salt works' — the ONLY processor of food_security.salt, so the salt chain can never run in any market town (verified end-to-end: salt_flats town generated with no Salt works, no salt chain); 'Butchers (3-8)' removes Shepherd and Dairy farmer (textiles/livestock/alpine_wool processors). Charcoal burner is a processor for raw_extraction.fuel, whose absence makes the smelting chain itself 'vulnerable — needs imported fuel'. Subsumption is supposed to remove EQUIVALENT lesser institutions; here it removes the chain inputs the cohesion engine then reports as broken.  
  _Fix:_ Delete the smelter→charcoal-burner/mine, merchant-guild→salt-works/vintner, butchers→shepherd/dairy-farmer, and craft-guild→dairy-farmer rules; subsumption should only collapse same-function upgrades.
- **[high] needKey vocabulary mismatch: consumers filter 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' but generation emits 'trade_entrepot'/'raw_extraction'/'arcane_magical'** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/causalState.js:360; src/domain/hookEscalation.js:430; src/generators/steps/generateEconomy.js:240-263; src/domain/supplyChainState.js:107-138`  
  Three sim consumers use a needKey vocabulary the generator never produces: (1) causalState.deriveTradeConnectivity filters chains.filter(c => c.needKey === 'trade') — trade chains NEVER feed trade_connectivity; (2) hookEscalation builds the smuggling_rise clock on chain.needKey === 'trade' — never fires; (3) generateEconomy's trace switch cases 'trade', 'energy', 'arcane' never match, so downstream targets tradeConnectivity/fuelSupply/magicCapacity are never recorded and those chains fall to generic 'economy'; (4) supplyChainState NEED_HEURISTICS keys 'trade'/'energy'/'arcane' are dead — entrepôt and arcane chains get generic 'settlement residents' beneficiaries/victims instead of their authored ones.  
  _Fix:_ Canonicalize on the SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS keys (trade_entrepot, arcane_magical, raw_extraction) at all four sites, or add an alias map in supplyChainState used by every consumer.
- **[high] Stressor→condition promotion misses wartime, insurgency, and mass_migration** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/conditionPromotion.js:28-46; src/domain/causalState.js:505`  
  promoteStressorsToConditions matches regexes against `stressor.type + stressor.name`, but stress entries carry `label`, not `name` (buildStressEntry), so matching runs on snake_case type keys only. 'wartime' fails /\bwar\b/ (no word boundary inside 'wartime'); 'insurgency' matches none of /rebellion|revolt|uprising|insurrection|mutiny/; 'mass_migration' fails /migrant/ ('migration' ≠ 'migrant'). All three have existing target archetypes (war_pressure, rebellion, regional_migration_pressure). A settlement generated mid-insurgency or under mass migration gets activeConditions:[] — exactly the gap this pass was written to close. deriveHousingPressure's refugee regex (/refugee|displaced|influx|migrant/) also misses 'mass_migration', so the housing consequence never fires either.  
  _Fix:_ Add |wartime|war\b, |insurgenc, |migration to the rules (and include stressor.label in the matched text); add 'migration' to the housing regex.
- **[high] healingLedger classifier omits 'hospital' (and almshouse/foundling/physician)** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/healingLedger.js:23`  
  HEALING_INSTITUTION_PATTERN is /(temple|chapel|infirmary|healer|hospice|herbalist|apothecary|shrine)/i. 'Small hospital', 'Major hospital', and 'Hospital network' match NOTHING ('hospital' ≠ 'hospice'), nor do Almshouse/Foundling home — the very institutions the healing_medicine.hospital chain lists as processors and INSTITUTIONAL_SERVICE_MAP bills as 'Medical Services'. A city whose healing rests on its Major hospital reads healerCount=0; causalState.deriveHealingCapacity gives -10 'No dedicated healing institutions found' and capacityModel supply only gets the +4 services-only rescue. The dossier shows a hospital while the substrate insists healing is absent — an incoherent receipt for the DM.  
  _Fix:_ Add hospital|almshouse|foundling|physician|surgeon to HEALING_INSTITUTION_PATTERN (single source of truth, so one edit fixes all lenses).
- **[high] Slave-trade, military-services, and forced-goods exports are computed then wiped by the chain override** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2060-2113 (built) vs 2219-2226 (wiped)`  
  generateEconomicState builds heuristic exports/imports (re/q), including the military-services export (militaryEffective>=60 + garrison), the rng-gated slave-trade export plus 'Enslaved labour' import, transit-labelled exports, and DM goods-toggle force-pushes — then at the chain-derivation stage does re.length=0 / q.length=0 and refills exclusively from deriveExportsFromChains/deriveImportsFromChains. Everything pushed earlier is silently discarded (rng still consumed). Consequence: the criminal_economy.slave_trade chain exists and is exportable:true in data, but its income/exports can never appear; high-military settlements never export mercenary contracts via this path (only via deriveInstitutionalServices if a 'mercenary quarter' exists). Order-dependency bug: dead code that still looks load-bearing.  
  _Fix:_ Either delete the pre-chain export blocks (and their rng draws) or move the military/slave/forced-good augmentation to AFTER the chainExports override so it survives.
