- **[high] 'magically_sustained' chain status is invisible to the canonical sim layer** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/supplyChainState.js:57-79; src/generators/chainMagicSubstitution.js:63,83; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:320-334`  
  applyMagicSubstitution sets chain.status='magically_sustained' (the owner's magic-as-supplement feature) but does not set substituteActive. canonicalSupplyChainStatus has no mapping for 'magically_sustained', so it falls through to the default 'stable' — even though the canonical vocabulary has 'substituted' for exactly this case (the comment at supplyChainState.js:49 says so). Result: at the gen/sim boundary a druid-sustained famine-adjacent grain chain reads as a perfectly healthy stable chain (+8 food_security in causalState, +6 in capacityModel), inferSubstitutes() returns [], and no consumer can tell magic is holding the chain up. Also: pass 2 of upstream propagation in computeActiveChains can overwrite 'magically_sustained' back to 'vulnerable', erasing the state it just granted.  
  _Fix:_ Map magically_sustained → 'substituted' in LEGACY_TO_CANONICAL, set substituteActive=true in applyMagicSubstitution, and exempt magically_sustained from the second downgrade pass.
- **[medium] RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS references seven chain ids that don't exist — desert/mountain resources never activate chains** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1557-1568,1529-1540`  
  Script-verified dead refs: date_palms→agricultural.food_processing/agricultural.brewing, desert_salt→agricultural.food_processing, camel_herds→agricultural.livestock, alpine_pasture→agricultural.livestock/agricultural.textiles, hot_springs_mineral→services.hospital ('agricultural' and 'services' need keys don't exist), plus foraging_areas/ancient_grove→food_security.beekeeping_wax (beekeeping_wax lives under manufacturing). These resources can never set activatedByResource, so their chains never reach 'running', deriveLocalProductionFromChains skips their outputs, and the whole desert/mountain biome content the data file authored (date palms, camel caravans, alpine wool) is half-inert.  
  _Fix:_ Rewrite to existing ids (manufacturing.food_processing, food_security.brewing/livestock, manufacturing.textiles, healing_medicine.hospital, manufacturing.beekeeping_wax) and add a unit test that every RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS id exists in SUPPLY_CHAIN_NEEDS.
- **[medium] Religion/law/healing chains are 'processed' by the wrong institutions; outputs include institution names as goods** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:1094-1145,906-932,1026-1045`  
  religion_civic.parish ('Parish & Faith') lists processors ['Almshouse','Foundling home'] — no church, temple, or cathedral; law_governance lists ['Workhouse','Public bathhouse'] — no courthouse/town hall; healing_medicine.hospital lists ['Almshouse','Foundling home'] — no hospital; divine_healing lists ['Foundling home'] only. So a town with a Cathedral and Courthouse but no almshouse shows NO faith or law chain, while a bathhouse 'processes' governance. Separately, spellcasting outputs include "Wizard's tower" and "Mages' guild", and divine_healing outputs include "Mages' guild" — institution names emitted as tradeable goods, polluting export/consumption vocabulary downstream (searchableChainText, exports).  
  _Fix:_ Re-point processors to the real institutions (Parish church/Cathedral/Temple; Courthouse/Town hall/Mayor and council; Small/Major hospital) and strip institution names from outputs arrays.
- **[medium] 13 chain processors match no catalog institution; fortification chain effectively requires a Citadel** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:814-877 et al.; consumed via src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:114-117; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:486-502`  
  Script-verified phantom processors (slice(0,12) includes-match against all tiers): 'Barracks (town)', 'City guard district' (garrison chain), 'City wall district', 'Town fortifications' (fortification chain), 'Wizard Tower' (no apostrophe — catalog has "Wizard's tower"), 'Horse market', 'Village brewhouse', "Dyers' workshop", 'Armourers', 'Specialist craftsmen', "Bowyer's shop", 'Leatherworkers', 'Inn/Tavern District'. Worst case: defense_security.fortification only matches via 'Citadel', so towns with 'Town walls'/'City walls and gates' (the actual catalog names) get NO fortification chain — and defenseGenerator's +6 military chain bonus (chainById['fortification']) almost never applies despite being wired for it.  
  _Fix:_ Align processor names with institutionalCatalog (add 'Town walls', 'City walls', 'Garrison', 'Barracks'); add a test asserting every processingInstitution fragment matches ≥1 catalog name.
- **[medium] Duplicate chain id 'shipbuilding' defined twice in raw_extraction** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:292-304 and 347-358`  
  raw_extraction contains two chains with id 'shipbuilding' ('Shipbuilding & Boatwright', resource 'Managed woodland', minTier village; and 'Shipbuilding and Timber', resource 'Coastal Timber', minTier town). Both can be pushed into activeChains with identical chainId, so chainById (Object.fromEntries) silently keeps only the last one for the CHAIN_DEPS cascade and defense linkage, trace ids collide (two 'chain.raw_extraction.shipbuilding' receipts with different statuses), and the upstream resolution set dedupes them. A river village and a coastal city share one identity in every downstream lookup.  
  _Fix:_ Rename the second to 'coastal_shipbuilding' (and update RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS.shipbuilding_timber), or merge them with resourceSubstitutes.
- **[medium] 10 of 69 TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS keys name institutions that don't exist** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/economicData.js (TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS); consumed at src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2130-2157`  
  tradeDependencies are looked up by EXACT institution name (TRADE_DEPENDENCY_NEEDS[inst.name]). Script-verified dead keys: 'Hospitality district', 'Specialist craftsmen quarters', 'Professional guard (hundreds)', 'Mercenary company HQ', 'Inner citadel', 'Navy (if coastal)', 'Sage/library', 'Multiple wizard towers', 'Stock exchange (early)', 'Major port'. These dependencies can never fire, so the institutions they describe (notably Major port — a port city's defining import dependency) never produce a trade dependency, never impair a chain via the dependency cross-reference, and never appear in the viability report. Producer-less archetype class at the data layer.  
  _Fix:_ Rename keys to exact catalog names (or switch the lookup to the same fuzzy match computeActiveChains uses) and add a key↔catalog test.
- **[medium] mustImport viability block is doubly dead (case-mismatch + never-populated config)** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:245-278`  
  generateStabilityScore checks config.mustImport, but (a) nothing ever writes mustImport into config — terrain mustImport flows only into resourceGenerator's buildViabilityReport — and (b) even if it did, the processor check lowercases the institution name then tests n.includes('Mill') / n.includes('Sawmill') / n.includes('Smith') / n.includes('Smelter') with capital letters, which can never match. The 'Imports timber/metal' dependency warnings and the two plot hooks (timber blight, wartime metal prioritization) — exactly the gameable consequences a DM wants from import dependence — are unreachable.  
  _Fix:_ Lowercase the keywords, and feed the block from the real signal (economicState.primaryImports or terrain.mustImport threaded through resolveConfig).
- **[medium] causalState credits 'Defensive walls in place' (+6) to every settlement** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/causalState.js:425-428`  
  deriveDefenseReadiness falls back to /wall|rampart|palisade/i.test(JSON.stringify(def)). defenseProfile.institutions is always { walls: [...], garrison: [...], ... } — the property NAME 'walls' is in the JSON even when the array is empty, so the regex always matches and every generated settlement gets +6 with the receipt 'Defensive walls in place.' This both inflates defense_readiness universally and — worse for this product — produces a false explanation in the contributors trace, undermining the 'honest receipts' promise. It also double-counts walls for settlements that genuinely have them (the defenseLedger military score already folds walls in, which is the exact double-count the ledger refactor removed from capacityModel).  
  _Fix:_ Test def.institutions?.walls?.length > 0 (or drop the bonus entirely and trust defenseLedger.military, matching the P3.3b de-dup convention).
- **[medium] Legitimacy defense patch drops tier scaling and misses the 'Lightly Defended' label** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:31-34,92-116; src/generators/factionDynamics.js:43-49,79-93; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:438-443`  
  computePublicLegitimacy tier-scales the defense contribution (thorp ×0.3 … city ×1.0) because 'small settlements being Vulnerable is NORMAL, not governance failure.' assembleSettlement then patches legitimacy with the REAL defense label using an unscaled DEFENSE_CONTRIB map, so the final score for thorps/hamlets re-applies the full ±10 the design explicitly scales away. Additionally, computeDefenseReadiness emits six labels but both DEFENSE_CONTRIB maps (assembleSettlement and factionDynamics) only know five — 'Lightly Defended' falls to the ??0 default, scoring identically to 'Defensible' and BETTER than 'Vulnerable', inverting the readiness ordering for legitimacy purposes.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'Lightly Defended': -3 to both maps and re-apply the same defScale in the patch (read tier from settlement.tier).
- **[medium] Three overlapping fishing chains; landlocked market towns 'run' a fishing chain** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:55-148,1504-1521`  
  food_security defines 'fish', 'fishing', and 'river_fishing' — three near-identical chains ('Fishmonger' is even listed twice in fishing's processors). The 'fishing' chain's processors include generic 'Merchant guilds (3-8)', 'Weekly market', and 'Cooper', and RESOURCE_TO_CHAINS maps salt_flats → food_security.fishing. Verified end-to-end: a crossroads town with grain/salt/iron resources and no water generated food_security.fishing:running. Each stable food chain adds +8 to causal food_security and +6 to food capacity, so duplicate fish chains systematically inflate food scores for any settlement near water (or salt), and a DM reading the dossier sees a fishing industry that has no fishery, no water, and no fishmonger.  
  _Fix:_ Merge fish/fishing into one chain with resourceSubstitutes:['River fisheries'], drop market/guild processors from it, and remove salt_flats→fishing.
- **[medium] Two parallel food-physics models can contradict each other** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:284-583 vs src/generators/foodGenerator.js:32-308`  
  buildFactionList (feeds economicViability warnings/plot hooks) and generateFoodSecurity (feeds the conserved foodLedger, prosperity, defense famine score) duplicate the caloric model with diverging inputs: terrain agri from TERRAIN_DATA object vs a hardcoded TERRAIN_AGRI map; magic boost gated at priorityMagic>75 AND town+ vs >25 tier-scaled with different multipliers; custom food content tallied only in buildFactionList; ±8% seeded cropFortune only in generateFoodSecurity; import coverage 0.6 crossroads in one vs 0.60 + terrain boosts in the other. The same settlement can emit a 'Heavy Food Import Dependency' viability issue while its foodSecurity ledger says 'Secure' — contradictory receipts in one dossier. The capacityModel comment claims the ledger 'retires the two-food-models gap', but the viability path still uses the parallel model.  
  _Fix:_ Have generateEconomicViability read foodLedger/foodSecurity for its deficit numbers and keep buildFactionList only for the warning/hook text.
- **[medium] Only food (and defense, via bare ids) chains have needKey-specific sim consumers; healing/arcane/manufacturing/knowledge chains feed nothing** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/causalState.js:167,360; src/domain/capacityModel.js:392,535-621`  
  Generation produces 11 need categories of chains, but the substrate reads statuses by needKey only for food_security (causalState.deriveFoodSecurity, capacityModel.deriveFoodProduction) and the dead 'trade' filter. defenseGenerator reads garrison/fortification/mercenary/food_processing by bare id (good). Nothing reads: healing_medicine chains into healing capacity (it counts institutions only), arcane_magical chains into magical_stability/magical capacity (ledger + factions only), manufacturing/raw_extraction chains into craft capacity (institution regex + exports only), knowledge/entertainment/criminal/religion chains anywhere. So a 'scarce' herbalism chain or an impaired weapons_armor chain changes NO simulation variable — the chain box on the dossier and the pressure model can drift apart. This is wiring existing chains into existing capacities, not new ledgers (per owner constraint).  
  _Fix:_ Mirror the food pattern: in deriveHealing/deriveMagical/deriveCraft, add a small status loop over ctx.chains filtered by healing_medicine/arcane_magical/manufacturing.
- **[low] DM-facing copy bug: 'weavers and fullers convert SEVERITY to cloth'** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1919,1673`  
  The Wool & Textile Trade income description reads 'Local flocks provide raw wool; weavers and fullers convert SEVERITY to cloth sold across the region.' — a refactor artifact where an identifier name (SEVERITY) replaced a word (presumably 'it'/'fleece') in user-visible dossier text. Also nearby: the metropolis property-rents ternary tests tier === 'metropolis' twice (line 1673), harmless but indicative of the same mechanical rename pass.  
  _Fix:_ Restore the word ('convert the fleece to cloth') and grep the file for other ALLCAPS identifier leaks in string literals.
- **[low] _INCOME_TO_CHAINS linkage table is dead config** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:36-47`  
  computeActiveChains.js declares _INCOME_TO_CHAINS ('Grain Sales' → ['food_security.grain', ...], 'Banking Fees' → ['trade_entrepot.transit_finance'], etc.), documented as 'Income source labels → chain IDs for linkage display', but nothing in the repo references it. The income-source ↔ chain mapping a DM would use to answer 'which chain pays for this revenue line?' was designed and then never wired; income sources currently have no traceable link to the chains that justify them.  
  _Fix:_ Either wire it into deriveSupplyChainState/explanation (annotate incomeSources with chainIds) or delete it.
- **[low] Divine-tradition gate excludes parish churches in chain substitution but not in food substitution** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:69-72 vs src/generators/foodGenerator.js:60; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:428-432`  
  computeActiveChains' divine tradition requires a name matching the first list (incl. 'parish church') AND a second list ('priest','cathedral','monastery','friary','great cathedral') that 'parish church' does not satisfy — so a village whose only faith institution is a Parish church gets NO divine magic substitution on impaired food/healing chains. Meanwhile foodGenerator's hasDivine and buildFactionList's hasDivine both include 'parish church', so the same village DOES get the divine food offset. Two gates for the same fantasy concept disagree; the chain-level magic supplement (the owner's feature) is the one that loses.  
  _Fix:_ Drop the redundant second hasTradition() call (it adds nothing the first doesn't) so parish churches enable divine substitution.
- **[low] Fuzzy resource-label→key matching is order-dependent and can bind the wrong resource** (doesnt_make_sense) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:13-23`  
  resourceLabelToKey does word-overlap scoring with startsWith in both directions against ALL RESOURCE_DATA keys, taking the first highest score. Ambiguous labels resolve by key iteration order: 'Mountain Pass' (mountain_pass_trade chain) scores 1 against both mountain_timber and defended_pass — so a town with mountain timber can satisfy the Mountain Pass Control chain's resource check; 'Coastal Timber' ties shipbuilding_timber vs mountain_timber. This silently couples chains to the wrong terrain resources and makes correctness depend on object-literal ordering.  
  _Fix:_ Add an explicit label→key map for chain resources (there are ~30) and fall back to fuzzy matching only for custom content.
- **[low] Chains declare service categories outside the canonical service vocabulary** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:368-449,744-802 vs src/domain/customCategories.js:22-34`  
  Canonical availableServices keys are food/lodging/healing/equipment/information/transport/legal/employment/entertainment/magic/criminal (customCategories.SERVICE_TYPES). Chains in supplyChainData declare services: ['trade'] (oasis_agriculture, date_palm_harvest, crossroads_trade, camel_caravan), ['military','trade'] (mountain_pass_trade, coastal shipbuilding), ['security'] (adventuring_escort), ['crafts'] (river_milling, desert_glasswork), ['construction','fuel'] (mountain_timber_harvest), ['textiles'] (alpine_wool). chain.services is consumed for text search (searchableChainText) and display, so nothing crashes, but producer and consumer vocabularies have drifted — any future bucket-keyed use will silently drop these chains, and the regional-condition matcher already treats them as free-text rather than typed categories.  
  _Fix:_ Normalize chain services to the 11 canonical keys (trade→transport or legal; crafts→equipment; security→employment) and lint against SERVICE_TYPES.
- **[low] Garrison/fortification chains structurally vulnerable at their own minTier** (realism_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/supplyChainData.js:814-842; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:289-315; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:493-501`  
  defense_security.garrison (minTier hamlet) lists upstreamChains:['food_processing'] (minTier village), and fortification (minTier hamlet) lists ['stone'] (minTier village). A hamlet that legitimately rolls a garrison chain ALWAYS gets 'vulnerable — Needs imported food_processing, no local source', and defenseGenerator then applies chainMilBonus -5. Small settlements are thus systematically penalized for upstream chains they are tier-forbidden from having — the dependency gate fires below the tier where the dependency can exist.  
  _Fix:_ Skip upstream-missing downgrades when the upstream chain's minTier exceeds the settlement tier (subsistence garrisons provision locally).
- **[low] Misleading function names in economicGenerator obscure the gen flow** (incoherence) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:66,284,793,202,947,1151,1385`  
  The viability pipeline's helpers are named for a different domain than what they compute: buildFactionList computes the FOOD BALANCE, computeFactionPowers does RESOURCE-CHAIN analysis, buildPowerNarrative checks WATER dependencies, generateStabilityScore generates FOOD plot hooks, getHistoryModifiers/getGoodsModifiers roll EXPORT lists, getUpgradeChain returns IMPORT goods. For an audit of 'does it trace coherently from config to sim', this naming is an active hazard — generateEconomicViability reads as a faction/power computation when it is food/water/trade viability.  
  _Fix:_ Rename to computeResourceChainIssues, computeFoodBalance, checkWaterDependencies, computeFoodPlotHooks, rollTierExports, getTierImports.
- **[low] capacityModel.deriveHealing bypasses the magic ledger with stale 'pervasive' vocabulary** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/domain/capacityModel.js:221-224`  
  deriveHealing reads s.config?.magicLevel directly and tests magic === 'high' || magic === 'pervasive'. The generator vocabulary is none/low/medium/high (getMagicLevel) — 'pervasive' is never produced. More importantly this is the exact pattern the conserved-ledger refactor was built to retire: deriveMagical and deriveMagicalStability were migrated to magicLedger (which canonicalizes legacy bands), but this one read was missed, so legacy saves with old band words get inconsistent healing supply vs magical supply.  
  _Fix:_ Replace with const m = magicLedger(s); if (m.magicLevel === 'high') ... — matching the other two magic lenses.
- **[low] Finished-goods 'alchemical' supplier keyword 'foraging' is dead** (dead_config) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/data/economicData.js (INSTITUTION_FINISHED_GOODS_DEMAND.alchemical); src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1542-1549`  
  computeFinishedGoodsDemand treats supplier keywords containing '_' as resource keys and others as institution-name keywords. INSTITUTION_FINISHED_GOODS_DEMAND's alchemical category lists supplier 'foraging' (no underscore) — checked against institution names, where nothing matches (script-verified). The intended signal was almost certainly the foraging_areas resource, so wild-reagent terrain never offsets alchemical demand and such settlements over-import reagents.  
  _Fix:_ Rename the key to 'foraging_areas' so it routes through the hasRes branch.
- **[medium] Leather export gate demands 'tannery' while chains run on 'Tanner (established)' — and a subsumption rule removes the Tannery** (mapping_gap) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:408-414; src/generators/steps/subsumptionPass.js:38`  
  CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES gates 'Leather goods'/'Leather armour'/'Boots and shoes'/'Saddles and harness'/'Tanned leather' on the keyword 'tannery'. The leather chains' canonical processors are 'Tanner (established)' and "Cobbler's guild" — neither contains 'tannery', so a settlement whose leather chain runs on the established tanner exports NOTHING from it. Worse, subsumption rule 38 ('tanner (established)' subsumes 'tannery') deletes the one institution that passes the gate whenever both exist. So generation actively removes leather-export capability from its best leather towns. (Cobbler's guild also self-deletes per the other finding, compounding it.)  
  _Fix:_ Make the gate ['tannery','tanner'] and drop the tanner→tannery subsumption rule (they're tiers of the same trade — use UPGRADE_CHAINS instead).
- **[low] DM goods-toggle 'force' affects exports but is silently dropped from localProduction** (inconsistency) — `C:/Users/stoke/Desktop/settlement_work/src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2035-2059 vs 2243-2246; src/generators/computeActiveChains.js:636-651`  
  When a DM forces a good, the goodsToggles branch pushes it into exports AND v.localProduction (economicGenerator.js:2044-2051). But localProduction is then wiped and rebuilt from deriveLocalProductionFromChains (2243-2246), which never consults goodsToggles. Net: the forced good appears in primaryExports (deriveExportsFromChains re-applies toggles) but not in localProduction — the dossier shows the town exporting something it apparently doesn't produce. The 'allow:false' exclusion is similarly lost for localProduction.  
  _Fix:_ Apply the goodsToggles force/exclude pass to chainLocalProd after the rebuild (or inside deriveLocalProductionFromChains).

Strengths: The conserved-ledger refactor is genuinely well executed: foodLedger/defenseLedger/governanceLedger/magicLedger/healingLedger each have one read-point, defensive present-gating, documented per-lens weights, and explicit de-dup decisions (e.g. capacityModel no longer double-counts walls when defenseLedger.present, and trade-route food import coverage is applied only as a no-ledger fallback). The gen→ledger→causal/capacity loop closes cleanly for food, defense, governance, and magic.; conditionPromotion closes the 'generated plague town has activeConditions:[]' gap correctly for the stress types its regexes do match (siege, famine, plague, occupation, slave revolt): idempotent, severity-max collapsing per archetype, deterministic, and wired at the right place (after normalizeSettlement in assembleSettlement).; Trace receipts (recordTrace) are emitted at every generation step — institution selection with base-chance × resource-multiplier causes, subsumption/cascade removals naming the absorber, stressors with intended-vs-emergent-vs-declined results, per-chain activation causes — with a deterministic trace clock. This is exactly the 'honest receipts for WHY' the product promises.; defenseGenerator actually consumes generated chain state (garrison/fortification/mercenary/food_processing statuses feed military/economic score modifiers), and assembleSettlement back-patches legitimacy with the real defense label — a real bidirectional gen→sim→gen wiring, not just display.; Magic-as-supplement is implemented coherently at three levels with sensible realism limits: chain-level substitution (chainMagicSubstitution, with druid > divine > arcane recovery rates and exportable=false so magic sustains subsistence but never exports), food-physics offsets (tier-scaled, institution-gated, capped), and economy-level teleportation infrastructure that substitutes for trade routes everywhere isolation is penalized (imports, dependencies, prosperity, viability text). Dead-magic worlds correctly zero the dial at resolveConfig so nothing leaks.; deriveExportsFromChains' extraction and processing gates (RESOURCE_EXTRACTION_GATES, CHAIN_OUTPUT_INST_GATES, the external-mill banalité special case with its DM-facing note) encode real medieval-economy logic — you can't export iron ore without a mine, or flour without your own mill — which is exactly the right realism altitude for this audience.; tradeRouteSemantics canonicalization and the magicLedger band-folding show the team systematically hunting the vocabulary-drift class of bug; the remaining instances found in this audit are stragglers of a pattern already being fixed, and the in-code comments documenting WHY each de-dup or fallback exists are unusually good.

### validation-narrative

The validator's live core is solid and DM-appropriate (tier/dependency/exclusivity/threat/isolation checks, by-design receipts surfaced in the UI), and the Supabase edge function's grounding discipline is genuinely good — but the narrative layer between them is riddled with producer/consumer vocabulary drift. The worst breaks: faction conflicts are generated but every narrative consumer reads them from powerStructure.conflicts where they never live; aiLayer treats the stability label string as a 0-100 number so its power note claims contested authority in every settlement; the arrival-scene tables are cross-wired (route-keyed templates indexed by a phantom tradeCommodity field, ambience-keyed templates indexed by route), leaving most settlements with a flat 'X comes into view.'; and case-sensitive requiredInstitution matching severs seven institution-to-export links in the live goods path. A second tier of rot — self-satisfying GATE dependency checks, a mostly-dead low-magic warning list, five stress types with no arrival vignette, the never-called _resolveUpgrades auto-fix layer, and aiLayer's discarded prompt builder — means a meaningful fraction of the coherence/receipts surface looks comprehensive but is provably inert. None of it is architectural; nearly every finding is a one-line field-path or vocabulary fix, plus one missing cross-vocabulary test that would have caught all of them.</summary>
</invoke>


- **[high] Faction conflicts generated but invisible to every narrative layer (wrong location read)** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/assembleSettlement.js:73; src/generators/aiLayer.js:46,102; supabase/functions/generate-narrative/index.ts:335,617,998,1090`  
  generatePopulation produces conflicts (steps/generatePopulation.js:101) and assembleSettlement stores them at top-level settlement.conflicts (steps/assembleSettlement.js:73). But every narrative consumer reads powerStructure.conflicts, which generatePowerStructure never sets (powerGenerator.js:2201-2208 returns factions/stability/recentConflict/publicLegitimacy/factionRelationships/criminalCaptureState only). Affected: aiLayer.js:46+102 (prompt 'Conflicts:' line and frictionPoints never populate), dailyLifeLogic.js:27, ChroniclePanel.jsx:173, and the edge function generate-narrative/index.ts:335, 617 (the entire 'conflicts' refinement pass extracts from an always-empty array — a no-op), 998 (dmCompass digest), 1090 (tabNotes digest). The engine's richest cross-domain output (faction-vs-faction conflict with issue/stakes) never reaches the AI grounding or local prose.  
  _Fix:_ Either copy conflicts onto powerStructure in assembleSettlement (powerStructure.conflicts = conflicts) or change all consumers to read settlement.conflicts. One-line producer fix is safest.
- **[high] aiLayer treats powerStructure.stability (a string) as a 0-100 number — power note always claims contested authority** (inconsistency) — `src/generators/aiLayer.js:99,160,279; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:1804-1849,2203`  
  powerGenerator emits stability as a label string ('Stable', 'Unstable — criminal governance', 'Critical (active siege…)', powerGenerator.js:1804-1849). aiLayer.js:99 does stability: ps.stability ?? 50, then the prompt prints 'Political stability: Stable/100' (aiLayer.js:160) and buildLocalNotes (aiLayer.js:279) tests ctx.stability >= 60 — always false for a string — so the power tab note says authority 'should feel personal, contested, and frequently renegotiated' for EVERY settlement, including ones the engine labels Stable/Ordered. This is exactly the prose-contradicts-data failure the DM-receipts contract forbids. narrativeGenerator's consumers handle the same field correctly as a string (genCoherence:807, generatePressureSentence:1005), so the producer vocabulary is fine — aiLayer alone misreads it.  
  _Fix:_ Treat stability as a label: print it verbatim in the prompt, and branch the local note on substring checks ('Stable'/'Ordered' vs 'Unstable'/'Fractured'/'Critical') like narrativeGenerator does.
- **[high] Arrival-scene tables cross-wired: ARRIVAL_SCENES keyed by ambience but indexed by route; ARRIVAL_ADDONS keyed by route but indexed by a field that never exists** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:1074-1092; src/data/narrativeData.js:108-196; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2402-2449`  
  generateArrivalScene (narrativeGenerator.js:1074) looks up ARRIVAL_SCENES[route] where route ∈ {road, river, port, crossroads, isolated}, but ARRIVAL_SCENES keys are {market, river, smoke, guild, ordinary} (narrativeData.js:108-145). Only 'river' coincides; every non-stressed road/port/crossroads/isolated settlement gets the flat fallback '<Name> comes into view.', and 4 of 5 ambience pools are unreachable. Meanwhile ARRIVAL_ADDONS (narrativeData.js:147-196) IS keyed by route with 20 rich route-arrival templates taking (name, tier) — but the consumer indexes it by economicState.tradeCommodity (narrativeGenerator.js:1090-1092), a field economicGenerator never sets (state object at economicGenerator.js:2402-2449 has no tradeCommodity; only historyGenerator's internal context has one). So the addon never fires. The wires are visibly swapped: route arrivals dead, ambience pools dead, all stitched into the dossier's single most prominent prose block.  
  _Fix:_ Use ARRIVAL_ADDONS[route] as the route-flavoured opener (it takes name+tier) and pick ARRIVAL_SCENES ambience from institutions (market/guild presence) as the addon. Either set economicState.tradeCommodity from primaryExports or delete the commodity branch.
- **[high] Case-sensitive requiredInstitution breaks 7 institution-to-export links in the live goods table** (mapping_gap) — `src/data/tradeGoodsData.js (7 requiredInstitution entries); src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1158-1163`  
  GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER (the LIVE export path via getGoodsModifiers, economicGenerator.js:1151-1168) matches requiredInstitution with w.name === req || w.name.includes(req) — case-sensitive. Seven entries use Title Case that the catalog spells in sentence case: 'Hunter's Lodge' vs catalog 'Hunter's lodge' (Game meat), 'Charcoal Burner' vs 'Charcoal burner' (Charcoal), 'Peat Cutter' vs 'Peat cutter' (Peat fuel), 'Fisher's Landing' vs 'Fisher's landing' (Fresh fish), 'Dairy Farmer' vs 'Dairy farmer' (Fresh milk and dairy), 'Cobbler's Guild' vs 'Cobbler's guild' (Quality boots and shoes), 'Tailor's Guild' vs 'Tailor's guild' (Finished garments). A hamlet with a Hunter's lodge can never export game meat; a town's Cobbler's guild never produces boots for export. Institutions exist, goods exist, the link silently never resolves — the canonical institution-should-produce-good orphan.  
  _Fix:_ Lowercase both sides at the comparison (one-line fix in getGoodsModifiers) and add a startup assertion that every requiredInstitution resolves to a catalog name.
- **[medium] GATE_FEATURES dependency checks are largely self-satisfying or dead** (doesnt_make_sense) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:143-149,355-409; src/data/spatialData.js (GATE_FEATURES)`  
  checkStructuralValidity expands instNames with SPATIAL_FEATURES implications BEFORE checking gate.requires (structuralValidator.js:338,367). Because an institution's own SPATIAL_FEATURES entry often contains its requirement, the gate is a tautology: 'Multiple adventurers' guilds' requires 'Adventurers' guild hall' — a name that exists nowhere in the catalog — but SPATIAL_FEATURES['Multiple adventurers' guilds'] implies that very name, so the check can never fail (same pattern for Mages' guild→Wizard's tower, Mercenary quarter→Mercenary company HQ). Separately, 22 GATE_FEATURES keys name institutions/services that never appear in instNames ('Major port', 'University', 'Spellcasting services (1st-4th/6th/8th level)', 'Resurrection services (10,000+ only)', 'Magic item consignment', 'Navy (if coastal)', etc.) — those gates never evaluate at all. The validator looks comprehensive but a large fraction of its dependency surface is provably inert.  
  _Fix:_ Check requires against the raw instNames (or expansion excluding the gated institution itself), and add a dev-time audit that every GATE_FEATURES key and requires/blockedBy value exists in the catalog.
- **[medium] Low-magic exotic-institution warning misses 8 of 12 names (catalog suffix drift)** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:429-447`  
  HIGH_MAGIC_INSTITUTIONS (structuralValidator.js:430-435) checks exact names against the expanded set, but the catalog spells most of them with a '(high magic)' suffix or doesn't have them at all: 'Airship docking' vs 'Airship docking (high magic)', 'Dream parlor' vs 'Dream parlors (high magic)', 'Message network' vs 'Message network (high magic)', plus 'Magical banking', 'Magic item consignment', 'Enchanting quarter', 'High magic district', 'Extradimensional vault' (no catalog match). Only Golem workforce, Undead labor, Planar embassy, and Teleportation circle can actually trigger the warning. The realism guard the DM relies on — 'you set magic to Low but this settlement has an airship dock' — is silently dead for two-thirds of its list.  
  _Fix:_ Match case-insensitively on name prefixes (or strip parenthetical suffixes before comparing), and verify the list against the catalog in a test.
- **[medium] _resolveUpgrades (auto-fix layer) is dead code — plagued/siege/slave-revolt institution forcing never runs** (dead_config) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:750-907`  
  _resolveUpgrades (structuralValidator.js:750-907) holds real logic: force minimum walls+militia in 'plagued' regions, add walls under 'under_siege' stress, add a Slave market under 'slave_revolt', adventurers' charter hall for militia-only frontier settlements, slider-driven additions at >85 priority, and removal of port/naval/high-magic institutions lacking infrastructure. It is never called anywhere (only definition site matches). Some of it is redundant (catalog tradeRouteRequired gates docks; powerGenerator's slave_revolt text handles a missing slave market), but the survival forcing is not: a plagued-region town can generate with zero defenses, and the validator then emits a 'this settlement will fall' error (lines 475-516) with no mechanism ever attempting the fix the code was written to apply. Dead config plus a realism gap the function was built to close.  
  _Fix:_ Either wire _resolveUpgrades into assembleInstitutions before validation (preserving the violation as a receipt when the DM disabled the categories), or delete it and document that survival gaps are surfaced-not-fixed by design.
- **[medium] 5 of 15 stress types have no arrival vignette and no founding stress note** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:175-276,591-612; src/data/stressTypes.js:12`  
  STRESS_TYPE_MAP defines 15 canonical stress types (data/stressTypes.js:12). STRESS_DESCS (narrativeGenerator.js:175-276) covers only 10 — insurgency, mass_migration, wartime, religious_conversion, and slave_revolt have no arrival vignette, so those settlements fall through to the route-based arrival (itself broken per the cross-wiring finding) and open with '<Name> comes into view.' STRESS_NOTES in genArrivalDetail (narrativeGenerator.js:591-612) misses the same five, so their founding context gets stressNote:null. The priority-ordering arrays in genSettSummary/genPressureDetail/generateArrivalScene DO list all 15 (three hand-copied duplicates of the same list, itself a drift hazard), and PRESSURE_SENTENCES covers all 15 — so the gap is specifically the arrival/founding layer. A DM generating a slave-revolt or wartime settlement gets a crisis dossier with a serene arrival paragraph.  
  _Fix:_ Add the five missing STRESS_DESCS/STRESS_NOTES entries, and derive the priority list from STRESS_TYPE_MAP keys instead of three inline copies.
- **[medium] Pressure sentences for insurgency/mass_migration/wartime branch on r.compound, which genPressureDetail never provides** (mapping_gap) — `src/data/narrativeData.js:56-88; src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:727-757`  
  PRESSURE_SENTENCES.insurgency/mass_migration/wartime (narrativeData.js:56-88) select between two variants using r.compound?.criminalEffective/militaryEffective/economyOutput. The object passed is genPressureDetail's return (narrativeGenerator.js:727-757), which has no compound field — compound lives at economicState.compound. With defaults, wartime always renders the 'losing people and resources… running thin' variant even when the settlement has militaryEffective 80 and a booming economy; mass_migration always renders the 'absorbing more people' (influx) variant even when the engine's economy says the settlement is shrinking; insurgency always renders the institutional-ledger variant. The data-conditional prose was designed to track the simulation and silently doesn't — prose can directly contradict the economy/defense scores on the same page.  
  _Fix:_ Add compound: settlement.economicState?.compound to genPressureDetail's return.
- **[medium] aiLayer reads three phantom fields: incomeSources count is always 0, criticalImports always empty, plotHooks always empty** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/aiLayer.js:80,119,137; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:2409,2547-2562`  
  (1) aiLayer.js:80 reads via.incomeSources — economicViability has no such field (incomeSources lives on economicState, economicGenerator.js:2409) — so the AI prompt always states 'Income sources: 0', telling the model a metropolis has zero revenue streams. (2) aiLayer.js:119 reads via.metrics.criticalImports — metrics contains only foodBalance/tradeAccess/counts (economicGenerator.js:2555-2561) — so 'Critical imports:' never renders (PDF gets them from resourceAnalysis.imports.critical instead). (3) aiLayer.js:137 reads s.plotHooks — hooks live at economicViability.plotHooks (UI reads via.plotHooks, EconomicsTab.jsx:391) — so the prompt's EMERGING PLOT HOOKS section never renders, buildLocalCompass.hooks is always [], and the plot_hooks note always falls back to generic 'Local tensions'. Three structured outputs produced by the engine, all invisible to the narrative grounding through location/vocabulary drift.  
  _Fix:_ Point them at economicState.incomeSources, resourceAnalysis.imports.critical (or economicState.necessityImports), and economicViability.plotHooks respectively.
- **[medium] Edge-function tab-note digests read phantom fields: defense readiness, magic label, local production never reach the AI** (mapping_gap) — `supabase/functions/generate-narrative/index.ts:1105-1117; src/generators/defenseGenerator.js:438-444; src/domain/magicProfile.js:239`  
  generate-narrative's tabNotes extract (index.ts:1105-1117) reads s.defenseAssessment?.readinessLabel || s.defense?.readinessLabel — but the settlement stores it at defenseProfile.readiness.label (defenseGenerator.js:438-444) — and s.magicProfile?.label || s.magic?.label — deriveMagicProfile (domain/magicProfile.js:239) is never attached to the settlement and returns no .label field anyway — and s.localProduction, which lives at economicState.localProduction (economicGenerator.js:2414). So the model writes the 'defense' note without the defense posture, the magicLabel is always absent, and resourceState.local is always empty. The notes are still grounded in other fields, but the specific lenses these keys were added for are silently un-fed — the AI can only guess the defense posture it is instructed to characterize.  
  _Fix:_ Read s.defenseProfile?.readiness?.label, s.economicState?.localProduction, and either attach a magic profile summary to the settlement or drop the magicLabel key.
- **[medium] Food surplus reported as a percentage when it is absolute units** (math_error) — `src/generators/aiLayer.js:55-60; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:566-581`  
  economicViability.metrics.foodBalance.surplus is absolute daily units (Math.round(Math.max(surplus,0)), economicGenerator.js:571), while deficitPercent is a percentage. aiLayer.js:55-60 formats the deficit branch correctly with deficitPercent but the surplus branch as `${Math.round(fb.surplus)}% food surplus` — a village producing 300 units over need reads '300% food surplus' in the AI prompt, the local dailyLife prose ('Food feels like 300% food surplus'), and the identityMarkers. The PDF treats the same field correctly as units ('Surplus of X units', pdf/sections/IdentityDailyLife.jsx:201), so the dossier and the narrative can state numerically incompatible food situations for the same settlement.  
  _Fix:_ Compute surplus percent as surplus/dailyNeed*100, or print units with the word 'units' as the PDF does.
- **[medium] AI safety pass rewrites engine verdict prose (economicViability.summary) with only instruction-level protection** (incoherence) — `supabase/functions/generate-narrative/index.ts:802-851; src/generators/aiLayer.js:75`  
  The 'safety' refinement pass extracts economicViability.summary and writes the model's rewrite back over it (generate-narrative/index.ts:808, 822-825), along with safetyProfile.guardEffectivenessDesc/safetyDesc/economicDragDesc and crimeTypes[].desc. The instruction asks the model to 'preserve the ✗ NOT VIABLE: prefix exactly' (line 842) but apply() does no code-level check — if the model drops or softens the prefix, the narrated dossier's viability verdict prose can contradict the still-engine-owned viable:false flag and critical issues list shown beside it. Since aiLayer.js:75 also parses 'prosperity' out of this same summary string, an AI-rewritten summary feeds back into later local-narrative regeneration. Engine receipts should not be overwritable by model output without validation.  
  _Fix:_ In apply(), if the source summary started with '✗ NOT VIABLE:' (or '✓ VIABLE:'), enforce the same prefix on the refined value or reject the rewrite. Better: write AI prose to a sibling field (summaryProse) and keep summary engine-owned.
- **[medium] Dead export path (SERVICE_TIER_DATA + getHistoryModifiers field mismatch) still drives the Generate Wizard's trade-goods UI** (dead_config) — `src/generators/economicGenerator.js:860-900,947-965; src/generators/servicesGenerator.js:491-765; src/components/TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:27`  
  getHistoryModifiers (economicGenerator.js:947-965) reads h.on and h.p from SERVICE_TIER_DATA, whose entries define defaultEnabled and baseChance instead (servicesGenerator.js:491-765) — so it always returns []; its only caller _computeIncomeStreams (economicGenerator.js:860) is itself never called. The live path is generateTradeIncomeStreams → getGoodsModifiers → GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER (on/p fields, tradeGoodsData.js). But GenerateWizard step 3 renders TradeDynamicsPanel from SERVICE_TIER_DATA (TradeDynamicsPanel.jsx:6,27; GenerateWizard.jsx:730), which is a strict subset: GOODS-only entries — including 'Enslaved persons', 'Glassware', 'Salted fish', 'Refined iron ingots', 'Finished garments' — never appear in the toggle UI, so a DM cannot see or disable them (slave-trade exports especially matter for table content control). The config surface and the engine read different tables.  
  _Fix:_ Delete SERVICE_TIER_DATA/_computeIncomeStreams/getHistoryModifiers and point TradeDynamicsPanel at GOODS_MODIFIERS_BY_TIER so the UI and engine share one goods vocabulary.
- **[medium] aiLayer claims to call the Claude API; the 85-line prompt is built and discarded, progress messages are theatrical** (dead_config) — `src/generators/aiLayer.js:2-14,146-231,300-336; src/components/OutputContainer.jsx:230-251`  
  The header (aiLayer.js:2-14) says the module 'calls the Claude API and returns a structured narrative object'. In fact runAiLayer (aiLayer.js:300-336) computes buildAiLayerPrompt into _prompt and never uses it, sleeps 200ms twice while emitting 'Reading the settlement…'/'Weaving the narrative…' progress, then returns local template prose. The real AI lives in the Supabase edge function (OutputContainer.jsx:235-242 routes there when configured; runAiLayer is the offline fallback) — a legitimate architecture, but the dead prompt builder (aiLayer.js:146-231) is the only place the 'full settlement prompt' exists client-side and it silently rots (it already contains the stability/100 and Income-sources:0 bugs that nothing exercises). Misleading doc + 90 lines of unexercised grounding logic in the exact module named as the grounding layer.  
  _Fix:_ Delete buildAiLayerPrompt or actually use it; rewrite the header to say 'local offline narrative fallback; real AI is supabase/functions/generate-narrative'; drop the fake progress delays or label them as formatting.
- **[low] Prosperity vocabulary drift across narrative consumers ('Thriving', 'Modest', missing Comfortable/Struggling)** (inconsistency) — `src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:567-588,839; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:1062; src/generators/historyGenerator.js:222`  
  economicState.prosperity is one of Struggling/Poor/Moderate/Comfortable/Prosperous/Wealthy (economicGenerator.js:1062). genCoherence's prosperous-criminal note tests ['Prosperous','Wealthy','Thriving'] (narrativeGenerator.js:839) — 'Thriving' is never produced. genArrivalDetail's OVERCOMING_BY_PROSPERITY (narrativeGenerator.js:567-588) has keys for only Wealthy/Prosperous/Moderate/Poor, so Comfortable and Struggling settlements silently get the Moderate founding story; historyGenerator defaults prosperity to 'Modest' (historyGenerator.js:222), which is not in the label set either (also falls to Moderate). All degrade gracefully via fallbacks, but the vocabulary has visibly forked and a Struggling settlement's founding reads as if it overcame 'through determination and cooperation' rather than 'at significant cost'.  
  _Fix:_ Centralize the prosperity label list in one constant, add Comfortable/Struggling entries, and delete 'Thriving'.
- **[low] Unset magic priority reads as 'medium', 'medium-ish 50', and '0' in three different consumers** (inconsistency) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:350-352; src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:1067; src/generators/aiLayer.js:127`  
  When config.priorityMagic is undefined: checkStructuralValidity maps it to magicLevel||'medium' (structuralValidator.js:350-352); generateArrivalScene uses ?? 50, which can render the magelight-lamppost detail at the 40+ threshold (narrativeGenerator.js:1067,92-97); aiLayer uses || 0 (aiLayer.js:127) and prints 'priority 0/100' in the prompt, telling the model this is a no-magic settlement. The same unset dial is simultaneously medium for validation, visibly magical in the arrival scene, and zero for AI grounding. Also || 0 coerces an explicit 0 and undefined identically, losing the configured-vs-unset distinction.  
  _Fix:_ Resolve priorityMagic once in resolveConfig (effectiveConfig.priorityMagic ?? 50) so all downstream consumers see one value.
- **[low] checkInstCompat landmark branches keyed to institutions that can never exist ('Major port')** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:110,293-310; src/data/spatialData.js:5,11`  
  checkInstCompat's harbour-crane arrival landmark fires on has('major port') (structuralValidator.js:293-298), but no catalog institution name contains 'major port' — port settlements get 'Docks/port facilities' and 'Harbour master's office'. So port cities never get their signature landmark line in the arrival scene. The 'university' branch (line 305) is reachable only via 'Academy of magic'. 'Major port' and 'Navy (if coastal)' also persist in INSTITUTION_SPATIAL access checks (spatialData.js:5,11) and SPATIAL_FEATURES (structuralValidator.js:110) as vocabulary from an older catalog generation.  
  _Fix:_ Key the port landmark on 'docks/port' or 'harbour', and purge 'Major port'/'Navy (if coastal)' from the validator vocabulary or add them to the catalog.
- **[low] Local thesis embeds raw UI verdict strings ('✓ VIABLE: … 4 plot hooks available.') into in-world prose** (incoherence) — `src/generators/aiLayer.js:75,258-263; src/generators/economicGenerator.js:53-63`  
  aiLayer.js:75 derives 'prosperity' by splitting economicViability.summary on an em-dash that buildConflict's output never contains (economicGenerator.js:53-63 produces '✓ VIABLE: Settlement can survive but has 2 trade dependencies. 3 plot hooks available.'), so ctx.prosperity is the whole verdict string. buildLocalThesis (aiLayer.js:258-263) then writes 'the economy presents as ✓ VIABLE: … 3 plot hooks available.' — glyphs, mechanics-counts, and meta-language ('plot hooks available') inside the narrative thesis a DM reads aloud. The actual prosperity label (economicState.prosperity) is never consulted by aiLayer at all.  
  _Fix:_ Use economicState.prosperity for the prosperity slot and keep the viability verdict string out of generated prose (or strip the prefix/counts before embedding).
- **[low] Validator emits a seeded-random 40% violation — re-validation on edit makes warnings flicker** (doesnt_make_sense) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:563-576; src/domain/coherence/checkDraftEdit.js:36`  
  checkStructuralValidity rolls _rng() for the isolated-thorp/hamlet 'subsistence_struggle' warning (structuralValidator.js:563-576, 40% chance). The same function is re-invoked by checkDraftEdit on every dossier edit (domain/coherence/checkDraftEdit.js:36) with whatever rng state is current, so the warning can appear after one unrelated edit and vanish after the next — a validator whose findings aren't a function of the settlement. Validation should be a pure predicate; flavour-probability belongs in generation, not in the checker.  
  _Fix:_ Make the struggle note deterministic (derive from seed/foodBalance) or always emit it at 'info' severity and let display decide prominence.
- **[low] generatePower trace reads powerStructure.governingName, which is never returned — governing-faction receipts never fire** (mapping_gap) — `src/generators/steps/generatePower.js:44-66; src/generators/powerGenerator.js:948,2201-2208`  
  steps/generatePower.js:44 reads powerStructure?.governingName to decide isGoverning for the per-faction trace, but generatePowerStructure returns only factions/stability/recentConflict/publicLegitimacy/factionRelationships/criminalCaptureState (powerGenerator.js:2201-2208). governingName is always null, so isGoverning is always false: the trace result is never 'governing', and the 'inherits public legitimacy' cause (lines 60-66) is never recorded. The factions themselves carry isGoverning flags (powerGenerator.js:948), so the fix is trivial — the receipt layer is just keyed on the wrong field. The PipelineRail can currently never answer 'why is this faction governing?'.  
  _Fix:_ Use f.isGoverning directly instead of substring-matching a nonexistent governingName.
- **[low] Dead duplicates and doc rot inside structuralValidator/narrativeGenerator** (dead_config) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js:154-247,876-922; src/generators/narrativeGenerator.js:107-146,173,732,876-933`  
  structuralValidator.js carries unused private copies of live logic: _getPriorityModifiers (154-165, live version in institutionProbability.js:8), _getTierConstraints (179-247, live duplicate in powerGenerator.js:88 — two copies that can drift), _getSettReason in narrativeGenerator.js:876-912 (unused), plus a dangling getBaseChance JSDoc with no function at structuralValidator.js:909-922 (the real one is re-exported at line 9). servicesGenerator.js:27 has another _getTierConstraints stub. narrativeGenerator's STRESS_DESCS comment (line 173) claims 'Exported for use by UI components' but the const is not exported; buildPoliticalNarrative's JSDoc (line 916) claims it adds 'faction affiliation' but it only overlays secret/presentation; genPressureDetail.healersRef (line 732) is computed but no PRESSURE_SENTENCES template consumes it. buildStressProfile (narrativeGenerator.js:107-146) duplicates historyGenerator.js:~60-103 verbatim.  
  _Fix:_ Delete the dead copies, fix the comments, and import shared helpers from one module so the two getTierConstraints can't diverge.
- **[low] Missing: no validator check that prose-bearing fields exist for the stress/route the settlement actually has** (missing) — `src/generators/structuralValidator.js (absent check); tests/ (absent)`  
  structuralValidator validates institutions against config thoroughly, but nothing validates the narrative layer's coverage: there is no check (test or runtime) that every STRESS_TYPE_MAP key has a STRESS_DESCS vignette, a STRESS_NOTES founding note, and a PRESSURE_SENTENCES entry; that ARRIVAL tables are keyed by the vocabulary their consumers index with; or that aiLayer/edge-function digest paths resolve to real settlement fields. Every gap found in this audit (conflicts location, stability type, phantom tradeCommodity, defenseAssessment, plotHooks, h.on/h.p) would have been caught by a single cross-vocabulary test enumerating producers vs consumers. For a product whose thesis is 'honest receipts', the receipt pipeline itself has no coherence guard.  
  _Fix:_ Add one vitest that generates settlements across all 15 stresses x 5 routes and asserts: arrival scene is not the bare fallback, pressure sentence exists, and every aiLayer/tabNotes digest field is non-undefined for a fully-populated settlement.

Strengths: structuralValidator's live checks form a genuinely layered coherence contract well-tuned for DMs: tier gates, dependency/blocker gates, trade-route access requirements, government exclusivity, threat-scaled military adequacy with funding nuance (plagued + milPriority<25 = 'this settlement will fall'), isolation viability with an explicit magical-trade exception and a physical-fallback warning, and resource-route compatibility (structuralValidator.js:333-737).; Deliberate DM overrides are surfaced as 'by_design' receipts rather than blocked — out-of-tier institutions and exclusivity conflicts become plot-seed annotations ('why do both exist?'), exactly the right posture for a cohesion engine vs a hard sim (structuralValidator.js:692-724).; Violations and suggestions flow all the way to the user: structuralViolations render in Overview/Defense/Viability tabs and the PDF, so the validator's receipts are actually visible, not just logged.; The generate-narrative edge function is a model of grounded AI: each pass extracts a compact digest of real structured fields, instructions forbid inventing names ('ONLY use names that appear in the provided lists'), apply() functions defensively validate shapes/synonyms/wrapper-peeling, and the engine-owned viable boolean and issue lists are never handed to the model (supabase/functions/generate-narrative/index.ts).; PRESSURE_SENTENCES covers all 15 canonical stress types, and its stability-string consumers (genCoherence occupation check, generatePressureSentence's Unstable/Fractured branch) match the producer vocabulary exactly — as does genCoherence's 'church controls' cross-check against computeEconomicViability's actual output string.; resolveStress records intended-vs-applied-vs-declined stressor traces, and assembleInstitutions emits per-institution selection receipts (required/forced/probability x resource lift) — the 'why does this exist' question is answerable from data for the generation core.; aiLayer's institution category keys (Government/Economy/Crafts/Defense/Religious/Magic/Criminal/Infrastructure) match the catalog's casing exactly, and flattenServices defensively handles both availableServices shapes — the documented crash fix shows the producer/consumer contract is being actively maintained where it has bitten before.; genCoherence's cross-tab contradiction notes (criminal faction in an entrepôt distorting trade figures, siege nullifying trade income, church-economy vs secular-government tension, collapse-then-boom recovery narrative) are exactly the cross-domain 'honest receipt' content the product thesis calls for, and all of their data reads check out against the producers.
